Standing Near the Imam at Arafah – A Recommended Practice
Ruling on recommended positioning at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the pilgrim's position relative to the Imam at Arafah and explain why it is recommended (sunnah) rather than obligatory.

Core Idea
Proximity to the Imam and facing Qibla are meritorious but not required at Arafah.

While the entire plain of Arafah is valid for the essential standing (Wuquf), the Hanafi school encourages pilgrims to stand near the Imam to hear his teachings and behind him to face the Qibla. This lesson clarifies that these are recommendations, not obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is positioning oneself relative to the Imam during Wuquf. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), as the text states 'bayan al-afdaliyyah'.
2
Recognize the reasoning
The author gives two benefits: hearing the Imam's du'a and teaching, and facing Qibla by standing behind.
3
Note the scope
The text explicitly says this is a statement of preference because all of Arafah is mawqif.
4
Apply the ruling
The pilgrim should strive to do this, but if not possible, the wuquf is still valid.
5
Distinguish from obligation
Unlike the essential standing which is wajib, this is merely recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنّى لوگ امام کے قریب ٹھہریں
(عنایه )
قَالَ وَيَبْغِي لِلنَّاسِ أَنْ يَقِفُوا بِقُرُبِ الإِمَام لِأَنَّهُ يَدْعُوَ وَيُعْلَمُ فَيَعُوا وَيَسْتَمِعُوا وَيَسْعَى أَن يَقِفُوا وَرَاءَ الْإِمَامِ لِيَكُوْنَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ وَهَذَا بَيَانُ الأفضلية لأنَّ عَرَفَاتَ كُلَّهَا مَوَقَفٌ عَلَى مَاذَكَرْنَا
ترجمہ اور لوگوں کو چاہئے کہ وہ امام کے قریب کھڑے ہوں۔ کیونکہ امام دعا کرے گا اور احکام سکھلائے گا۔ پس لوگ یاد کر ہیں اور کان لگا کر سنیں اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ امام کے پیچھے کھڑے ہوں تا کہ قبلہ رخ ہو جائے اور یہ بیان افضلیت ہے کیونکہ عرفات پورے کا پورا موقف ہے اس بناء پر جو ہم نے ذکر کیا۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں دو باتوں کی ہدایت کی گئی ہے ایک یہ حاجی میدان عرفات میں امام المسلمین سے نزدیک کھڑا ہوتا کہ اسکی بیان کردہ باتیں سن کر یاد کر سکے، دوم یہ کہ امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہوتا کہ امام کی طرح یہ بھی مستقبل قبلہ ہو جائے۔ لیکن یہ باتیں واجب نہیں ہیں بلکہ افضل ہونے کا درجہ رکھتی ہیں۔
People should stand near the Imam (from 'Inayah). He said: It is desirable for the people to stand near the Imam, because he will make du'a and teach, so they may understand and listen. And it is appropriate that they stand behind the Imam so that they become facing the Qibla. And this is a statement of preference, because all of Arafat is a standing place, as we have mentioned. Translation: And the people should stand near the Imam. Because the Imam will make du'a and teach the rulings. So the people should remember and listen attentively. And it is appropriate that they stand behind the Imam so that they face the Qibla. And this is an expression of preference, because the entire Arafat is a standing place, based on what we have mentioned. Elaboration: In this passage, two things are guided: first, the pilgrim in the field of Arafah should stand near the Imam to hear and remember his words; second, he should stand behind the Imam to face the Qibla like the Imam. But these matters are not obligatory; they are merely preferred.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the recommended positioning of pilgrims relative to the Imam during Wuquf at Arafah. The author, drawing from al-Hidayah and the commentary al-'Inayah, advises pilgrims to stand close to the Imam to benefit from his du'a and teaching. Additionally, they should stand behind the Imam to ensure they are facing the Qibla. However, the text explicitly states that these are matters of preference (afdaliyyah), not obligation (wajib), because the entire plain of Arafah is valid for Wuquf. The Hanafi school emphasizes the virtue of proximity to the Imam and facing the Qibla, but does not require it.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): The entire area of Arafah, all of which is a valid place for Wuquf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why should pilgrims stand near the Imam according to the text?
A) To receive the Imam's blessing directly.
B) To hear his du'a and teaching.
C) To be closer to the Qibla.
D) To facilitate the stoning ritual later.

Key Takeaway
Standing near the Imam at Arafah is a recommended sunnah, not a wajib; the entire plain is valid for Wuquf.

Ghusl Before Wuquf is Sunnah, Not Wajib
Ruling on ghusl before standing at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ghusl before Wuquf at Arafah and explain why wudu suffices, using the analogy to Jumu'ah and Eid.

Core Idea
Ghusl before Wuquf is sunnah, not wajib; wudu suffices just as for Jumu'ah and Eid.

This lesson unpacks a concise ruling from al-Quduri about recommended acts before standing at Arafah. The author of al-Hidayah clarifies that ghusl is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation, and that wudu is sufficient. The analogy to Jumu'ah and Eid prayers provides the legal basis. Additionally, earnest du'a is recommended, following the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling for ghusl before Wuquf? The text says it is mustahabb/sunnah, not wajib.
Focus on the distinction between sunnah and wajib.
2
Understand the proof by analogy
The same ruling applies to Jumu'ah, Eid, and ihram. Why? Because all are occasions of gathering and worship where ghusl is recommended but not required.
This is qiyas jaliy – clear analogy.
3
Determine the consequence of not performing ghusl
If one does not perform ghusl, can he still stand at Arafah? Yes, wudu suffices. The act remains valid.
Missing a sunnah does not invalidate the act.
4
Analyze the du'a component
Striving in du'a is also mustahabb. The Prophet did so, and his du'as were accepted except for bloodshed and injustices.
This highlights the importance of du'a at Arafah and the need to resolve rights of others.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
A pilgrim arrives at Arafah without the ability to perform ghusl. Can he simply make wudu? Yes, according to the Hanafi school.
This avoids unnecessary hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أنْ يَعْتَسِلَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةِ وَيَجْتَهِدُ فِي الدُّعَاءِ أَمَّا الْاِغْتِسَالُ فَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِوَاجِبٍ وَلَوْ كتفى بِالْوُضُوءِ جَازَ كَمَا فِي الْجُمْعَةِ وَالْعَيْدَيْنِ وَعِندَ الإِحَرَامِ وَأَمَّا الْإِجْتِهَادُ فَلَأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ اجْتَهَدَ فِي الدَّعَاءِ فِى هَذَا الْمَوْقَفِ لِأُمَّتِهِ فَاسْتَجِيْب لَهُ إِلَّا فِى الدّمَاءِ وَالْمَظالم
ترجمہ کہا کہ مستحب ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے غسل کرے اور دعاؤں میں خوب کوشش کرے۔ رہا غسل کرنا تو وہ سنت ہے اور واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے وضو پر اکتفاء کیا تو جائز ہے جیسے جمعہ، عیدین اور بوقت احرام ہے اور کوشش سے دعا کرنا تو اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم
نے اس موقف میں اپنی امت کے لئے دعا میں بہت کوشش کی ہے تو آپ کی دعا سب قبول کی گئی سوائے خونوں اور مظالم کے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے غسل کرنا اور خوب دعا کرنا مستحب یعنی غیر واجب ہے۔ مستحب کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے غسل کرنا سنت ہے واجب نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر وضو پر اکتفاء کیا تو بھی جائز ہے جیسے جمعہ، عیدین اور بوقت احرام غسل کرنا سنت ہے۔ لیکن اگر وضو پر اکتفاء کیا تو جائز ہے۔ اور دعا میں کوشش کرنا مستحب اس لئے ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنی امت کے لئے اس موقف میں بہت کوشش کے ساتھ دعا کی ہے علاوہ قتل ناحق اور ان مظالم کے جو حقوق العباد سے متعلق ہیں۔ تمام دعائیں قبول بھی کی گئی ہیں ۔
He said: It is recommended to take a bath (ghusl) before standing at Arafah and to exert oneself in supplication. As for the bath, it is a sunnah, not an obligation. If he suffices with wudu, it is permissible, as in the case of Friday, the two Eids, and at the time of ihram. As for exertion in supplication, it is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) exerted himself in supplication at this standing place for his community, and it was accepted from him except in matters of blood and injustices. Translation: He said that it is mustahabb to perform ghusl before Wuquf at Arafah and to strive in du'a. Regarding ghusl, it is sunnah and not wajib, and if he suffices with wudu, it is permissible, like in Jumu'ah, the two 'Ids, and at the time of ihram. And striving in du'a is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) strove in du'a at this standing place for his ummah, so it was accepted from him except in matters of bloodshed and oppression. Elaboration: Al-Quduri said that ghusl before Wuquf and striving in du'a are mustahabb (not wajib). Clarifying mustahabb, the author of al-Hidayah says that ghusl before Wuquf is sunnah, not wajib. So if one suffices with wudu, it is permissible, like in Jumu'ah, the two 'Ids, and at ihram. And striving in du'a is mustahabb because the Prophet (peace be upon him) strove in du'a at this place for his ummah, and his du'as were accepted except those concerning wrongful killing and oppression related to rights of people.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the recommendation of ghusl and earnest du'a before Wuquf. The author explains that performing ghusl before standing at Arafah is a sunnah (recommended) not a wajib (obligation). One may suffice with wudu, just as in the cases of Jumu'ah and Eid prayers and at the time of ihram. The Hanafi school places this in the category of mustahabb or sunnah. The proof for the du'a is the Prophet's own practice of supplicating earnestly for his ummah, and it was accepted except for matters of blood (unjust killing) and injustices (zulm) related to the rights of others. This indicates that while personal du'a is accepted, certain sins require additional repentance and resolution between people.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; synonymous with sunnah in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ghusl before Wuquf at Arafah?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah, and wudu suffices.
C) It is mandatory only for the Imam.
D) It is not recommended at all.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl before Wuquf is a sunnah, not an obligation; wudu suffices, based on analogy to Jumu'ah and Eid.

When to Stop Talbiyah? Hanafi vs Maliki
Ruling on reciting Talbiyah at Arafah until stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that Talbiyah continues until Jamrat al-Aqabah and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Talbiyah continues until stoning — the Prophet's practice and analogy to takbir prove it.

A pilgrim in Hajj recites the Talbiyah, but when does it end? The Hanafi school maintains it continues until stoning the Jamrat al-Aqabah, while Imam Malik holds that it stops as soon as one stands at Arafah. This lesson unpacks the proofs behind each view, focusing on the Hanafi reliance on a specific hadith and a powerful analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, identify the Hanafi ruling: Talbiyah is recited intermittently at Arafah and continues until the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah, not cut at Wuquf.
2
Identify the opposing school and their argument
Next, note Imam Malik's view: Talbiyah is cut upon standing at Arafah, because the verbal response to the call of Hajj is only before engaging in the physical pillars.
Malik's reasoning is based on the sequence of Hajj actions.
3
Analyze the Hanafi textual proof
Examine the hadith cited: the Prophet continued Talbiyah until Jamrat al-Aqabah. This is a direct evidence (dalil naqli).
The hadith is ahad, but accepted in practice.
4
Analyze the Hanafi analogical proof
The second proof is qiyas: Talbiyah is analogous to takbir in salah. Just as takbir is recited until the end of salah, Talbiyah continues until the end of ihram, marked by stoning.
This analogy highlights the continuous nature of the pilgrimage's verbal response.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Finally, clarify the practical difference: Malikis stop Talbiyah at Wuquf; Hanafis continue until stoning. This affects the actual recitation during the day of Arafah and onward.
The Hanafi view is the mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُلَتِي فِي مَوْقَفَ سَاعَةً بَعْدَسَاعَةِ وَقَالَ مَالِكِ يَقْطَعُ التَّلْبِيَّةَ كَمَا يَقِفُ بِعَرَفَةَ لِأَنَّ الْإِجَابَةَ بِاللَّسَانِ قَبْلَ الْإِشْتِغَالِ بِالْأَرْكَانِ وَلَنَا مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَازَالَ يُلَبّى حَتَّى أتَى جَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةَ وَلِأَنَّ التَّلْبِيَةَ فِيهِ كَالتَّكْبِيرِ فِي الصَّلوةِ فَيَأْتِي بِهَا إِلَى آخِرِ جُزْءٍ مِّنَ الْإِحْرَامِ
ترجمہ اور اپنے موقف میں تھوڑی تھوڑی دیر کے بعد تلبیہ کہتا ہے۔ اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ جوں ہی عرفہ میں کھڑا ہو تلبیہ قطع کر دے۔ کیونکہ زبان سے حاضری کا جواب دینا ارکان کے ساتھ مشغول ہونے سے پہلے ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے کہ رسول اللہ برابر تلبیہ پڑھتے رہے یہاں تک کہ جمرۃ العقبہ تشریف لے آئے اور اس لئے کہ حج میں تلبیہ ایسا ہے جیسے نماز میں تکبیر ہے تو احرام کے آخری جز تک تلبیہ لائے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، حاجی میدان عرفات میں اپنے موقف میں برابر تلبیہ کہتا ہے یہاں تک کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے ۔ حضرت امام مالک
He recites Talbiyah at his standing place hour after hour. Malik said: He cuts the Talbiyah as soon as he stands at Arafah, because the response with the tongue is before engaging in the pillars (arkan). Our evidence is what was narrated: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) kept reciting Talbiyah until he came to Jamrat al-Aqabah. And because Talbiyah in Hajj is like the takbir in salah, so he brings it until the last part of ihram. Translation: And he recites Talbiyah in his standing place from time to time. Imam Malik said: As soon as he stands at Arafah, he should cut the Talbiyah, because the response with the tongue (i.e., answering the call of Hajj) is before occupying oneself with the pillars. And our (Hanafi) evidence is the hadith that the Prophet continuously recited Talbiyah until he reached Jamrat al-Aqabah. And because Talbiyah in Hajj is like the takbir in salah, so he performs it until the last part of ihram. Elaboration: The pilgrim in the field of Arafah recites Talbiyah continuously at his standing place until he stones Jamrat al-Aqabah. Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that one should stop Talbiyah upon beginning Wuquf.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the timing of Talbiyah during Wuquf. The Hanafi position, stated first, is that the pilgrim should continue reciting Talbiyah intermittently ('hour after hour') at Arafah. Imam Malik's position is that Talbiyah should be cut off as soon as one stands at Arafah, arguing that the verbal response (talbiyah) is for the journey before engaging in the pillars of Hajj. The Hanafi response provides two proofs: (1) a hadith that the Prophet continued Talbiyah until he reached Jamrat al-Aqabah; (2) an analogy (qiyas) that Talbiyah is like the takbir in salah, which is recited until the end of the prayer; similarly, Talbiyah continues until the end of ihram, which is marked by stoning the Jamrat al-Aqabah. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that Talbiyah is not cut at Wuquf but continues until the stoning of the great Jamrah.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The specific invocation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited during Hajj and Umrah.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqabah): The largest of the three stoning pillars at Mina, representing the devil's first appearance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, until when should a pilgrim recite Talbiyah?
A) Until entering Makkah.
B) Until standing at Arafah.
C) Until stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah.
D) Until the end of Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Talbiyah continues until Jamrat al-Aqabah, based on explicit hadith and analogy to takbir in salah.

Ghusl Before Wuquf at Arafah: Sunnah, Not Wajib
Ruling with proof: ghusl before Wuquf is sunnah, analogized to Jumu'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl before Wuquf, explain the qiyas analogy to Jumu'ah and Eid, and identify that wudu suffices.

Core Idea
Ghusl before Arafah is sunnah, not wajib; wudu suffices, as analogized to Jumu'ah and Eid.

The passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the recommended bath before the standing at Arafah. While some may assume it is obligatory, the text clarifies that it is a sunnah practice, not a wajib. The ruling is derived by analogy to other occasions where ghusl is sunnah. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and practical implications for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ghusl (full-body wash) before Wuquf at Arafah. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites analogy (qiyas) to ghusl for Jumu'ah, the two Eids, and upon entering ihram.
The phrase 'as in Jumu'ah, the two Eids, and at the time of ihram' is the explicit analogical link.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The shared effective cause (illah) is that all these are major religious gatherings where ghusl is sunnah. Thus, by analogy, Wuquf at Arafah is similarly sunnah.
4
Note the substitute
The text explicitly states that if one suffices with wudu, it is permissible. Wudu can replace ghusl without any penalty.
5
Identify the practical consequence
Pilgrims may perform wudu if water is scarce or if they find it difficult; the standing remains valid and the sunnah is fulfilled by wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أنْ يَعْتَسِلَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةِ وَيَجْتَهِدُ فِي الدُّعَاءِ أَمَّا الْاِغْتِسَالُ فَهُوَ سُنَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِوَاجِبٍ وَلَوْ كتفى بِالْوُضُوءِ جَازَ كَمَا فِي الْجُمْعَةِ وَالْعَيْدَيْنِ وَعِندَ الإِحَرَامِ وَأَمَّا الْإِجْتِهَادُ فَلَأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ اجْتَهَدَ فِي الدُّعَاءِ فِى هَذَا الْمَوْقَفِ لِأُمَّتِهِ فَاسْتَجِيْب لَهُ إِلَّا فِى الدّمَاءِ وَالْمَظالم ترجمہ کہا کہ مستحب ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے غسل کرے اور دعاؤں میں خوب کوشش کرے۔ رہا غسل کرنا تو وہ سنت ہے اور واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر اس نے وضو پر اکتفاء کیا تو جائز ہے جیسے جمعہ، عیدین اور بوقت احرام ہے اور کوشش سے دعا کرنا تو اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس موقف میں اپنی امت کے لئے دعا میں بہت کوشش کی ہے تو آپ کی دعا سب قبول کی گئی سوائے خونوں اور مظالم کے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے غسل کرنا اور خوب دعا کرنا مستحب یعنی غیر واجب ہے۔ مستحب کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے غسل کرنا سنت ہے واجب نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر وضو پر اکتفاء کیا تو بھی جائز ہے جیسے جمعہ، عیدین اور بوقت احرام غسل کرنا سنت ہے۔ لیکن اگر وضو پر اکتفاء کیا تو جائز ہے۔ اور دعا میں کوشش کرنا مستحب اس لئے ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنی امت کے لئے اس موقف میں بہت کوشش کے ساتھ دعا کی ہے علاوہ قتل ناحق اور ان مظالم کے جو حقوق العباد سے متعلق ہیں۔ تمام دعائیں قبول بھی کی گئی ہیں ۔
He said: It is mustahabb to take a bath before standing at Arafat and to strive in supplication. As for bathing, it is sunnah and not obligatory. If he suffices with wudu, it is permissible, just as in Jumu'ah, the two Eids, and at the time of ihram. As for striving in supplication, it is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) strove in supplication at this standing for his ummah, so his supplication was answered except concerning blood and injustices. Translation: He said that it is mustahabb to bathe before the standing at Arafat and to make much effort in supplications. As for bathing, it is sunnah and not obligatory. If he suffices with wudu, it is permissible, as in Jumu'ah, the two Eids, and at the time of ihram. And making effort in supplication is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made great effort in supplication at this standing for his ummah, so his supplication was accepted except for unlawful blood and those injustices that pertain to the rights of servants. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that bathing before the standing at Arafat and making much supplication is mustahabb, i.e., not obligatory. Elucidating mustahabb, the author of al-Hidayah says that bathing before the standing at Arafat is sunnah, not obligatory. Thus, if one suffices with wudu, it is permissible, as bathing for Jumu'ah, the two Eids, and at the time of ihram is sunnah. But if one suffices with wudu, it is permissible. And making effort in supplication is mustahabb because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made great effort with supplication for his ummah at this standing, except for unjust killing and those injustices that pertain to the rights of servants. All supplications were accepted.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on bathing (ghusl) before the standing at Arafah during Hajj. The author of al-Hidayah states that it is mustahabb (recommended) and clarifies that it is sunnah, not wajib. This means it is a confirmed practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) but not obligatory. If one performs only wudu instead of ghusl, it is valid and sufficient, analogous to the sunnah ghusl for Friday prayer, the two Eid prayers, and upon entering ihram. The emphasis on striving in supplication is based on the Prophet's own practice at Arafah, where his supplications were accepted except for matters involving bloodshed and injustices against others. Thus, the pilgrim is encouraged to make abundant du'a, but it is not obligatory either.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Full-body ritual washing; here it refers to the recommended bath before the standing at Arafah.
سنة (sunnah): A practice established by the Prophet; here it means recommended but not obligatory (between mustahabb and wajib).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; used interchangeably with sunnah in this context to indicate a non-obligatory meritorious act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on ghusl before the standing at Arafah according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is wajib, and wudu does not suffice.
B) It is sunnah, and wudu suffices if one cannot perform ghusl.
C) It is fard, and missing it invalidates Hajj.
D) It is makruh to perform ghusl before Wuquf.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl before Wuquf is sunnah, not wajib; wudu suffices, by analogy to Jumu'ah and Eid.

Ruling on Talbiyah During Wuquf: Hanafi vs Maliki
Resolves Hanafi-Maliki dispute on when to stop talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when talbiyah ceases during Hajj, explain its evidence, and distinguish it from the Maliki view.

Core Idea
Talbiyah continues until the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqabah, not stopping at Wuquf.

The timing of talbiyah during Hajj is a point of difference between the Hanafi and Maliki schools. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position that talbiyah continues from Wuquf until the first pebble is thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah. It refutes the Maliki view that talbiyah should stop immediately upon standing at Arafah. Understanding this difference helps you apply the correct practice and appreciate how the schools derive rulings from hadith and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling of the Hanafi school regarding the duration of talbiyah. The pilgrim recites talbiyah intermittently during Wuquf and continues until the first pebble is thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the Maliki objection
Imam Malik holds that talbiyah should cease as soon as the pilgrim stands at Arafah for Wuquf. Understand the rationale for this view.
The Maliki reasoning is that talbiyah is a verbal response, and once the actual pillar (Wuquf) begins, the response is no longer required.
3
Follow the Maliki proof
Examine the Maliki evidence: talbiyah is a verbal response (ijabah bil-lisan) that precedes engagement in the pillars (arkan). Therefore, it should stop when the pillar starts.
This is an argument based on the nature of talbiyah as a preparatory act.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school provides two proofs: (1) a hadith that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he reached Jamrat al-Aqabah; (2) an analogy (qiyas) to takbir in prayer, which is repeated until the end. The hadith overrides the qiyas in the matter of ramy itself.
The Hanafi response acknowledges that pure qiyas would require talbiyah during ramy, but the explicit hadith limits it to the first pebble.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi pilgrims continue talbiyah throughout Wuquf, Muzdalifah, and the journey to Mina, stopping only at the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqabah. Maliki pilgrims stop at the moment of Wuquf at Arafah.
This difference affects the performance of Hajj and potential need for dam if a wajib is missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُلَتِي فِي مَوْقَفَ سَاعَةً بَعْدَسَاعَةِ وَقَالَ مَالِكِ يَقْطَعُ التَّلْبِيَّةَ كَمَا يَقِفُ بِعَرَفَةَ لِأَنَّ الْإِجَابَةَ بِاللَّسَانِ قَبْلَ الْإِشْتِغَالِ بِالْأَرْكَانِ وَلَنَا مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَازَالَ يُلَبّى حَتَّى أتَى جَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةَ وَلِأَنَّ التَّلْبِيَةَ فِيهِ كَالتَّكْبِيرِ فِي الصَّلوةِ فَيَأْتِي بِهَا إِلَى آخِرِ جُزْءٍ مِّنَ الْإِحْرَامِ ترجمہ اور اپنے موقف میں تھوڑی تھوڑی دیر کے بعد تلبیہ کہتا ہے۔ اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ جوں ہی عرفہ میں کھڑا ہو تلبیہ قطع کر دے۔ کیونکہ زبان سے حاضری کا جواب دینا ارکان کے ساتھ مشغول ہونے سے پہلے ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے کہ رسول اللہ برابر تلبیہ پڑھتے رہے یہاں تک کہ جمرۃ العقبہ تشریف لے آئے اور اس لئے کہ حج میں تلبیہ ایسا ہے جیسے نماز میں تکبیر ہے تو احرام کے آخری جز تک تلبیہ لائے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، حاجی میدان عرفات میں اپنے موقف میں برابر تلبیہ کہتا ہے یہاں تک کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے ۔ حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ عرفی میں وقوف کرتے ہی تلبیہ ختم کر دے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تلبیہ زبان سے حاضری کا جواب ہے اور زبان سے حاضری کا جواب ارکان حج کے ساتھ مشغول ہونے سے پہلے پہلے ہے۔ پس جو نبی حج کارکن یعنی وقوف عرفہ شروع کیا تو تلبیہ ختم کر دے۔ ہماری دلیل حدیث رسول ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم رمی جمار تک برابر تلبیہ کہتے رہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تلبیہ حج کے اندر ایسا ہے جیسا کہ نماز کے اندر تکبیر اور نماز کے اندر تکبیر مکرر ہوتی ہے حتی کہ آخر نماز تک باقی رہتی ہے۔ پس اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے تلبیہ بھی آخر احترام تک باقی رہے گا۔ لیکن سوال ہو گا کہ اس قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ رمی جمار کے وقت بھی تلبیہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ جمرہ عقبہ پر پہلی کنکری پھینکتے ہی تلبیہ ختم کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ جواب: قیاس کا مقتضی تو یہی تھا لیکن اجتماع اور حدیث کی وجہ سے اس قیاس کو ترک کر دیا گیا۔
And he recites talbiyah at the standing place from time to time. Malik said: He stops talbiyah as soon as he stands at Arafah, because the response by the tongue is before engaging in the pillars. Our evidence is what was narrated: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) continued reciting talbiyah until he came to Jamrat al-Aqabah. And because talbiyah in it is like the takbir in prayer, so he performs it until the last part of ihram. Translation: And at his standing place he recites talbiyah intermittently. Imam Malik said: As soon as he stands at Arafah, he should stop talbiyah, because the verbal response is before occupying oneself with the pillars. Our evidence is the hadith that the Messenger of Allah continued reciting talbiyah until he came to Jamrat al-Aqabah. And because talbiyah in Hajj is like takbir in prayer, so he brings it until the last part of ihram. Explanation: The pilgrim, while standing in the plain of Arafat, continues reciting talbiyah until he throws the pebbles at Jamrat al-Aqabah. Imam Malik said that as soon as he makes Wuquf at Arafah, he should stop talbiyah. Imam Malik's evidence is that talbiyah is a verbal response, and the verbal response is before engaging in the pillars of Hajj. So when one begins the pillar of Hajj, i.e., Wuquf at Arafah, he should stop talbiyah. Our evidence is the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) continued reciting talbiyah until the throwing of the Jamarat. A second evidence is that talbiyah in Hajj is like takbir in prayer, and takbir in prayer is repeated and remains until the end of the prayer. So by analogy, talbiyah will remain until the end of ihram. However, a question arises: this analogy would require that talbiyah be recited at the time of throwing the Jamarat, but it is not; rather, at the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqabah, talbiyah is stopped. Answer: This is what analogy would require, but due to consensus (or narration) and hadith, this analogy is abandoned.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the timing of ending talbiyah during Hajj. The Hanafi position is that talbiyah should continue from the moment of Wuquf at Arafah until the pilgrim throws the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqabah. The Maliki position, attributed to Imam Malik, is that talbiyah should cease immediately upon standing at Arafah. The Hanafi evidence is twofold: first, a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) continued reciting talbiyah until he reached Jamrat al-Aqabah; second, an analogy (qiyas) to takbir in prayer, which is repeated until the end of the prayer. The Maliki evidence is that talbiyah is a verbal response to the call of Hajj, and once one begins the actual pillar (Wuquf), the response is no longer needed. The Hanafi response acknowledges that the analogy would suggest talbiyah during the throwing itself, but this is overridden by the hadith and consensus, so talbiyah stops at the first pebble.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim during Hajj as a response to God's call.
جمرہ عقبہ (Jamrat al-Aqabah): The largest of the three stone pillars at Mina, where the pilgrim throws seven pebbles on the day of Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the talbiyah end?
A) Immediately upon standing at Arafah
B) At sunset on the day of Arafah
C) At the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah
D) After completing all three Jamarat

Key Takeaway
Talbiyah continues until the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqabah, based on prophetic practice and analogy to takbir.

Departure to Muzdalifah After Sunset
States ruling on leaving Arafah after sunset for Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time and manner of departing from Arafah to Muzdalifah and identify the two proofs (dalil) cited.

Core Idea
Depart after sunset with calm, emulating the Prophet and opposing the polytheists.

This passage from the Hidayah explains the sunnah of departing from Arafah to Muzdalifah after sunset on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. The ruling emphasizes both timing and demeanor—leaving after sunset with calmness and dignity. The proofs are the Prophet's practice and the wisdom of distinguishing Muslims from the pre-Islamic polytheists who would leave early.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the passage rules on the departure (ifadah) from Arafah to Muzdalifah. Determine the hukm level: it is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasised sunnah).
The act is not obligatory but highly recommended.
2
Locate the first proof (dalil naqli)
The author cites the Prophet's action: he departed after sunset. This is a sunnah mutawatir (continuous practice). Analyse how the Prophet's fi'l establishes the ruling.
The Arabic quote: 'أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دَفَعَ بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ'.
3
Locate the second proof (wisdom/opposition)
The passage mentions that departing after sunset expresses opposition to the polytheists (mushrikeen) who left before sunset. This is a fiqhi consideration that reinforces the sunnah.
This proof is not a direct naql but a rationale (hikmah) that aligns with the sunnah.
4
Note the manner of departure
The text emphasises moving 'ala hīnatihim' (with dignity and calmness) and that the Prophet walked calmly on his mount. Identify that this calmness is also sunnah.
Haste is discouraged; the entire movement should be serene.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا غَرَبَتِ الشَّمْسُ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ مَعَهُ عَلَى هِيْنَتِهِمْ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا الْمُرْدَلَقَةَ لأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دَفَعَ بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَلِأَنَّ فِيهِ إِظْهَارُ مُخَالَفَةِ الْمُشْرِكِينَ وَكَانَ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ يَمْشِي عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ فِي الطريق على هيئة ترجمہ کہا اور جب آفتاب غروب ہو گیا تو امام لوگوں اور لوگ اس کے ساتھ ہوں اپنے وقار پر، یہاں تک کہ مزدلفہ میں آئیں۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم غروب کے بعد روانہ ہوئے تھے اور اس لئے کہ ایسا کرنے میں مشرکین کی مخالفت کا اظہار ہے اور حضور پیے اپنی اونٹنی پر راستہ میں سکون کے ساتھ چلتے تھے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، نویں ذی الحجہ کو آفتاب غروب ہونے کے بعد بغیر نماز مغرب پڑھے امام اور لوگ پر وقار طریقہ سے لوٹ کر مزدلفہ آ جائیں۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے غروب کے بعد واپسی فرمائی ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ کہ اس میں مشرکین کی مخالفت کا اظہار ہے۔ کیونکہ جاہلیت میں مشرکین عرفات سے غروب آفتاب سے پہلے ہی لوٹ جاتے تھے۔ اور حضور پیے اپنی اونٹنی قصواء پر انتہائی سکون اور وقار کے ساتھ چلتے تھے۔
He said: When the sun sets, the Imam and the people with him move from Arafah in a dignified manner until they come to Muzdalifah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) departed after sunset, and because in it is an expression of opposition to the polytheists. The Prophet (peace be upon him) would walk on his mount on the road in a dignified manner. Translation: He said: When the sun sets, the Imam and the people with him move in their dignity until they come to Muzdalifah. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) departed after sunset, and because in this is an expression of opposition to the polytheists. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) would walk on his she-camel on the road with great calm and dignity. Explanation: On the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah, after sunset without praying Maghrib, the Imam and the people should return to Muzdalifah in a dignified manner. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) returned after sunset. A second evidence is that it shows opposition to the polytheists, as in the days of ignorance they would leave Arafah before sunset. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) would walk on his she-camel Qaswa with extreme calm and dignity.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on the departure from Arafah to Muzdalifah. After sunset on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah, the Imam and the pilgrims should proceed to Muzdalifah in a calm and dignified manner, without praying Maghrib on the way. The evidence is the Prophet's own practice: he departed after sunset. Additionally, this practice distinguishes Muslims from the polytheists of Jahiliyyah who would leave before sunset. The Prophet is reported to have moved with tranquility on his she-camel, teaching that haste is not recommended.

Key Terms
إفاضة (ifadah): The movement from Arafah to Muzdalifah after sunset; also used for the Tawaf al-Ifadah.
مزدلفہ (Muzdalifah): The plain between Arafah and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after Wuquf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the pilgrim depart from Arafah to Muzdalifah?
A) Before sunset on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah
B) Immediately after sunset, with calm and dignity
C) After praying Maghrib at Arafah
D) At midnight

Key Takeaway
The sunnah departure from Arafah is after sunset, in calmness, based on the Prophet's practice and opposition to the polytheists.

Departing Before the Imam Due to Crowding
Ruling on early departure from Arafah due to crowding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on departing from Arafah before the Imam due to crowding and explain the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Departing before the Imam is valid if still within Arafah, but staying is better; fear of crowding excuses.

In Hajj, the Wuquf at Arafah is a central rite. The Imam's departure marks the end of the standing. But what if crowds make it dangerous to stay? This lesson clarifies that the Hanafi school permits leaving a bit early to avoid harm, as long as you remain inside Arafah's boundaries. We also examine the prophetic practice of Aisha to support this dispensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What specific action is being ruled upon? The pilgrim departing from Arafah before the Imam due to fear of crowding. The ruling is 'jaiz' (permissible) but not optimal.
The ruling is derived from the principle of necessity (darurah).
2
Locate the Condition for Validity
The text states that the departure is valid only if the pilgrim does not go beyond the boundaries of Arafah. Staying within the boundary is the key condition.
This condition ensures the Wuquf is still considered performed at Arafah.
3
Identify the Preferred Action (Afdal)
Despite the permissibility, the more virtuous (afdal) action is to remain in place until the Imam departs. This is to avoid performing the rite before its proper time.
The virtue is tied to following the Imam's lead as a sunnah.
4
Examine the Dalil (Proof)
The text cites the action of Aisha (ra) who, after the Imam's departure, called for a drink and broke her fast before departing. This shows that a slight delay after the Imam is acceptable and by extension, that departing before him is permissible if there is a valid reason.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim but its meaning is referenced.
5
Apply to Modern Context
In crowded Hajj conditions today, if a pilgrim fears being crushed or harm, they may depart a bit early as long as they stay within the marked boundaries of Arafah.
This ruling does not apply to leaving without a valid excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنَّ خَافَ الرِّحَامَ فَدَفَعَ قَبْلَ الْإِمَامِ وَلَمْ يُجَاوِرُ حُدُودَ عَرَفَةَ أَجْزَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُفِضُ مِنْ عَرَفَةَ وَالْأَفَضَلُّ أَنْ يُقِفَ فِي مَقَامِهِ كَيْلَا يَكُرُنُ أُخِذَا فِي الأَدَاءِ قَبْلَ وَقَتِهَا فَلَوْ مَكَثَ قَلِيلًا بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَإِفَاضَةِ الْإِمَامِ لِخَوفِ الرِّحَامِ فَلَا بَأسَ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ عَائِشَةَ بَعْدَ إِفَاضَةِ الْإِمَامِ دَعَتْ بِشَرَابٍ فَافَطْرَتَ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَتْ ترجمہ پس اگر حاجی نے ازدحام کا خوف کیا اور امام سے پہلے چل دیا اور حدود عرفہ سے باہر نہیں ہوا تو جائز ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ وہ عرفہ سے نہیں آیا۔ اور افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنے مقام پر تھہرا ر ہے تا کہ ادا کو اس کے وقت سے پہلے شروع کرنے والا نہ ہے پس اگر غروب آفتاب اور امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد ازدحام کے خوف کی وجہ سے تھوڑی دیر خبر گیا تو کچھ مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے
If he fears crowding and departs before the Imam and does not go beyond the boundaries of Arafah, it suffices, because he has not left Arafah. And the more virtuous is that he stays in his place so that he is not one who performs the act before its time. If he waits a little after sunset and the Imam's departure due to fear of crowding, there is no harm, because it is narrated that Aisha, after the Imam's departure, called for a drink and broke her fast, then departed. Translation: So if the pilgrim fears crowding and leaves before the Imam, and does not go beyond the boundaries of Arafah, it becomes permissible. Because he has not left Arafah. And the better is that he remains in his place so that he is not one who begins the act before its time. So if after sunset and the Imam's departure, due to fear of crowding, he waited a little, there is no harm, because it is narrated that Aisha, after the Imam's departure, asked for a drink and broke her fast, then departed.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a pilgrim fears excessive crowding and considers departing from Arafah before the Imam's departure. The ruling is that if he leaves but remains within the boundaries of Arafah, his Wuquf is still valid because he has not actually left the designated area. However, it is more virtuous (afdal) to stay in his place and depart only after the Imam, to ensure that the act is performed at its proper time. If he waits a short while after sunset and after the Imam has departed, due to crowding concerns, it is permissible. The evidence is the narration of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who, after the Imam's departure, asked for a drink and broke her fast (i.e., ended her fast of the day) before departing herself. This shows that a slight delay after the Imam's departure is acceptable.

Key Terms
إفاضة (ifadah): Departure from Arafah; here used for the movement towards Muzdalifah.
ازدحام (izdiham): Crowding or thronging of people, causing difficulty.

B) It is permissible as long as he stays within the boundaries of Arafah.
C) It is obligatory to leave before the Imam in case of crowding.
D) It is not allowed under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits early departure from Arafah if needed to avoid crowding, provided the pilgrim stays within the boundary; however, waiting for the Imam is more virtuous.

When Does Talbiyah End? Hanafi vs Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on talbiyah timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on when talbiyah ends and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the textual evidence and qiyas.

Core Idea
Talbiyah ends at the first stoning, not at Arafah — the Prophet's practice overrides analogy.

In this passage, we examine a key difference between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the timing of ending the talbiyah during Hajj. The Maliki view holds that talbiyah ends at the standing of Arafah, while the Hanafi school argues that it continues until the stoning of Jamrah al-Aqabah. Understanding the proofs behind each position sharpens your ability to weigh textual evidence against analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly when the talbiyah ends according to the Hanafi school.
It ends upon throwing the first pebble at Jamrah al-Aqabah.
2
Identify the Maliki position and their proof
What does the Maliki school hold, and what is their evidence?
They argue talbiyah is a verbal response of presence, so it ends when the central ritual (wuquf) begins.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the hadith of the Prophet continuing talbiyah until stoning, and the analogy (qiyas) with takbir in prayer.
The hadith is the primary evidence; the qiyas supports it but is not the main pillar.
4
Address the objection to the qiyas
Why does the Hanafi school abandon the analogy's requirement that talbiyah should continue throughout stoning?
The specific hadith and consensus (ijma) override the qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in the pilgrimage?
Hanafi pilgrims continue talbiyah until stoning; Maliki pilgrims stop at Arafah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نے فرمایا کہ عرفی میں وقوف کرتے ہی تلبیہ ختم کر دے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تلبیہ زبان سے حاضری کا جواب ہے اور زبان سے حاضری کا جواب ارکان حج کے ساتھ مشغول ہونے سے پہلے پہلے ہے۔ پس جو نبی حج کارکن یعنی وقوف عرفہ شروع کیا تو تلبیہ ختم کر دے۔ ہماری دلیل حدیث رسول ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم رمی جمار تک برابر تلبیہ کہتے رہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تلبیہ حج کے اندر ایسا ہے جیسا کہ نماز کے اندر تکبیر اور نماز کے اندر تکبیر مکرر ہوتی ہے حتی کہ آخر نماز تک باقی رہتی ہے۔ پس اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے تلبیہ بھی آخر احترام تک باقی رہے گا۔ لیکن سوال ہو گا کہ اس قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ رمی جمار کے وقت بھی تلبیہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ جمرہ عقبہ پر پہلی کنکری پھینکتے ہی تلبیہ ختم کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ جواب: قیاس کا مقتضی تو یہی تھا لیکن اجتماع اور حدیث کی وجہ سے اس قیاس کو ترک کر دیا گیا۔
He said that at Arafah, when one stands, he should end the talbiyah. Imam Malik's evidence is that talbiyah is the verbal response of presence, and the verbal response of presence is before engaging in the rituals of Hajj. So when the Prophet started the act of Hajj, i.e., standing at Arafah, he ended the talbiyah. Our evidence is the hadith of the Messenger that he continued saying talbiyah until the stoning of the Jamarat. The second evidence is that talbiyah in Hajj is like takbir in prayer, and takbir in prayer is repeated until the end of prayer. So by analogy, talbiyah will remain until the end of the rituals. But there is a question: this analogy requires that talbiyah be present at the time of stoning, but it is not; rather, at Jamrah al-Aqabah, upon throwing the first pebble, talbiyah is ended. Answer: The analogy required that, but due to consensus and hadith, this analogy was abandoned.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the timing of ending the talbiyah during Hajj. Imam Malik holds that talbiyah ends when one begins the standing (wuquf) at Arafah, reasoning that talbiyah is a verbal declaration of presence, which precedes engagement in the physical rituals of Hajj. The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith that the Prophet continued talbiyah until the stoning of the Jamarat, argues that talbiyah continues until the first stoning at Jamrah al-Aqabah. They support this with an analogy to takbir in prayer, which remains until the end. However, they acknowledge a counter-analogy: if talbiyah continues by analogy to takbir, it should last throughout stoning, but it actually ends at the first stone. The Hanafi response is that this analogy is overridden by the specific hadith and the consensus (ijma) of the Companions on ending talbiyah at stoning. The author follows the author's order, first stating the Maliki view and evidence, then the Hanafi view and evidence, and finally addressing the objection.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The formula 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by pilgrims during Hajj.
وقوف عرفہ (wuquf Arafah): The standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, a rukn of Hajj.
رمی جمار (ramy al-jimar): The stoning of the three pillars (Jamarat) in Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the talbiyah end?
A) At the beginning of wuquf at Arafah
B) Upon throwing the first pebble at Jamrah al-Aqabah
C) After completing the tawaf al-ifadah
D) At sunset on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Talbiyah ends at the first stoning of Jamrah al-Aqabah according to the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Companions.

Leaving Arafah Before the Imam Due to Crowding
Ruling on leaving Arafah early due to crowding without exiting boundaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pilgrim leaves Arafah before the Imam due to fear of crowding while staying within the boundaries, and identify when a sacrifice (dam) is required.

Core Idea
Leaving Arafah early is permissible if you stay within the boundaries; exceeding them may require a sacrifice.

This lesson addresses the common concern of extreme crowding at Arafah. The Hanafi school provides a specific ruling that balances the obligation of standing at Arafah with practical necessity. Understanding the conditions and consequences of early departure is essential for every pilgrim and those guiding them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
The pilgrim fears crowding and leaves Arafah before the Imam. Determine whether he stays within the boundaries of Arafah or exits them.
Boundaries are defined; staying inside means he has not truly departed.
2
Apply the ruling for staying within boundaries
If he stays within boundaries, his Hajj is valid (ajzahu) although it is khilaf al-awla (contrary to what is better). No dam required.
This is makruh tanzihan.
3
Identify the conditions for dam
If he exits the boundaries before sunset and does not return before the Imam's departure, a dam is wajib. If he returns and then departs with the Imam after sunset, the dam is dropped. Returning after sunset does not drop the dam.
The commentary adds these details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنَّ خَافَ الرِّحَامَ فَدَفَعَ قَبْلَ الْإِمَامِ وَلَمْ يُجَاوِرُ حُدُودَ عَرَفَةَ أَجْزَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُفِضُ مِنْ عَرَفَةَ وَالْأَفَضَلُّ أَنْ يُقِفَ فِي مَقَامِهِ كَيْلَا يَكُرُنُ أُخِذَا فِي الأَدَاءِ قَبْلَ وَقَتِهَا فَلَوْ مَكَثَ قَلِيلًا بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَإِفَاضَةِ الْإِمَامِ لِخَوفِ الرِّحَامِ فَلَا بَأسَ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ عَائِشَةَ بَعْدَ إِفَاضَةِ الْإِمَامِ دَعَتْ بِشَرَابٍ فَافَطْرَتَ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَتْ ترجمہ پس اگر حاجی نے ازدحام کا خوف کیا اور امام سے پہلے چل دیا اور حدود عرفہ سے باہر نہیں ہوا تو جائز ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ وہ عرفہ سے نہیں آیا۔ اور افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنے مقام پر تھہرا ر ہے تا کہ ادا کو اس کے وقت سے پہلے شروع کرنے والا نہ ہے پس اگر غروب آفتاب اور امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد ازدحام کے خوف کی وجہ سے تھوڑی دیر خبر گیا تو کچھ مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد پانی مانگا پھر روزہ افطار کیا پھر روانہ ہوئیں۔ (رش) تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاجی از دحام شکلکے اندیشہ سے امام سے پہلے ہی عرفات سے روانہ ہو گیا اور حدود عرفہ سے نہیں نکلا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عرفات سے روانگی نہیں کہلائے گی۔ لیکن پھر بھی یہ خلاف اولیٰ ہے۔ بلکہ افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنی جگہ ٹھہرا ر ہے تا کہ وقت سے پہلے ادا یعنی عرفات سے روانہ ہونا متفق نہ ہو۔ مذکورہ عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر امام کے روانہ ہونے سے پہلے اور غروب سے پہلے حدود عرفات سے تجاوز کر گیا تو اس پر قربانی واجب ہو گی لیکن اگر عرفات کی طرف لوٹ آیا پھر امام کے ساتھ غروب کے بعد روانہ وہا تو قربانی ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر غروب کے بعد لوٹا تو ساقط نہیں ہوگی ۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاجی نے غروب آفتاب اور امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد خوف ازدحام کی وجہ سے تھوڑی دیر کی تو اس میں کوئی مضا کننہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے عرفات سے امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد پانی مانگ کر روزہ افطار کیا ہے اور پھر روانہ ہوئیں اور ظاہر ہے کہ پانی مانگنے اور روزہ افطار کرنے میں کچھ دیر لگی ہوگی ۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ امام کے روانہ ہونے اور آفتاب غروب ہونے کے بعد کچھ دیر ٹھہرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
If he fears crowding and leaves before the Imam and does not exceed the boundaries of Arafah, it suffices him, because he did not depart from Arafah. And it is better that he stay in his place so that he is not one who performs the action before its time. So if he waits a little after sunset and the Imam's departure due to fear of crowding, there is no harm because it is narrated that Aisha after the Imam's departure asked for a drink, broke her fast, then departed. Translation: So if the pilgrim feared crowding and left before the Imam and did not go beyond the boundaries of Arafah, it became permissible. Because he did not come from Arafah. And it is better that he stay in his place so that he is not one who begins the action before its time. So if after sunset and the Imam's departure due to fear of crowding he delays a little, there is no harm, because it is reported that Aisha after the Imam's departure asked for water, broke her fast, then departed. Explanation: The first issue: If the pilgrim leaves Arafat before the Imam due to fear of crowding and does not exit the boundaries of Arafah, it is permissible. Because this is not considered leaving Arafat. But it is contrary to what is better. Rather, it is better to stay in his place so that he is not one who performs the action before its time. From the aforementioned expression it is known that if he exceeds the boundaries of Arafat before the Imam's departure and before sunset, a sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory upon him. But if he returns to Arafat and then departs with the Imam after sunset, the sacrifice is dropped. If he returns after sunset, it is not dropped. Second issue: If the pilgrim delays a little after sunset and the Imam's departure due to fear of crowding, there is no harm. Because it is reported that Aisha after the Imam's departure from Arafat asked for water, broke her fast, and then departed. It is obvious that asking for water and breaking the fast took some time. So it is established that there is no harm in waiting a little after the Imam's departure and sunset.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues regarding departure from Arafah. First: If a pilgrim fears extreme crowding and leaves the area of Arafah before the Imam, but does not go beyond the actual boundaries of Arafah (i.e., he remains within the defined limits), his Hajj remains valid because he technically has not 'departed' from the sacred precinct. However, this is makruh tanzihan (disliked) and contrary to the preferred practice. If he actually leaves the boundaries entirely before sunset and before the Imam, a sacrifice (dam) is required. But if he returns to the boundaries and then departs with the Imam after sunset, the dam is waived; if he returns only after sunset, the dam is not waived. Second: It is permissible for a pilgrim to delay his departure from Arafah for a short while after the Imam has moved and after sunset, if the delay is due to necessity (like fear of crowding), and the proof is the action of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who, after the Imam departed, took time to drink and break her fast before leaving.

Key Terms
ازدحام (izdiham): Crowding or congestion that causes difficulty for pilgrims.
قربانی (qurbani): A sacrifice (dam) required as compensation for certain violations or as a substitute for a missed wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a pilgrim leaves Arafah before the Imam due to crowding but stays within the boundaries?
A) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is permissible but disliked (makruh tanzihan)
C) It is forbidden and requires a dam
D) It is better than staying with the Imam

Key Takeaway
Leaving Arafah early due to crowding is permissible if boundaries are not exceeded; exceeding boundaries may require a sacrifice unless the pilgrim returns in time.

Delaying Departure from Arafah After Sunset and Imam's Departure
Ruling on delaying departure after Imam's departure due to crowding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the permissibility of delaying departure from Arafah after the Imam has left and after sunset, citing the evidence from Aisha's action.

Core Idea
Delaying departure from Arafah after the Imam is permissible, especially if due to necessity like crowding.

This lesson addresses a second scenario: what if a pilgrim has already stayed with the Imam until sunset and the Imam has departed, but the pilgrim delays his own departure for a short while due to fear of crowding? The Hanafi school rules this permissible, based on the action of Aisha (RA). This demonstrates how the sunnah of the Companions provides practical guidance for easing hardship in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
The pilgrim has already stood at Arafah, the Imam has departed after sunset, but the pilgrim delays his own departure for a short time due to fear of crowding.
The delay is after the Imam's departure, not before.
2
State the ruling
There is no harm (la ba'sa) in this delay. It is permissible.
The text uses 'la ba'sa' which indicates permissibility, not obligation.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is the action of Aisha (RA) who, after the Imam departed, asked for a drink, broke her fast, and then departed. This shows that a short delay is acceptable.
The hadith is cited as evidence (riwayah).
4
Consider the rationale
The delay is allowed to avoid harm from crowding. The Hanafi school considers necessity (haja) as grounds for leniency.
This is consistent with the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

فَإِنَّ خَافَ الرِّحَامَ فَدَفَعَ قَبْلَ الْإِمَامِ وَلَمْ يُجَاوِرُ حُدُودَ عَرَفَةَ أَجْزَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُفِضُ مِنْ عَرَفَةَ وَالْأَفَضَلُّ أَنْ يُقِفَ فِي مَقَامِهِ كَيْلَا يَكُرُنُ أُخِذَا فِي الأَدَاءِ قَبْلَ وَقَتِهَا فَلَوْ مَكَثَ قَلِيلًا بَعْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَإِفَاضَةِ الْإِمَامِ لِخَوفِ الرِّحَامِ فَلَا بَأسَ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ عَائِشَةَ بَعْدَ إِفَاضَةِ الْإِمَامِ دَعَتْ بِشَرَابٍ فَافَطْرَتَ ثُمَّ أَفَاضَتْ ترجمہ پس اگر حاجی نے ازدحام کا خوف کیا اور امام سے پہلے چل دیا اور حدود عرفہ سے باہر نہیں ہوا تو جائز ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ وہ عرفہ سے نہیں آیا۔ اور افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنے مقام پر تھہرا ر ہے تا کہ ادا کو اس کے وقت سے پہلے شروع کرنے والا نہ ہے پس اگر غروب آفتاب اور امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد ازدحام کے خوف کی وجہ سے تھوڑی دیر خبر گیا تو کچھ مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد پانی مانگا پھر روزہ افطار کیا پھر روانہ ہوئیں۔ (رش) تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاجی از دحام شکلکے اندیشہ سے امام سے پہلے ہی عرفات سے روانہ ہو گیا اور حدود عرفہ سے نہیں نکلا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عرفات سے روانگی نہیں کہلائے گی۔ لیکن پھر بھی یہ خلاف اولیٰ ہے۔ بلکہ افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنی جگہ ٹھہرا ر ہے تا کہ وقت سے پہلے ادا یعنی عرفات سے روانہ ہونا متفق نہ ہو۔ مذکورہ عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر امام کے روانہ ہونے سے پہلے اور غروب سے پہلے حدود عرفات سے تجاوز کر گیا تو اس پر قربانی واجب ہو گی لیکن اگر عرفات کی طرف لوٹ آیا پھر امام کے ساتھ غروب کے بعد روانہ وہا تو قربانی ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر غروب کے بعد لوٹا تو ساقط نہیں ہوگی ۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاجی نے غروب آفتاب اور امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد خوف ازدحام کی وجہ سے تھوڑی دیر کی تو اس میں کوئی مضا کننہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے عرفات سے امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد پانی مانگ کر روزہ افطار کیا ہے اور پھر روانہ ہوئیں اور ظاہر ہے کہ پانی مانگنے اور روزہ افطار کرنے میں کچھ دیر لگی ہوگی ۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ امام کے روانہ ہونے اور آفتاب غروب ہونے کے بعد کچھ دیر ٹھہرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
If he fears crowding and leaves before the Imam and does not exceed the boundaries of Arafah, it suffices him, because he did not depart from Arafah. And it is better that he stay in his place so that he is not one who performs the action before its time. So if he waits a little after sunset and the Imam's departure due to fear of crowding, there is no harm because it is narrated that Aisha after the Imam's departure asked for a drink, broke her fast, then departed. Translation: So if the pilgrim feared crowding and left before the Imam and did not go beyond the boundaries of Arafah, it became permissible. Because he did not come from Arafah. And it is better that he stay in his place so that he is not one who begins the action before its time. So if after sunset and the Imam's departure due to fear of crowding he delays a little, there is no harm, because it is reported that Aisha after the Imam's departure asked for water, broke her fast, then departed. Explanation: The first issue: If the pilgrim leaves Arafat before the Imam due to fear of crowding and does not exit the boundaries of Arafah, it is permissible. Because this is not considered leaving Arafat. But it is contrary to what is better. Rather, it is better to stay in his place so that he is not one who performs the action before its time. From the aforementioned expression it is known that if he exceeds the boundaries of Arafat before the Imam's departure and before sunset, a sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory upon him. But if he returns to Arafat and then departs with the Imam after sunset, the sacrifice is dropped. If he returns after sunset, it is not dropped. Second issue: If the pilgrim delays a little after sunset and the Imam's departure due to fear of crowding, there is no harm. Because it is reported that Aisha after the Imam's departure from Arafat asked for water, broke her fast, and then departed. It is obvious that asking for water and breaking the fast took some time. So it is established that there is no harm in waiting a little after the Imam's departure and sunset.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues regarding departure from Arafah. First: If a pilgrim fears extreme crowding and leaves the area of Arafah before the Imam, but does not go beyond the actual boundaries of Arafah (i.e., he remains within the defined limits), his Hajj remains valid because he technically has not 'departed' from the sacred precinct. However, this is makruh tanzihan (disliked) and contrary to the preferred practice. If he actually leaves the boundaries entirely before sunset and before the Imam, a sacrifice (dam) is required. But if he returns to the boundaries and then departs with the Imam after sunset, the dam is waived; if he returns only after sunset, the dam is not waived. Second: It is permissible for a pilgrim to delay his departure from Arafah for a short while after the Imam has moved and after sunset, if the delay is due to necessity (like fear of crowding), and the proof is the action of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who, after the Imam departed, took time to drink and break her fast before leaving.

Key Terms
ازدحام (izdiham): Crowding or congestion that causes difficulty for pilgrims.
افاضة (ifadah): The departure from Arafah after sunset; also used for the flowing of pilgrims from Arafah to Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The action of Aisha (RA)
C) A saying of Abu Hanifa
D) Consensus of the scholars

Key Takeaway
Delaying departure from Arafah after the Imam due to necessity is permissible, supported by the action of Aisha.

Preferred Standing at Mount Quzah in Muzdalifah
Rulings on recommended standing in Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended actions upon arriving in Muzdalifah and explain the evidentiary basis for each.

Core Idea
Standing near Mount Quzah in Muzdalifah is mustahab because the Prophet and Umar did so.

This lesson covers three practical sunnahs (recommendations) for the pilgrim upon reaching Muzdalifah, based on the actions of the Prophet ﷺ and the caliph Umar. Understanding these nuances enhances the spiritual quality of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommended acts
The text lists: stand near Mount Quzah, avoid descending on the road, and stand behind the Imam.
All three are mustahab.
2
State the ruling level
The Hanafi school classifies each as mustahab (recommended), not wajib.
Mustahab = performed for reward, omitted without sin.
3
Locate the dalil for each
Standing near Quzah: the Prophet and Umar did it. Avoiding road: to prevent harming passersby. Standing behind Imam: same reasoning as at Arafah.
The dalil for Quzah is a direct action of the Prophet.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action establishes recommendation (sunnah); Umar's action reinforces it.
Without a command, action indicates istihbab, not wujub.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا أَتَى مُزدَلَفَةً فَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يُقِفَ بِقُرْبِ الْجَلِ الَّذِى عَلَيْهِ المِيْقَدَةُ يُقَالُ لَهُ قُرَحْ لِأَنَّ نبيَّ وَقَفَ عِدَ هَذَا الْجَبَلِ وَكَذَا عُمَرُ وَ يَتَحَرَّرُ فِي التَّزُولِ عَنِ الطَّرِيقِ كَيْلا يَضُرَّ بِالْمَارَّة فَيَنْزِلُ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ أَوْ يَسَارِه. وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أنْ يَقِفَ وَرَاءَ الْإِمَامِ لِمَا بَيَّنَا فِي الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةً ترجمہ کیا اور جب مزدلفہ میں آجائیں تو مستحب یہ ہے کہ وقف اس پہاڑ کے قرب میں کرے جس پر آتشدان ہے جس کو قزح کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اسی پہاڑ کے نزدیک ٹھہرے اور یونہی عمر بن خطاب اور راستہ کے اندر اترنے میں احتراز کرے تا کہ گذرنے والوں کو ضر نہ پہنچے۔ پس راستہ سے دائیں یا بائیں اترے اور مستحب یہ ہے کہ امام کے پیچھے بھمبر ے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے وقوف عرفہ میں بیان کی ہے۔ کی تشریح حاجی کے لئے مزدلفہ میں جبل قزح کے قریب ٹھہر نا مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ اس پہاڑ کے نزدیک ٹھہرے ہیں اور فاروق اعظم نے بھی اس کے قریب وقوف کیا ہے۔ حاجی کو چاہئے کہ راستہ میں نہ اترے بلکہ راستہ سے دائیں یا بائیں طرف اترے۔ کیونکہ راستہ میں اترنے کی صورت میں لوگوں کو تکلیف ہوگی۔ اور حاجی کے لئے مزدلفہ میں بھی امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہونا مستحب ہے۔ دلیل وہی ہے جو وقوف عرفہ کے سلسلہ میں گذر چکی ہے۔ فوائد قزح قاف کے ضمہ اور زاء کے فتحہ کے ساتھ ۔ یہ لفظ قزح بمنی ارتفع سے ماخوذ ہے بلند ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا نام قرح رکھ دیا لیں۔ اس پہاڑ پر میقد وہ تھا جس میں زمانہ جاہلیت والے آگ روشن کیا کرتے تھے ۔ اور ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں لیلیہ مزدلفہ میں شمع روشن کی جاتی تھی اور ہارون رشید کے بعد بڑے بڑے چراغ روشن کئے جاتے رہے۔
He said: When he comes to Muzdalifah, it is recommended that he stand near the mountain on which there is the fire-place, called Quzah, because the Prophet stood near this mountain, and likewise Umar, and he should avoid descending in the road so as not to harm passersby; so he should descend to its right or left. And it is recommended that he stand behind the Imam for the reason we explained for standing at Arafah. Translation: He said, and when they come to Muzdalifah, it is recommended to stand near the mountain on which there is a fireplace, called Quzah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood near this mountain, and likewise Umar ibn al-Khattab, and he should avoid descending on the road so as not to harm passersby. So he should descend to the right or left of the road. And it is recommended that he stand behind the Imam for the reason we stated in the section on standing at Arafah. Explanation: For the pilgrim, standing near Mount Quzah in Muzdalifah is recommended. Because the Messenger of Allah stood near this mountain, and Farooq the Great also stood near it. The pilgrim should not descend on the road but should descend to the right or left of the road, because descending on the road will cause discomfort to people. And for the pilgrim, standing behind the Imam in Muzdalifah is also recommended. The proof is the same as that which passed in the section on standing at Arafah. Benefits: Quzah is with a dammah on qaf and fathah on za. This word is derived from 'qazah' meaning 'elevated', so the mountain was named Quzah because of its height. On this mountain there was a fireplace in which the people of the Jahiliyyah used to kindle fire. And during the time of Harun al-Rashid, a candle was lit in Muzdalifah on the night of Muzdalifah, and after Harun al-Rashid, large lamps were lit.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on the recommended actions upon reaching Muzdalifah. Firstly, it is mustahab (recommended) to stand near Mount Quzah, the mountain on which there was a fireplace used in pre-Islamic times, because the Prophet stood there, and also Umar ibn al-Khattab. Secondly, one should avoid standing on the road itself, but rather descend to the right or left side of the road, so as not to inconvenience other pilgrims. Thirdly, it is mustahab to stand behind the Imam (i.e., not in front of him) when making the standing (wuquf) in Muzdalifah, based on the same reasoning given for standing behind the Imam at Arafah (i.e., following the Imam's lead). The final paragraph gives linguistic and historical notes about the name 'Quzah' and the tradition of lighting fires there.

Key Terms
قزح (Quzah): The name of a mountain in Muzdalifah near which it is recommended to stand.
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended act; omission does not incur sin but is rewarded if done.
مزدلفہ (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafah and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Anywhere within Muzdalifah
B) Near Mount Quzah
C) On the road to Mina
D) In front of the Imam

Key Takeaway
In Muzdalifah, the pilgrim should stand near Mount Quzah, avoid the road, and stand behind the Imam — all as mustahab acts following the Prophet's example.

Leaving Arafat Before the Imam and Delaying After Sunset
Explains two issues: leaving Arafat early and delaying after sunset

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving Arafat early (within boundaries vs. crossing boundaries) and explain when a sacrificial dam becomes wajib or is waived, using the proof from the action of Aisha (RA).

Core Idea
Leaving Arafat early is permissible within boundaries; crossing boundaries before sunset triggers a dam unless you return before sunset.

Many pilgrims worry about navigating the crowds at Arafat on the day of Hajj. May they leave early? May they delay departure? This lesson clarifies two issues based on the Hanafi school: the permissibility of leaving Arafat before the imam while staying within the boundaries, and the permissibility of delaying a short while after sunset. The Prophet's ﷺ emphasis on ease (yusr) underlies these rulings, with the sacrifice (dam) serving as compensation for any violation of the proper sequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage addresses two separate issues: (a) leaving Arafat early due to crowding, and (b) delaying departure after sunset due to crowding.
Stay focused on the distinction; each has a different ruling.
2
Classify the first scenario
Determine whether the pilgrim leaves within the boundaries of Arafat or crosses them. This distinction changes the ruling from permissible (ja'iz) to requiring a dam.
The text specifies that staying within boundaries does not count as leaving Arafat (khuruj).
3
Apply the dam rule
If the pilgrim crosses boundaries before sunset and before the imam departs, a dam becomes wajib. If he returns to Arafat before sunset and later departs with the imam, the dam is waived; if he returns after sunset, the dam remains.
The condition for waiver is returning before sunset, not after.
4
Understand the second scenario
After sunset and after the imam's departure, a short delay is permissible, as proven by Aisha's action of asking for water and breaking her fast before departing.
The delay is justified by necessity (crowding) and the Prophet's Sunnah as demonstrated by his household.
5
Recognize the epistemological weight
The ruling is from the Hanafi school, recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah, and is mufta bihi. While other schools may require staying until sunset without exception, Hanafi school allows flexibility in case of hardship.
This ikhtilaf is considered legitimate; both positions are based on valid proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد پانی مانگا پھر روزہ افطار کیا پھر روانہ ہوئیں۔(رش)تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاجی ازدحام شدید کے اندیشہ سے امام سے پہلے ہی عرفات سے روانہ ہو گیا اور حدود عرفات سے نہیں نکلا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عرفات سے روانگی نہیں کہلائے گی۔ لیکن پھر بھی یہ خلاف اولیٰ ہے۔ بلکہ افضل یہ ہے کہ اپنی جگہ ٹھہرا رہے تا کہ وقت سے پہلے ادائی یعنی عرفات سے روانہ ہونا متفق نہ ہو۔ مذکورہ عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر امام کے روانہ ہونے سے پہلے اور غروب سے پہلے حدود عرفات سے تجاوز کر گیا تو اس پر قربانی واجب ہو گی لیکن اگر عرفات کی طرف لوٹ آیا پھر امام کے ساتھ غروب کے بعد روانہ ہوا تو قربانی ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر غروب کے بعد لوٹا تو ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاجی نے غروب آفتاب اور امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد خوف ازدحام کی وجہ سے تھوڑی دیر کی تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے عرفات سے امام کے روانہ ہونے کے بعد پانی مانگ کر روزہ افطار کیا ہے اور پھر روانہ ہوئیں اور ظاہر ہے کہ پانی مانگنے اور روزہ افطار کرنے میں کچھ دیر لگی ہوگی۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ امام کے روانہ ہونے اور آفتاب غروب ہونے کے بعد کچھ دیر ٹھہرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
After the imam departed, she asked for water, then broke her fast, then departed. Commentary: The ruling is that if a pilgrim, out of fear of severe crowding, leaves Arafat before the imam but does not exit the boundaries of Arafat, it is permissible. Because this will not be considered leaving Arafat. However, it is against what is preferable. Rather, it is better to stay in one's place so that early departure from Arafat is not agreed upon. From the mentioned phrase, it is understood that if one crosses the boundaries of Arafat before the imam's departure and before sunset, then sacrificing a dam is obligatory. But if he returns to Arafat and then departs after sunset with the imam, the dam is waived. And if he returns after sunset, it is not waived. Second issue: If a pilgrim, after sunset and after the imam's departure, delays a little due to fear of crowding, there is no harm in that. Because it is narrated that Lady Aisha asked for water after the imam's departure from Arafat and broke her fast, then departed. It is obvious that asking for water and breaking the fast took some time. Thus it is proven that there is no harm in staying a little after the imam's departure and after sunset.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses two issues related to staying at Arafat. The first issue: if a pilgrim leaves Arafat before the imam due to fear of severe crowding but remains within the boundaries, it is permissible but less than ideal (khilaf awla). However, if he crosses the boundaries before sunset and before the imam departs, a dam (one sheep) becomes wajib. This obligation is dropped if he returns to Arafat and later departs with the imam after sunset. But if he returns only after sunset, the dam remains. The second issue: after sunset and after the imam leaves, the pilgrim may delay a short while due to crowding. This is based on the action of Lady Aisha, who requested water and broke her fast after the imam's departure, indicating a delay is allowable. The Hanafi school thus permits a reasonable delay to avoid hardship, but the preferred practice is to depart promptly after the imam.

Key Terms
عرفات (Arafat): A plain near Makkah where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; boundaries are specified.
حدود (hudud): The legal boundaries of Arafat within which waqf must occur.
قربانی (qurbani/dam): A sacrificial animal offered as compensation for a violation of Hajj rituals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim crosses the boundaries of Arafat before sunset and before the imam's departure, what is required?
A) The Hajj is invalid
B) A dam becomes wajib
C) Nothing is required
D) The pilgrim must repeat the waqf

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits leaving Arafat early within boundaries and delaying after sunset for necessity, but crossing boundaries before sunset without return requires a dam.
