Preferred Place for Standing in Muzdalifah
Describes the mustahabb location near Jabal Qarh and etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mustahabb location for waqf in Muzdalifah and explain the basis for its recommendation.

Core Idea
Standing near Jabal Qarh in Muzdalifah is mustahabb because the Prophet and Umar did so.

This lesson examines the recommended location for standing (waqf) in Muzdalifah as described in Al-Hidayah. The text identifies a specific mountain called Jabal Qarh, provides evidence from the Prophet's practice, and includes etiquette for avoiding inconvenience to others. Understanding this ruling helps pilgrims align their Hajj with the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is waqf (standing) in Muzdalifah. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
Waqf in Muzdalifah is not a rukn of Hajj but a sunnah.
2
Locate the specific recommended place
The text specifies standing near the mountain called Qarh (Jabal Qarh), which has a fireplace. This is the precise recommended location.
The mountain is also known as Jabal Qarh, derived from 'irtifa' (height).
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The ruling is based on the Prophet's (peace be upon him) practice and the example of Caliph Umar. Their actions serve as dalil for recommendation.
According to Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi'l indicates istihbab unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Apply the etiquette
The pilgrim should avoid descending on the road to prevent harm to passersby. Instead, he should stand to the right or left. Also, standing behind the imam is mustahabb, as at Arafat.
This etiquette preserves community harmony.
5
Understand the historical context
Jabal Qarh was used for lighting fires in pre-Islamic times and later for lamps during the Abbasid era. The name Qarh means 'high'.
The fireplace (mīqada) on the mountain is a historical landmark.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا أَتَى مُزدَلَفَةً فَالْمُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يُقِفَ بِقُرْبِ الْجَبَلِ الَّذِى عَلَيْهِ المِيْقَدَةُ يُقَالُ لَهُ قُرَیْحٌ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَقَفَ عِنْدَ هَذَا الْجَبَلِ وَكَذَا عُمَرُ رضي الله عنه وَيَتَحَرَّزُ فِي النُّزُولِ عَنِ الطَّرِيقِ كَيْلا يَضُرَّ بِالْمَارَّةِ فَيَنْزِلُ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ أَوْ يَسَارِهِ. وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أنْ يَقِفَ وَرَاءَ الْإِمَامِ لِمَا بَيَّنَا فِي الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةً.ترجمہ: اور جب مزدلفہ میں آجائیں تو مستحب یہ ہے کہ وقف اس پہاڑ کے قرب میں کرے جس پر آتشدان ہے جس کو قریح کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اسی پہاڑ کے نزدیک ٹھہرے اور یونہی عمر بن خطاب رضی اللہ عنہ اور راستہ میں اترنے سے احتراز کرے تاکہ گذرنے والوں کو ضرر نہ پہنچے۔ پس راستہ سے دائیں یا بائیں اترے اور مستحب یہ ہے کہ امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہو اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے وقوف عرفہ میں بیان کی ہے۔تشریح: حاجی کے لئے مزدلفہ میں جبل قریح کے قریب ٹھہرنا مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ ﷺ اس پہاڑ کے نزدیک ٹھہرے ہیں اور فاروق اعظم نے بھی اس کے قریب وقوف کیا ہے۔ حاجی کو چاہئے کہ راستہ میں نہ اترے بلکہ راستہ سے دائیں یا بائیں طرف اترے۔ کیونکہ راستہ میں اترنے کی صورت میں لوگوں کو تکلیف ہوگی۔ اور حاجی کے لئے مزدلفہ میں بھی امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہونا مستحب ہے۔ دلیل وہی ہے جو وقوف عرفہ کے سلسلہ میں گذر چکی ہے۔ فوائد: قریح قاف کے ضمہ اور راء کے فتحہ کے ساتھ، یہ لفظ اَرْتَفَعَ سے ماخوذ ہے بلند ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا نام قریح رکھا گیا۔ اس پہاڑ پر میقدہ تھا جس میں زمانہ جاہلیت والے آگ روشن کیا کرتے تھے۔ اور ہارون رشید کے زمانہ میں لیلہ مزدلفہ میں شمع روشن کی جاتی تھی اور ہارون رشید کے بعد بڑے بڑے چراغ روشن کئے جاتے رہے۔
He said: When he comes to Muzdalifah, it is mustahabb to stand near the mountain on which the fireplace is, called Qarh, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood near this mountain, and similarly Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). And he should be careful when descending from the road so as not to harm passersby, so he should descend to its right or left. And it is mustahabb to stand behind the imam for the reason we explained regarding standing at Arafah. Translation: When you come to Muzdalifah, it is recommended to stop near the mountain that has a fireplace, called Qarh, because the Prophet stood near this mountain, and also Umar Radiyallahu Anhu. And he should avoid descending on the road so as not to harm passersby. So he should descend to the right or left of the road. And it is mustahabb to stand behind the imam for the reason we explained in the section on standing at Arafah. Commentary: For the pilgrim, it is mustahabb to stand near Jabal Qarh in Muzdalifah, because the Messenger of Allah stood near this mountain, and also Umar al-Farooq stood near it. The pilgrim should not descend on the road but rather to the right or left side of the road, because descending on the road will cause inconvenience to people. And it is mustahabb for the pilgrim to stand behind the imam in Muzdalifah as well, for the reason already mentioned in the context of the standing at Arafah. Benefits: Qarh is with dammah on qaf and fatah on ra, derived from irtafa'a (to be high), and it was named Qarh due to its height. On this mountain there was a fireplace where the people of the Jahiliyyah used to light fires. And in the time of Harun al-Rashid, a candle was lit on the night of Muzdalifah, and after Harun al-Rashid, large lamps continued to be lit.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended place for staying (waqf) in Muzdalifah. The preferred location is near Jabal Qarh, the small mountain with a fireplace, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) and Caliph Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) stood there. The pilgrim should avoid standing on the road to prevent inconvenience to others; instead, he should stand to the right or left of the road. Additionally, it is mustahabb to stand behind the imam, just as at Arafat. The commentary also provides linguistic and historical notes: the name Qarh derives from 'irtifa' (height), and the mountain was used for fire-lighting in pre-Islamic times and later for lamps during the Abbasid era. This ruling emphasizes following the Prophet's Sunnah in even the specific locations within Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
مزدلفہ (Muzdalifah): A place between Mina and Arafat where pilgrims spend the night after Arafat and perform waqf.
جبل قریح (Jabal Qarh/Qurahy): A specific mountain in Muzdalifah near which the Prophet stood; also known as Jabal Qarh.
وقف (waqf): Standing in a specific place as part of Hajj rituals.

The Number of Iqamas for Combined Prayer at Muzdalifah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqama count for Muzdalifah combination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of iqamas for combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and explain why Zufar's qiyas is rejected.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, one iqama suffices because Isha is in its time; extra iqama at Arafat is for notification of an advanced prayer.

When performing the Hajj, the imam combines Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi school, following the hadith of Jabir, uses one adhan and one iqama. But Imam Zufar argues for two iqamas, analogizing to the combination at Arafat. This lesson examines the proofs and reasoning behind the majority Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the point of dispute: the number of iqamas for combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah.
2
Identify the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn hold that only one adhan and one iqama are needed.
This is based on direct hadith evidence.
3
Understand Zufar's qiyas
Zufar analogizes to the combination at Arafat, where two iqamas are used for Zuhr and Asr.
His argument is that both are combinations, so the same rule should apply.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The key difference: at Arafat, Asr is advanced (prayed before its time), requiring extra notification via a second iqama. At Muzdalifah, Isha is in its time, so no extra iqama is necessary.
This distinction breaks the analogy.
5
Apply the hadith evidence
The hadith of Jabir directly states that the Prophet combined with one adhan and one iqama. This explicit Sunnah overrides qiyas.
The mufta bihi follows the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيُصَلَّى الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ الْمَغْرِبَ وَالْعِشَاءَ بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَتَيْنِ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْجَمْعِ بِعَرَفَةَ وَلَنَا رِوَايَةُ جَابِرٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ جَمَعَ بَيْنَهُمَا بِأَذَانٍ وَإِقَامَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَلِأَنَّ الْعِشَاءَ فِي وَقَتِهِ فَلَا يُفْرَدُ بِالْإِقَامَةِ إِعْلَامًا بِخِلَافِ الْعَصْرِ بِعَرَفَةَ لِأَنَّهُ مُقَدَّمٌ عَلَى وَقْتِهِ فَأُفْرِدَ بِهَا لِزِيَادَةِ الْإِعْلَامِ.ترجمہ: کہا۔ اور امام لوگوں کو مغرب اور عشاء ایک اذان اور ایک اقامت کے ساتھ پڑھائے اور امام زفر نے کہا ہے کہ ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ، عرفہ میں ظہر و عصر کو جمع کرنے پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور ہماری دلیل حضرت جابر کی روایت ہے کہ حضور نے ان دونوں کو ایک اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ جمع فرمایا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ عشاء اپنے وقت میں ہے لہذا آگاہ کرنے کے لئے اقامت علیحدہ نہیں کہی جائے گی۔ برخلاف عرفہ میں عصر کے کیونکہ وہ اپنے وقت پر مقدم ہے تو آگاہی زیادہ کرنے کے لئے اس کے واسطے اقامت علیحدہ کی گئی ہے۔تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام مغرب اور عشاء کو مزدلفہ میں عشاء کے وقت میں ایک اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ جمع کرے۔ امام زفر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ پڑھے۔ امام زفر نے مزدلفہ کے اندر جمع بین المغرب والعشاء کو عرفات میں جمع بین الظهر والعصر پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح عرفات میں ظہر و عصر کو ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ جمع کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح مزدلفہ میں مغرب اور عشاء کو ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ پڑھا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل حضرت جابر کی حدیث ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مغرب و عشاء کو مزدلفہ میں ایک اذان اور ایک اقامت کے ساتھ جمع فرمایا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عشاء اپنے وقت میں ہے لہذا لوگوں کو آگاہ کرنے کے لئے علیحدہ اقامت کی قطعا ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ برخلاف عصر کے کہ میدان عرفات میں عصر کی نماز اپنے وقت سے پہلے پڑھی جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے لوگوں کو مزید آگاہ کرنے کے لئے عصر کے واسطے اقامت کہی جائے گی۔
He said: The imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqama. And Zufar said: with one adhan and two iqamas, analogizing to the combination at Arafa. And our proof is the narration of Jabir that the Prophet combined them with one adhan and one iqama. And because Isha is in its time, so it is not given a separate iqama for notification, unlike Asr at Arafa because it is advanced to its time, so it was given a separate iqama for increased notification. Translation: He said: The imam should pray with the people Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqama. Imam Zufar said: with one adhan and two iqamas, analogizing to the combination of Zuhr and Asr at Arafa. Our proof is the narration of Jabir that the Prophet combined them with one adhan and one iqama. And because Isha is in its time, so a separate iqama is not needed for informing, unlike Asr at Arafa because it is advanced to its time, so a separate iqama was made for it for greater notification. Commentary: The issue is that the imam combines Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah at the time of Isha with one adhan and one iqama. Imam Zufar's view is that it should be with one adhan and two iqamas. Imam Zufar analogizes the combination of Maghrib and Isha in Muzdalifah to the combination of Zuhr and Asr at Arafat, i.e., just as Zuhr and Asr are combined at Arafat with one adhan and two iqamas, likewise Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah would be with one adhan and two iqamas. Our proof is the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqama. The second proof is that Isha is in its time, so there is absolutely no need for a separate iqama for informing. Unlike Asr, because the Asr prayer in the field of Arafat is prayed before its time, therefore for additional notification, an iqama is recited for Asr.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (the view followed in the matn and the majority) and Imam Zufar regarding the number of iqamas for the combined Maghrib and Isha prayer at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi position, supported by the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah (may Allah be pleased with him), is that only one adhan and one iqama are necessary. The reasoning is that Isha is performed within its own time, so there is no need for an extra iqama to announce an advanced prayer. In contrast, at Arafat, Asr is performed before its time, so a separate iqama is given to emphasize the timeliness. Imam Zufar's analogy (qiyas) is rejected because the situation differs: at Arafat, the combination involves advancing Asr, necessitating extra notification, whereas at Muzdalifah, Isha is not advanced. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, following the explicit hadith.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer recited before the prayer.
اقامت (iqama): The second call to prayer recited immediately before the prayer begins.
جمع بین الصلاتین (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers at one time, permissible in Arafat and Muzdalifah during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school use only one iqama for the combined prayer at Muzdalifah?
A) Because Maghrib and Isha are combined
B) Because Isha is in its time, so no extra notification needed
C) Because the hadith of Jabir does not mention iqama
D) Because only one prayer is obligatory

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school follows the explicit hadith of Jabir, using one iqama for combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, rejecting qiyas due to the difference in the time of the second prayer.

Prohibition of Nafl Between Combined Prayers at Muzdalifah
Prohibition of nafl with proof from prophetic action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on supererogatory prayer between Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, explain the consequence of violating it, and identify the basis for the ruling.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, nafl between combined prayers breaks the jam'; only iqama is repeated.

When pilgrims combine Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, they must preserve the unity of the combination. This lesson explains why supererogatory prayers are not allowed during that interval and what happens if someone prays them anyway — a crucial detail for those performing Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that one should not pray supererogatory (nafl) between the two combined prayers at Muzdalifah. This is a prohibition (makruh tahrimi) to preserve the jam'.
2
Understand the reason
The reason is that praying nafl would 'occupy' the time meant for the combination, creating a separation (fasl) between the two obligatory prayers.
3
Determine the consequence if violated
If one does pray nafl or engages in any other activity causing separation, he must repeat the iqama for Isha to reconnect the prayers.
The adhan is not repeated, unlike at Arafat.
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
The ruling is based on the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) at Muzdalifah: he prayed Maghrib, ate supper, then gave a separate iqama for Isha without repeating the adhan.
This demonstrates that a moderate separation followed by a fresh iqama suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَا يَتَطَوَّعُ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ يَحِلُّ بِالْجَمْعِ وَلَوْ تَطَوَّعَ أَوْ تَشَاغَلَ بِشَيْءٍ أَعَادَ الْإِقَامَةَ لِوُقُوعِ الْفَصْلِ وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُعِيدَ الْأَذَانَ كَمَا فِي الْجَمْعِ الْأَوَّلِ إِلَّا أَنَّا اكْتَفَيْنَا بِإِعَادَةِ الْإِقَامَةِ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى مَغْرِبَ بِمُزْدَلَفَةَ ثُمَّ تَعَشَّى ثُمَّ أَفْرَدَ الْإِقَامَةَ لِلْعِشَاءِ.ترجمہ: اور ان دونوں کے درمیان نفل نہیں پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ جمع میں محل ہے اور اگر نفل پڑھا یا کسی کام میں مشغول ہو گیا تو فصل کے واقع ہونے کی وجہ سے اقامت کا اعادہ کرے۔ اور مناسب تو یہ تھا کہ اذان کا بھی اعادہ کرے جیسے اول جمع میں ہے مگر ہم نے اقامت کے اعادہ پر اکتفاء کیا۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مزدلفہ میں مغرب پڑھی پھر کھانا تناول فرمایا پھر عشاء کے لئے علیحدہ اقامت کہی۔تشریح: مسئلہ مزدلفہ میں مغرب اور عشاء کے درمیان حاجی نفل نہ پڑھے کیونکہ درمیان میں نفل پڑھنا جمع میں مخل ہوگا۔ اور اگر درمیان میں نفل پڑھا یا کوئی دوسرا کام کیا تو چونکہ دونوں نمازوں یعنی مغرب اور عشاء میں فصل واقع ہو گیا اس لئے اقامت کا اعادہ کرے۔
He does not pray supererogatory between them because he becomes occupied with the combination. And if he prays supererogatory or busies himself with something, he repeats the iqama due to the separation occurring. And it would be proper to repeat the adhan as in the first combination (at Arafat), but we sufficed with repeating the iqama because it is narrated that the Prophet prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then ate supper, then gave a separate iqama for Isha. Translation: He should not pray supererogatory (nafl) between them (Maghrib and Isha) because the time is for the combination (jam'). If he prays nafl or engages in any other activity, he should repeat the iqama due to the separation (fasl) that has occurred. And it would be appropriate to also repeat the adhan, as in the first combination (at Arafat), but we suffice with repeating the iqama alone, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then ate dinner, then gave a separate iqama for Isha. Commentary: The issue is that at Muzdalifah, between Maghrib and Isha, the pilgrim should not pray any supererogatory prayer because praying nafl in between would interfere with the combination (jam'). And if he does pray nafl or does some other work, since a separation (fasl) has occurred between the two prayers (Maghrib and Isha), he must repeat the iqama.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This ruling prohibits performing any supererogatory (nafl) prayer between the combined Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah. The reason is that the combination (jam') requires continuity; introducing a nafl prayer or any other activity creates a separation (fasl) between the two obligatory prayers. If such a separation occurs, the iqama must be repeated for the second prayer (Isha) to reinstate the connection. Notably, the adhan does not need to be repeated, unlike at Arafat where both adhan and iqama are repeated if separation occurs. This is based on the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him), who after Maghrib ate supper and then gave a separate iqama for Isha without repeating the adhan. The wisdom is that at Muzdalifah, the emphasis is on maintaining the unity of the combination without unnecessary extra calls. The Hanafi school considers it makruh tahrimi to pray nafl between them because it disrupts the intended sunnah of combining.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayer, not obligatory at this time.
جمع بین الصلاتین (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers at one time, here at Muzdalifah for Maghrib and Isha.
فصل (fasl): Separation or break between the two prayers that disrupts the combination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing, the prayer is valid
B) Repeat both adhan and iqama
C) Repeat the iqama only
D) Repeat the adhan only

Key Takeaway
At Muzdalifah, to preserve the combination, no supererogatory prayer is allowed between Maghrib and Isha; if a separation occurs, only the iqama needs to be repeated.

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah: One Iqamah or Two?
Ruling on combining prayers at Muzdalifah with Zufar's qiyas objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of iqamahs for combining prayers at Muzdalifah, explain the proof from hadith and timing, and evaluate Zufar's qiyas objection.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, one iqamah suffices because Isha is in its own time, unlike Asr at Arafat.

This lesson addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ritual of combining Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah during Hajj. While the majority of the Hanafi school prescribes a single adhan and a single iqamah, Imam Zufar argued for two iqamahs by analogy to the combination of Zuhr and Asr at Arafat. Understanding the reasoning behind the majority view – based on direct Prophetic practice (hadith) and the differing temporal status of the prayers – is crucial for correctly performing this sunnah and appreciating how textual evidence overrides analogy in Hanafi methodology.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi ruling
Identify the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the number of adhans and iqamahs when combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah.
The ruling is: one adhan and one iqamah for both prayers.
2
Identify Zufar's opposing view
State Imam Zufar's position and the basis of his analogy (qiyas). He analogized to the combination at Arafat where two iqamahs are used.
Zufar's view: one adhan, two iqamahs.
3
Examine the primary Hanafi proof
Analyze the hadith of Jabir (radiAllahu anhu) as a direct textual evidence (dalil naqli) that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) combined with one adhan and one iqamah.
This is a stronger proof than qiyas because it is a direct sunnah.
4
Understand the secondary reasoning (ta'lil)
Understand why the timing of Isha (in its own time) justifies a single iqamah, while Asr at Arafat (advanced before its time) requires an extra iqamah for notification.
The extra iqamah serves as an alert; when the prayer is in its own time, no such alert is needed.
5
Apply the ruling and note the thamarah al-khilaf
Recognize the practical consequence: at Muzdalifah only one iqamah, at Arafat two iqamahs. Then determine which position is mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi is the majority view based on authentic hadith.

ترجمہ: کہا۔ اور امام لوگوں کو مغرب اور عشاء ایک اذان اور ایک اقامت کے ساتھ پڑھائے اور امام زفر نے کہا ہے کہ ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ، عرفہ میں ظہر و عصر کو جمع کرنے پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور ہماری دلیل حضرت جابر کی روایت ہے کہ حضور نے ان دونوں کو ایک اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ جمع فرمایا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ عشاء اپنے وقت میں ہے۔ لہذا آگاہ کرنے کے لئے اقامت علیحدہ نہیں کہی جائے گی۔ برخلاف عرفہ میں عصر کے کیونکہ وہ اپنے وقت پر مقدم ہے تو آگاہی زیادہ کرنے کے لئے اس کے واسطے اقامت علیحدہ کی گئی ہے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام مغرب اور عشاء کو مزدلفہ میں عشاء کے وقت میں ایک اذان اور اقامت کے ساتھ جمع کرے۔ امام زفر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ پڑھے۔ امام زفر نے مزدلفہ کے اندر جمع بین المغرب والعشاء کو عرفات میں جمع بین الظهر والعصر پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح عرفات میں ظہر و عصر کو ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ جمع کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح مزدلفہ میں مغرب اور عشاء کو ایک اذان اور دو اقامتوں کے ساتھ پڑھا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل حضرت جابر کی حدیث ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مغرب و عشاء کو مزدلفہ میں ایک اذان اور ایک اقامت کے ساتھ جمع فرمایا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عشاء اپنے وقت میں ہے لہذا لوگوں کو آگاہ کرنے کے لئے علیحدہ اقامت کی قطعا ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ بر خلاف عصر کے کہ میدان عرفات میں عصر کی نماز اپنے وقت سے پہلے پڑھی جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے لوگوں کو مزید آگاہ کرنے کے لئے عصر کے واسطے علیحدہ اقامت کہی جائے گی۔
He said: The Imam should lead the people in Maghrib and Isha prayers with one adhan and one iqamah. Zufar said: with one adhan and two iqamahs, drawing an analogy with the combination at Arafat. Our evidence is the narration of Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) combined them with one adhan and one iqamah, and because Isha is in its time, so it is not singled out with an iqamah as a notification, unlike Asr at Arafat because it is advanced before its time, so it was singled out with it for increased notification.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of combining Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The ruling, as per the majority of the Hanafi school, is that the Imam prays both prayers with a single adhan and a single iqamah. Imam Zufar differed, arguing that two iqamahs should be used, analogizing to the combination of Zuhr and Asr at Arafat. The Hanafi response cites the hadith of Jabir radiAllahu anhu that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) combined with one adhan and one iqamah. The second proof is that at Muzdalifah, Isha is offered in its own time, so no special notification is needed, whereas at Arafat, Asr is advanced before its time, necessitating an extra iqamah to alert the people. The commentary elaborates that the dispute is based on qiyas (analogy) versus the explicit sunnah. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view.

Key Terms
جمع (jama‘): Combining two prayers at one time (here, Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah).
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to commence prayer.

Optional Prayers Between Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah
Ruling that no nafl is prayed between the two combined prayers, and the effect of separating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing optional prayers between combined prayers at Muzdalifah and apply the rule of fasl to determine whether adhan or iqamah must be repeated.

Core Idea
No nafl between combined prayers at Muzdalifah; if separated, only iqamah is repeated, based on the Prophet's action.

When combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah during Hajj, the pilgrim is encouraged to pray them consecutively without any interruption. The Hanafi school clarifies that if an optional prayer or any activity separates them, only the iqamah is repeated for the second prayer, not the adhan. This ruling derives from the Prophet's practice as recorded in hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing optional (nafl) prayer between Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. The ruling: it should not be done; it is part of the sunnah to pray them consecutively. If done, it creates a separation (fasl) necessitating repetition of the iqamah only.
The ruling is specific to Muzdalifah, not Arafat.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) who prayed Maghrib, ate supper, then gave a separate iqamah for Isha without adhan.
This is a dalil naqli from the Prophet's action.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action shows that a separation (eating) occurred, but he only repeated the iqamah, not the adhan. This indicates that the adhan is not required to be repeated in this situation.
The analogy with Arafat (where both adhan and iqamah are repeated) is overridden by the specific practice at Muzdalifah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text mentions that theoretically, the adhan should be repeated as in the first combination (at Arafat), but the Hanafi school follows the specific practice at Muzdalifah.
No inter-madhhab dispute is mentioned; this is a choice within Hanafi based on evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the explicit hadith action, which is given precedence over the qiyas with Arafat. Thus, the mufta bihi is to repeat only the iqamah.
The authority weight is zahir riwayah from the Prophet's sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَا يَتَطَوَّعُ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ يَحِلُّ بِالْجَمْعِ وَلَوْ تَطَوَّعَ أَوْ تَشَاغَلَ بِشَيْءٍ أَعَادَ الْإِقَامَةَ لِوُقُوعِ الْفَصْلِ وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُعِيدَ الْأَذَانَ كَمَا فِي الْجَمْعِ الْأَوَّلِ إِلَّا أَنَّا اكْتَفَيْنَا بِإِعَادَةِ الْإِقَامَةِ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ صَلَّى مَغْرِبَ بِمُزْدَلَفَةَ ثُمَّ تَعَشَّى ثُمَّ أَفْرَدَ الْإِقَامَةَ لِلْعِشَاءِ
ترجمہ: اور ان دونوں کے درمیان نفل نہیں پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ جمع میں محل ہے اور اگر نفل پڑھا یا کسی کام میں مشغول ہو گیا تو فصل کے واقع ہونے کی وجہ سے اقامت کا اعادہ کرے۔ اور مناسب تو یہ تھا کہ اذان کا بھی اعادہ کرے جیسے اول جمع میں ہے مگر ہم نے اقامت کے اعادہ پر اکتفاء کیا۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مزدلفہ میں مغرب پڑھی پھر کھانا تناول فرمایا پھر عشاء کے لئے علیحدہ اقامت کہی۔
تشریح: مسئلہ مزدلفہ میں مغرب اور عشاء کے درمیان حاجی نفل نہ پڑھے کیونکہ درمیان میں نفل پڑھنا جمع میں مخل ہوگا۔ اور اگر درمیان میں نفل پڑھا یا کوئی دوسرا کام کیا تو چونکہ دونوں نمازوں یعنی مغرب اور عشاء میں فصل واقع ہو گیا اس لئے اقامت کا اعادہ کرے۔ مناسب تو یہ تھا کہ اذان کا بھی اعادہ کرے جیسا کہ عرفات میں ظہر وعصر کے درمیان فصل واقع ہونے کی صورت میں اذان کا اعادہ کیا جاتا ہے لیکن ہم نے فقط اقامت کے اعادہ پر اس لئے اکتفا کیا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک بار مزدلفہ میں مغرب کی نماز پڑھی پھر کھانا تناول فرمایا پھر عشاء کے لئے علیحدہ اقامت کہی یعنی اقامت کا اعادہ فرمایا نہ کہ اذان کا۔
He does not pray optional (nafl) between them because he is in a state of combination (jama‘). If he prays optional or becomes occupied with something, he repeats the iqamah due to the separation occurring. It would have been appropriate that he repeat the adhan as well, as in the first combination, but we sufficed with repeating the iqamah because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then ate supper, then singled out the iqamah for Isha.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on performing optional prayers between Maghrib and Isha when combining them at Muzdalifah. The general ruling is that one should not perform any optional prayer between the two, as it disrupts the sunnah of combining them consecutively. If one does perform an optional prayer or becomes engaged in any activity that creates a separation (fasl) between the two obligatory prayers, then the iqamah must be repeated for the second prayer (Isha). Theoretically, the adhan should also be repeated, as is the case when a separation occurs in the first combination (at Arafat between Zuhr and Asr). However, the Hanafi school relies on the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) who, after praying Maghrib, ate a meal and then gave a separate iqamah for Isha without repeating the adhan. Therefore, only the iqamah is repeated. This shows that the sunnah at Muzdalifah differs from that at Arafat in this detail.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu‘): Voluntary or optional prayer (nafl).
فصل (fasl): A separation or interruption between the two combined prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only the adhan
C) Only the iqamah
D) Nothing, the prayers are still valid

Key Takeaway
At Muzdalifah, if a separation occurs between combined prayers, only the iqamah is repeated for the second prayer, based on the Prophet's action.

Congregation Not a Condition for Combining at Muzdalifah
Ruling that congregation is not required for combining at Muzdalifah, with reasoning based on qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa does not require congregation for combining at Muzdalifah and distinguish this from the ruling at Arafat using the principle of conformity to qiyas.

Core Idea
What conforms to qiyas needs no strict textual condition; what contradicts qiyas demands full textual adherence.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a key distinction in the Hanafi school regarding the combination of prayers during Hajj. At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined with Maghrib delayed; at Arafat, Zuhr and Asr are combined with Asr advanced. The ruling on whether congregation is required differs based on the act's conformity to qiyas. Understanding this 'illa helps us see how Hanafi fiqh balances textual prescription and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State Abu Hanifa's position: congregation is not a condition for the combined prayers at Muzdalifah.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
2
Contrast with Arafat
Recognize that at Arafat, congregation IS a condition for combining Zuhr and Asr. The passage contrasts the two.
The difference hinges on whether the prayer is delayed or advanced.
3
Understand the 'Illa
Identify the effective cause: at Muzdalifah, Maghrib is delayed (ta'khir) which is in accordance with qiyas because qada of missed prayers is allowed in general. At Arafat, Asr is advanced (taqdim) which is against qiyas.
Delay conforms to analogy; advancement contradicts it.
4
Apply the Hanafi Principle
Learn the principle: When an act matches qiyas, the strict conditions of the text (like congregation) are not imposed. When an act opposes qiyas, the text's conditions must be followed exactly.
This is a key methodological rule in Hanafi usul.
5
Derive the Practical Consequence
Conclude: at Muzdalifah, a pilgrim may combine Maghrib and Isha individually; at Arafat, congregation is required for the combination to be valid.
The thamarah (practical difference) is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تَشْتَرِطُ الْجَمَاعَةُ لِهَذَا الْجَمْعِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّ الْمَغْرِبَ مُؤَخَّرَةٌ عَنْ وَقْتِهَا بِخِلَافِ الْجَمْعِ بِعَرَفَةَ لِأَنَّ الْعَصْرَ مُقَدَّمٌ عَلَى وَقْتِهَا
ترجمہ: اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس جمع کے لئے جماعت شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ مغرب اپنے وقت سے مؤخر ہے برخلاف عرفہ میں جمع بین الظهر والعصر کے کہ عصر اپنے وقت پر مقدم ہے۔
تشریح: حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مزدلفہ کے اندر مغرب و عشاء کو جمع کرنے کے لئے جماعت شرط نہیں ہے اور عرفات میں جمع بین الظہر و عصر کے لئے جماعت شرط ہے۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مغرب کی نماز مزدلفہ میں اپنے وقت سے مؤخر پڑھی جاتی ہے اور نماز کا وقت نکلنے کے بعد پڑھا جانا قیاس کے موافق ہے۔ کیونکہ قضاء تمام نمازوں میں مشروع ہے پس قیاس کے موافق ہونے کی وجہ سے مورد نص کی رعایت واجب نہیں ہے اور عصر کی نماز عرفات میں چونکہ وقت سے مقدم ادا کی جاتی ہے اور نماز کا وقت سے مقدم ہونا من کل وجہ خلاف قیاس ہے اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس ثابت ہوتی ہے اس میں نص کی پوری پوری رعایت ملحوظ ہوتی ہے۔ اور جمع بین الظهر والعصر میں چونکہ نص جماعت کے ساتھ وارد ہوئی ہے اس لئے اس میں جماعت شرط ہو گی۔
And congregation is not a condition for this combination according to Abu Hanifa, because Maghrib is delayed from its time, unlike the combination at Arafat because Asr is advanced before its time.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage explains Abu Hanifa's view on the condition of congregation (jama‘ah) for the combined prayers at Muzdalifah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, congregation is not a condition for the validity of combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. The reason given is that Maghrib is prayed after its actual time (it is delayed), and praying after the time has expired (qada) is in accordance with analogy (qiyas), because qada of missed prayers is prescribed generally. Therefore, the specific text (nass) regarding combining does not need to be strictly adhered to regarding congregation. In contrast, at Arafat, the combination involves advancing Asr before its time, which is against analogy (khilaf al-qiyas). Since it is contrary to analogy, the textual prescription must be followed exactly, and the text mentions congregation, making it a condition. Thus, at Muzdalifah, an individual may pray the combination alone, but at Arafat, congregation is required for the validity of the combination.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama‘ah): Congregational prayer performed with an imam.
تأخير (ta‘khir): Delaying the prayer from its usual time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is congregation not a condition for combining prayers at Muzdalifah?
A) Because the Prophet did not pray in congregation there
B) Because Maghrib is delayed, which is in accordance with analogy
C) Because it is easier for the pilgrims
D) Because the text does not mention congregation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between combining at Muzdalifah (delay, conforms to qiyas) and Arafat (advance, against qiyas), making congregation a condition only at Arafat.

Maghrib on the Way to Muzdalifah: Valid or Requires Repetition?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Maghrib validity on the way to Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Maghrib prayed on the way to Muzdalifah, identify the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the principle that an obligatory delay (wajib) affects validity.

Core Idea
Praying Maghrib early on the way to Muzdalifah—the Hanafi majority requires repetition before Fajr.

A pilgrim traveling from Arafat to Muzdalifah on the night of Hajj is required to combine Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. But what if he prays Maghrib on the road before reaching there? The Hanafi school is divided: the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rule the prayer invalid and demand a repeat, while Abu Yusuf holds it valid but makruh. This dispute hinges on whether delaying Maghrib to Muzdalifah is wajib or merely sunnah. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
The act is a pilgrim praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah, before reaching the place of combining. The dispute is whether this prayer is valid (tujzi'hu) or not, and what the pilgrim must do.
Note that this applies only to pilgrims on Hajj, not to residents.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the prayer is not valid (la tujzi'hu) and must be repeated before Fajr. Abu Yusuf: it is valid but the pilgrim has done wrong (asa'a) by abandoning the sunnah of delaying.
This is a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Dalil for the Majority
The majority cite the hadith of Usama: the Prophet said 'The prayer is ahead of you' on the road to Muzdalifah. This indicates that delaying is obligatory (wajib) to enable the combination. Praying early violates that wajib.
The hadith is ahad, so its dalala is zanni, but the school still considers it binding.
4
Understand Abu Yusuf's Reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that the prayer was offered in its correct time, so it is valid. Delay is only sunnah, so missing it makes the act makruh but does not invalidate.
Abu Yusuf compares it to praying after Fajr, where repetition is not required.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah)
According to the majority, the pilgrim must repeat Maghrib after reaching Muzdalifah, before Fajr, to achieve the combination. According to Abu Yusuf, no repeat is needed, but the pilgrim is blameworthy.
The mufta bihi position is the majority view: repetition is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ فِي الطَّرِيقِ لَمْ تُجْزِهِ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَيْهِ إِعَادَتُهَا مَا لَمْ يَطْلُعِ الْفَجْرُ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يُجْزِئُهُ وَقَدْ أَسَاءَ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ إِذَا صَلَّى بِعَرَفَاتٍ لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ أَدَّاهَا فِي وَقْتِهَا فَلَا يَجِبُ إِعَادَتُهَا كَمَا بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ إِلَّا أَنَّ التَّأْخِيرَ مِنَ السُّنَةِ فَيَصِيرُ مُسِيئًا بِتَرْكِهِ وَلَهُمَا مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَالَ لِأُسَامَةَ فِي طَرِيقِ الْمُزْدَلِفَةِ الصَّلَاةُ أَمَامَكَ مَعْنَاهُ وَقْتَ الصَّلَاةِ وَهَذَا إِشَارَةُ إِلَى أَنَّ التَّأْخِيرَ وَاجِبٌ وَإِنَّمَا وَجَبَ لِوُجُودِ الْجَمْعِ بَيْنَ الصَّلَاتَيْنِ بِالْمُزْدَلَفَةِ فَكَانَ عَلَيْهِ الْإِعَادَةُ مَا لَمْ يَطْلُعِ الْفَجْرُ لِيَصِيرَ جَامِعًا بَيْنَهُمَا وَإِذَا طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ لَا يُمْكِنُهُ الْجَمْعُ فَسَقَطَتِ الْإِعَادَةُ
ترجمہ: اور جس حاجی نے نماز مغرب راستہ میں پڑھ لی تو ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس کو کافی نہیں ہوتی اور اس پر نماز کا اعادہ واجب ہے جب تک کہ فجر طلوع نہ ہو۔ اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ اس کو کافی ہے مگر اس نے برا کیا۔ اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے جب اس نے عرفات میں مغرب پڑھ لی۔ ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے مغرب کو اپنے وقت میں ادا کیا تو اس کا اعادہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ طلوع فجر کے بعد مگر تا خیر کرنا سنت ہے تو ترک سنت سے برا کرنے والا ہوگا۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل وہ ہے جو روایت کیا گیا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اسامہ سے فرمایا: نماز تمہارے آگے ہے یعنی مزدلفہ میں، اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تاخیر واجب ہے اور یہ واجب اس لئے ہے کہ دونوں نمازوں کو مزدلفہ میں جمع کیا جائے۔ پس اعادہ کرے جب تک فجر طلوع نہ ہو تاکہ دونوں کو جمع کرے اور جب فجر طلوع ہو جائے تو جمع ممکن نہیں تو اعادہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔
And whoever prays Maghrib on the road (to Muzdalifah) — it is not valid for him according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and he must repeat it as long as dawn has not risen. Abu Yusuf said: it suffices him, but he has done wrong. And the same dispute applies if he prays at Arafat. For Abu Yusuf, he performed it in its time, so repetition is not obligatory, as after dawn, except that delay is sunnah, so he becomes wrong by abandoning it. Their evidence is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Usama on the way to Muzdalifah: 'The prayer is ahead of you,' meaning the time of prayer. This indicates that delay is obligatory, and it is obligatory only to achieve the combination of the two prayers at Muzdalifah. So he must repeat as long as dawn has not risen so that he becomes one who combines them. When dawn rises, he cannot combine, so the repetition drops.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a pilgrim who prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah before reaching the designated place for combining. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, such a prayer is not valid (does not suffice), and the pilgrim must repeat Maghrib after arrival at Muzdalifah, as long as the time of Fajr has not yet entered. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the prayer is valid and sufficient, but the pilgrim has done wrong by delaying the sunnah of combining. The same dispute applies if one prays Maghrib at Arafat. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the prayer was offered in its proper time (before the time of Isha), so no repetition is required, just as after Fajr, although delaying was sunnah. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) base their view on a hadith where the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) told Usama that the prayer is ahead, meaning at Muzdalifah. This indicates that delaying Maghrib to Muzdalifah is obligatory (wajib) to enable the combination. If one prays early, the prayer is not valid as a fulfillment of that obligation, and repetition is required before Fajr so that the combination can be achieved. After Fajr, repetition is no longer required because the time for combining has passed.

Key Terms
اعادة (i‘adah): Repeating the prayer to make it valid.
أساء (asa‘a): He did wrong (i.e., committed an act of disapproval).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what must a pilgrim do if he prayed Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) The prayer is valid and no action needed
B) He must repeat Maghrib before Fajr at Muzdalifah
C) He must repeat both Maghrib and Isha
D) He must perform Hajj again

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a pilgrim who prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah must repeat it before Fajr at Muzdalifah, as the delay is wajib to enable the combination of prayers.

Ruling on Maghrib Prayed Before Muzdalifah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity and repetition of Maghrib at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the majority of Hanafi imams require repetition of Maghrib prayed before Muzdalifah and distinguish their position from Abu Yusuf's.

Core Idea
Delaying Maghrib to Muzdalifah is wajib for combining; preemptive prayer is invalid and must be repeated before dawn.

During Hajj, the Prophet ﷺ delayed Maghrib until Muzdalifah and combined it with Isha. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute over a pilgrim who prays Maghrib on the way before reaching Muzdalifah. We will examine the evidence from the hadith of Usama and the reasoning behind the majority view versus Imam Abu Yusuf's alternative position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, Hasan) regarding Maghrib prayed before Muzdalifah. Note the ruling: prayer is invalid (not valid) and must be repeated before dawn.
The term 'tarafayn' (two sides) refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
State Imam Abu Yusuf's position: the prayer is valid but sinful due to abandoning the sunnah of delaying. Understand why he considers it valid (performed in its time).
Abu Yusuf also applies this reasoning to Maghrib prayed at Arafat.
3
Follow the majority's dalil
Recall the hadith of Usama: when asked to pray Maghrib on the way, the Prophet said 'الصلاة أمامك' (the prayer is ahead of you). This indicates that delaying is wajib, not merely sunnah, because the command is for an obligatory delay to enable combining.
The operative phrase is 'أمامك' meaning ahead, pointing to Muzdalifah.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof and the Hanafi response
Abu Yusuf argues via qiyas: any prayer performed in its time is valid and not repeated. The response: the hadith provides a specific command (dalil naqli) that overrides general qiyas. The wisdom (hikma) for the wajib delay is the combining of Maghrib and Isha.
The Hanafi response invokes the principle that a specific textual evidence takes precedence over analogical reasoning.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: under the majority, the pilgrim must repeat Maghrib before dawn; under Abu Yusuf, no repetition but the prayer is valid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view requiring i'adah before dawn.
After dawn, the opportunity to combine is lost, so repetition is dropped even according to the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسامہ بن زید سے مزدلفہ کے راستہ میں فرمایا کہ نماز تیرے آگے ہے۔ اسکی مراد وقت نماز ہے۔ اور یہ اشارہ ہے کہ تاخیر کرنا واجب ہے اور تا خیر اسی وجہ سے واجب ہوئی تاکہ مزدلفہ میں دونوں نمازیں جمع کرنا ممکن ہو ۔ پس جب تک فجر طلوع نہ ہو اس پر مغرب کا اعادہ واجب ہے تا کہ مغرب و عشاء کا جمع کرنے والا ہو جائے اور جب فجر طلوع ہو گئی تو جمع کرنا ممکن نہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے اعادہ ساقط ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاجی نے مغرب کی نماز مزدلفہ سے پہلے ہی راستہ میں ادا کر لی تو طرفین کے نزدیک یہ نماز درست نہ ہوگی بلکہ طلوع فجر سے پہلے پہلے اس پر اس نماز کا اعادہ واجب ہے۔ اسی کے قائل امام زفر اور حسن بن زیادہ ہیں۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ نماز تو درست ہو گئی ہے البتہ مخالفت سنت کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔ یہی اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب مغرب کی نماز عرفات میں ادا کر لی یعنی اس صورت میں بھی طرفین کے نزدیک مغرب درست نہ ہوگی اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک درست ہو جائے گی ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے مغرب کی نماز اس کے وقت میں ادا کی ہے اور جو شخص نماز وقت کے اندر ادا کرے اس پر اعادہ نماز واجب نہیں ہوتا جیسے کہ طلوع فجر کے بعد پڑھنے کی صورت میں اعادہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ اس موقع پر مغرب کو مؤخر کرنا سنت ہے۔ پس ترک سنت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار ضرور ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اسامہ بن زید نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے عرفات سے مزدلفہ جاتے ہوئے راستہ میں فرمایا کہ اللہ کے رسول نماز مغرب پڑھ لیں تو آپ نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ الصلوة امامنگ نماز کا وقت تیرے آگے ہے یعنی مزدلفہ میں اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مغرب کو موخر کرنا واجب ہے اور مغرب کو مؤخر کرنا فقط اس لئے واجب ہوا ہے تا کہ مغرب اور عشاء دونوں نمازوں کو مز دالفہ میں جمع کرنا ممکن ہو۔ پس اس جمع بین الصلاتین کی وجہ سے طلوع فجر سے پہلے پہلے مغرب کے اعادہ کو واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن جب فجر طلوع ہو گئی تو اب دونوں نمازوں کو جمع کرنا ممکن نہ رہا اس لئے طلوع فجر کے بعد اعادہ ساقط ہو گیا۔
Usama ibn Zaid was told on the way to Muzdalifah that prayer is ahead of you. Its meaning is the time of prayer. And this is an indication that delaying is wajib, and the delay became wajib for this reason so that both prayers can be combined at Muzdalifah. So as long as dawn has not risen, repeating Maghrib is wajib so that he becomes one who combines Maghrib and Isha, and when dawn rises, combining is no longer possible, so the repetition is dropped. Explanation of the issue: If a pilgrim performed Maghrib prayer on the way before reaching Muzdalifah, then according to the two sides this prayer is not valid, rather he must repeat it before dawn. Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad hold this opinion. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that the prayer is valid, but he becomes sinful for opposing the sunnah. The same difference occurs if he performed Maghrib at Arafat; in that case too, according to the two sides, Maghrib is not valid, but according to Abu Yusuf it is valid. Abu Yusuf's proof is that this person performed Maghrib in its time, and whoever prays within the time is not obliged to repeat, just as repetition is not wajib after dawn. However, delaying Maghrib at this place is sunnah, so he is sinful for abandoning the sunnah. The proof of the two sides is that Usama ibn Zaid said to the Prophet ﷺ on the way from Arafat to Muzdalifah, 'O Messenger of Allah, pray Maghrib,' and he replied, 'The prayer is ahead of you,' meaning at Muzdalifah. This shows that delaying Maghrib is wajib, and it became wajib only so that both prayers can be combined at Muzdalifah. Due to this combining (jama' bayn al-salatayn), repetition before dawn is made wajib. But when dawn rises, combining is no longer possible, so repetition after dawn is dropped.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a pilgrim who prays Maghrib before arriving at Muzdalifah. The majority view (Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, Imam Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad) holds that such a prayer is invalid and must be repeated before dawn, because the Prophet ﷺ instructed Usama to delay Maghrib until Muzdalifah, making the delay wajib. The wajib delay is to enable combining Maghrib and Isha. If dawn rises, the opportunity to combine is lost, so repetition is no longer required. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the prayer is valid because it was performed in its proper time; however, he considers it sinful to abandon the sunnah of delaying. The passage follows the author's order: first explaining the ruling, then detailing the disagreement, then presenting proofs for each side. The reader should note that this dispute is within the Hanafi school, and the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), requiring repetition before dawn.

Key Terms
طرفین (tarafayn): The two sides: here referring to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
اعادہ (i'adah): Repetition of a prayer due to invalidity or missing a wajib element

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams, what is the ruling if a pilgrim prays Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah?
A) The prayer is valid but he is sinful.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated before dawn.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated after dawn.
D) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.

Key Takeaway
When a specific command indicates wujub, it overrides the general rule of prayer validity, requiring repetition (i'adah) of an early prayer before the designated time.

Performing Fajr in Darkness at Muzdalifah
Ruling with proof for Fajr timing at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for Fajr at Muzdalifah and explain the two proofs (hadith and qiyas) that support it.

Core Idea
Fajr at Muzdalifah is prayed in darkness to accommodate wuquf, following the Prophet's practice.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific hajj-related prayer timing. While Fajr is normally prayed after full dawn (isfar), at Muzdalifah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the Imam leads the congregation in darkness. Understanding this ruling requires examining both the direct prophetic precedent and the legal analogy (qiyas) that links it to the advancing of Asr at Arafat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leading Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah on the Day of Sacrifice. The ruling is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah to pray in darkness (taghlis).
2
Analyze the first proof (hadith)
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud states that the Prophet ﷺ prayed Fajr at Muzdalifah in darkness. This establishes the practice as a prophetic sunnah.
The word 'بِعَلَس' (in darkness) is key.
3
Analyze the second proof (qiyas)
The author draws an analogy to advancing Asr at Arafat. Just as Asr is prayed earlier than its preferred time to accommodate the wuquf, Fajr is prayed earlier (in darkness) to accommodate the wuquf at Muzdalifah.
The illa is the need to fulfill the wuquf.
4
Determine the Hanafi classification
The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, because the evidence (ahad hadith and qiyas) indicates recommendation, not obligation.
The usual time (isfar) is not invalidated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا طَلَعَ الْفَجَرُ يُصَلَّى الْإِمَامُ بِالنَّاسِ الْفَجْرَ يعَلَى لِرِوَايَةِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلاهَا يَوْمَئِذٍ بِعَلَس ولأنَّ فِى التَعْلِيْس دَفَعَ حَاجَةِ الوُقُوفِ فَيَجُوزُ كَتَقْدِيم العصر يعرفة ترجمہ کہا۔ اور جب فجر طلوع ہوگئی تو امام لوگوں کو فجر کی نماز تاریکی میں پڑھائے کیونکہ عبداللہ بن مسعود کی روایت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس روز فجر کی نماز تاریکی میں پڑھی اور اس لئے کہ مفلس میں پڑھنے میں وقوف مزدلفہ کی حاجت پوری ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہ جائز ہے۔ جیسے عرفہ میں عصر کو مقدم مرنا جائز ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، جب یوم نحر کی فجر طلوع ہوگئی تو امام لوگوں کو فجر کی نماز فلس میں پڑھائے دلیل عبداللہ ابن مسعودؓ کی روایت ہے کہ جناب رسول اللہ ا نے آج کے دن فجر کی نماز غلس میں ادا کی ہے۔ دوسر بی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مزدلفہ میں فجر کی نماز کو غلس میں ادا کرنا وقوف مزدلفہ کی ضرورت کے پیش نظر ہے۔ پس جب وقوف عرفہ کی ضرورت کے پیش نظر عصر کو اس کے وقت مباح پر مقدم کرنا جائز ہے تو وقوف مزدلفہ کی وجہ سے فجر کو اس کے وقت معتاد معینی اسفار پر مقدم کرنا بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگا۔
He said: And when dawn breaks, the Imam should lead the people in Fajr prayer in darkness, based on the narration of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet prayed it that day in darkness, and because in praying in darkness the need for wuquf is fulfilled, so it is permissible, just as it is permissible to advance Asr at Arafat. Translation: He said: And when dawn breaks, the Imam leads the people in Fajr prayer in darkness because Abdullah ibn Mas'ud narrated that the Prophet ﷺ performed Fajr on that day in darkness, and because praying in darkness fulfills the need of wuquf at Muzdalifah, so it is permissible, like advancing Asr at Arafat. Explanation: When the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice breaks, the Imam leads Fajr in darkness. The proof is the narration of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet performed Fajr on this day in darkness. The second proof is that performing Fajr in darkness at Muzdalifah serves the need of wuquf. Just as it is permissible to advance Asr from its preferred time due to the need of wuquf at Arafat, it is even more permissible to advance Fajr to darkness due to the need of wuquf at Muzdalifah.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the Fajr prayer on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah) at Muzdalifah is to be performed in darkness (taghlis), meaning early dawn before full daylight. The author provides two proofs: first, the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet ﷺ did so; second, a qiyas (analogy) to the advancement of Asr at Arafat for the sake of wuquf. The commentary explains that performing Fajr early allows pilgrims more time for the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah, which is a wajib act. The qiyas is that just as Asr is prayed earlier than its usual time at Arafat to accommodate wuquf, similarly Fajr is prayed earlier (in darkness) at Muzdalifah. The author uses the principle of 'bilaawla al-maslaha' (priority of benefit) to argue that since wuquf is a pillar/wajib, facilitating it takes precedence. The reader should understand that this ruling applies specifically to the Imam and the congregation at Muzdalifah on that day.

Key Terms
تغلیس (taghlis): Performing the Fajr prayer in the early darkness before full dawn

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah performed in darkness according to the passage?
A) To imitate the Prophet's practice and to accommodate wuquf.
B) Because the time of Fajr is very short.
C) To make the prayer longer.
D) Because it is wajib to pray before dawn.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits and recommends praying Fajr at Muzdalifah in darkness to facilitate the wuquf, based on the Prophet's practice and legal analogy.

Standing and Supplication at Muzdalifah After Fajr
Ruling on standing and supplication at Muzdalifah after Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling of standing and making du'a at Muzdalifah after Fajr, and explain the hadith evidence used by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wuquf at Muzdalifah after Fajr is a sunnah muakkadah; the Prophet's du'a there was accepted even for murderers.

In this passage, Al-Hidayah (via Al-Quduri) describes the recommended practice after Fajr on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The Imam and pilgrims stand at the Mash'ar al-Haram and supplicate, following the Prophet's example. The text cites a powerful hadith from Ibn Abbas to emphasize the virtue of this moment. Even though wuquf at Muzdalifah is wajib, the specific act of standing after Fajr for du'a is a separate sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What is the recommended action after Fajr at Muzdalifah? Standing and supplication.
The text begins with 'Then he stood and the people stood with him, and he supplicated.'
2
State the ruling level
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status? Sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Not wajib, but highly recommended.
3
Locate the dalil
Which evidence is cited? The hadith of Ibn Abbas about the Prophet's accepted supplication.
The text says: 'it was narrated in the hadith of Ibn Abbas: His supplication for his ummah was accepted, even regarding bloodshed and injustices.'
4
Explain the proof
How does the hadith support the ruling? It shows the Prophet performed the act at this place and his du'a was accepted, establishing its virtue.
The prophetic action (fi'l) is a proof for sunnah.
5
Resolve the apparent contradiction
The note mentions the Prophet also supplicated at Arafat for the same sins; how is this reconciled? Acceptance was deferred to Muzdalifah.
This shows the special status of Muzdalifah for du'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ وَقَفَ وَوَقَفَ مَعَهُ النَّاسُ فَدَعَا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَقَفَ فِى هَذَا الْمَوْضِعِ يَدْعُو حَتَّى رُوِيَ فِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عَبَّاس فَاسْتَجِيْب لَهُ دُعَاؤُهُ لامَّتِهِ حَتَّى الدِّمَاءَ وَالْمَظَالِم ترجمہ پھر امام وقوف کرے اور اس کے ساتھ لوگ وقوف کریں اور دعا کرے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس موقع پر قوف کیا اس حال میں کہ دعا کرے تھے حتی کہ ابن عباس کی روایت میں مروی ہے کہ آپ کی دعا آپ کی امت کے حق میں قبول کی گئی حتی کہ خون اور مظالم کے حق میں بھی۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ مزدلفہ پہنچ کر امام جبل قزح کے پاس وقوف کرے۔ اور اس کے ساتھ لوگ بھی وقوف کریں اور امام اور لوگ اس جگہ دعا کریں کیونکہ یہ جگہ دعاؤں کے قبول ہونے کا مقام ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس جنگہ دعا کی اور ابن عباس کی روایت کے مطابق تمام دعائیں قبول کی گئیں حتی کہ ناحق قتل کرنے والے اور ظلم کرنے والے کو معاف کر دینے کے حق میں بھی یعنی قیامت میں اللہ تعالی ناحق مقتول اور مظلوم کو اس قدر نواز دیں گے کہ مقتول اور مظلوم خدا کی ان عنایات کو دیکھ کر اپنے مخصوص کو معاف کردیں گے پس اس وجہ سے قاتل اور ظالم مستحق مغفرت ہو جائیں گے۔ نوٹ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنی امت کے قاتلوں اور ظالموں کے لئے وقوف عرفہ کے موقع پر بھی دعا کی تھی لیکن ان کے حق میں اس وقت قبول نہ ہوئی تھی بلکہ وقوف مزدلفہ کے موقع پر قبول ہوئی۔ لہذا اب یہ اعتراض نہ ہوگا کہ وقوف عرفہ کے وقت ان دونوں کے حق میں قبول نہ ہونا بیان کیا گیا ہے اور یہاں قبول ہونا بیان کیا ہے۔
Then he stood and the people stood with him, and he supplicated because the Prophet ﷺ stood in this place supplicating, until it was narrated in the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'His supplication for his ummah was accepted, even regarding bloodshed and injustices.' Translation: Then the Imam should stand and the people should stand with him, and he should supplicate because the Messenger of Allah ﷺ stood at this place supplicating, until it is narrated in the hadith of Ibn Abbas that his supplication for his ummah was accepted, even regarding blood and injustices. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says: When reaching Muzdalifah, the Imam should stand near Jabal Qazh, and the people should stand with him, and the Imam and people should supplicate in this place because it is a place where supplications are accepted. This is why the Prophet ﷺ supplicated there, and according to the narration of Ibn Abbas, all supplications were accepted, even those regarding the forgiveness of murderers and oppressors. On the Day of Judgment, Allah will grant such rewards to the wrongfully killed and oppressed that they will forgive their murderers and oppressors, thus the latter become deserving of forgiveness. Note: The Prophet had also supplicated for the murderers and oppressors of his ummah during wuquf at Arafat, but it was not accepted then; it was accepted during wuquf at Muzdalifah. So there is no contradiction between the reports.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage describes the sunnah action after Fajr at Muzdalifah. The Imam and all pilgrims should stand (wuquf) at the Mash'ar al-Haram (the sacred monument) near Jabal Qazh and engage in supplication, following the example of the Prophet ﷺ. The passage cites a hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet's supplication was accepted, even for major sins like murder and oppression, indicating the great virtue of this place. The commentary explains the recompense on Judgment Day will lead to mutual forgiveness. A note resolves a potential objection: the Prophet had also supplicated at Arafat for these sinners, but acceptance came only at Muzdalifah, so there is no inconsistency. This ruling is based on explicit prophetic action and is considered a sunnah mu'akkadah of Hajj.

Key Terms
وقوف (wuquf): Standing at a sacred place during Hajj, here at Muzdalifah after Fajr
مشعر حرام (mash'ar al-haram): The sacred monument at Muzdalifah, specifically the area near Jabal Qazh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Leave immediately for Mina.
B) Stand and make supplication at the sacred monument.
C) Perform Tawaf.
D) Stone the Jamarat.

Key Takeaway
Standing and supplicating at Muzdalifah after Fajr is a confirmed sunnah based on the Prophet's practice and the promise of accepted du'a.

Legal Status of Wuquf at Muzdalifah: Wajib vs Rukn
Inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on wuquf Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies wuquf at Muzdalifah as wajib and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
Wuquf at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn — omitting it requires a dam but your Hajj is still valid.

The status of wuquf at Muzdalifah is a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While both agree it is essential, they diverge on whether its omission invalidates the Hajj or can be compensated. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: wuquf at Muzdalifah is wajib, not a rukn. If omitted without excuse, a dam is required but the Hajj remains valid.
This is the central claim.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i considers it a rukn, meaning omission invalidates the Hajj entirely.
The opposing school is clearly specified.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: Quran 2:198, 'And remember Allah at the Sacred Monument.' They interpret the imperative as establishing rukniyyah.
Understand how a command is used to claim pillar status.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Review the Hanafi rebuttals: (a) the Prophet sent the weak ahead by night, which would not be done if it were a rukn; (b) the verse mentions dhikr, not wuquf, and dhikr is not a rukn by consensus; (c) the hadith linking 'completion' to wuquf indicates wujub, not rukniyyah.
Note the use of prophetic practice (fi'l) and consensus (ijma').
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a pilgrim omits wuquf at Muzdalifah without excuse, the Hanafi ruling is dam + valid Hajj; the Shafi'i ruling is invalid Hajj.
This highlights the real-world impact of the legal classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوف مزدلفہ کی شرعی حیثیت ثُمَّ هَذَا الْوُقُوفُ وَاجِبٌ عِندَنَا وَلَيْسَ بِرُكن حَتَّى لَوْتَرَكَهُ بِغَيْرِ عُدْرِ يَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ إِنَّهُ رُكُن لِقَوْلِ، تَعَالَى فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ وَبِمَثَلِهِ يَنْبُتُ الرَّكْنَيَّةُ وَلَنَا مَارُويَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَدَمَ ضَعْفَةَ أَهْلِهِ ، بِاللَّيْلِ وَلَوْ كَانَ رُكُنَّا لَمَا فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ وَالْمَذْكُورُ فِيمَا تَلَا الذَّكَرَ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِرَّكُن بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَإِنَّمَا عَرَّفْنَا الوُجُوبَ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ وَقَفَ مَعَنَا هَذَا الْمُوقَفَ وَقَدْ كَانَ أفَاضَ قَبْلَ ذلِكَ مِنْ عَرَفَاتِ فَقَدَ تَمَّ حَجه عَلَقَ بِه تَمَامَ الْحَجِّ وَهذَا يَصْلُحُ أَمَارَةَ لِلْوُجُوبِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا تَرَكَهُ بِعُذرِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ بِهِ ضُعَفْ أَوَعِلَّةً أَو كَانَتْ امْرَأَةٌ تَخَافَ الرِّحَامَ لَا شَى عَلَيْهِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا
The Legal Status of Wuquf at Muzdalifah. Then this wuquf is wajib according to us and is not a rukn, such that if one leaves it without excuse, dam becomes obligatory. And al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn because of His statement: 'Remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (2:198). And by a command like this, rukniyyah is established. Our proof is what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) sent ahead the weak among his people by night; and if it had been a rukn, he would not have done that. And what is mentioned in the recited verse is dhikr, and that is not a rukn by consensus. We only established the wujub by his statement: 'Whoever stands with us at this standing place and had already departed from Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' This dependence on completion is an indication of wujub. However, if he leaves it with an excuse, such as being weak or ill, or a woman who fears crowding, nothing is upon him due to what we narrated.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal status of wuquf at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi position is that it is wajib, not rukn. If omitted without excuse, a dam (sacrifice) is required, but the Hajj remains valid. Imam al-Shafi'i argues it is a rukn, citing the Quranic verse commanding dhikr at the Mash'ar al-Haram, which he interprets as a pillar. The Hanafi response uses several proofs: (1) The Prophet sent the weak ahead at night, which would not be permissible if wuquf were a rukn (since a rukn cannot be omitted). (2) The verse mentions dhikr, not wuquf, and dhikr is not a rukn by consensus. (3) The hadith 'whoever stands with us at this standing place... his Hajj is complete' indicates completion, which is an attribute of wujub, not rukn. Additionally, if there is a valid excuse (weakness, illness, fear of crowding), no dam is required. This distinction highlights the Hanafi methodology of differentiating between rukn (core pillar) and wajib (essential but compensable obligation).

Key Terms
رکن (rukn): An integral pillar of Hajj; omission invalidates the Hajj
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (goat or sheep) required as compensation for omitting a wajib act in Hajj
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission requires compensation (e.g., dam) but does not invalidate the act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required if a pilgrim omits wuquf at Muzdalifah without an excuse?
A) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) A dam (sacrifice) is required, but the Hajj is valid.
C) Nothing is required because it is optional.
D) He must perform a make-up Hajj next year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of wuquf at Muzdalifah as wajib (not rukn) means that its omission can be compensated with a dam, preserving the validity of the Hajj.

The Hanafi Ruling on Wuquf Muzdalifah: Wajib with Dam for Omission
Defines the Hanafi ruling on wuquf Muzdalifah and its evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wuquf Muzdalifah, identify the dalil, and explain the consequence of omission with and without excuse.

Core Idea
Wuquf Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn; leaving it without excuse requires dam, but with excuse no penalty.

The standing at Muzdalifah is a key rite of Hajj. While all schools agree on its importance, the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib, a level between sunnah and rukn. Understanding this distinction affects the validity of the Hajj and the penalties involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wuquf (standing) at Muzdalifah. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory), not rukn (pillar).
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi evidence comes from two hadiths: (1) the Prophet sent weak family members ahead at night without requiring them to stand, and (2) the Prophet said, 'Whoever stands with us at this standing and has left Arafat, his Hajj is complete.'
The full Arabic is provided in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith shows that wuquf Muzdalifah can be omitted with excuse, which would not be possible if it were a rukn. The second hadith links completion of Hajj to this standing, indicating obligation (wujub), not pillar (rukn).
A rukn is never excused; a wajib can be excused with penalty.
4
Note the conditions for the ruling
If a pilgrim leaves wuquf Muzdalifah without a valid excuse (e.g., weakness, illness, fear of crowding for women), dam becomes obligatory. If there is a valid excuse, no penalty is incurred.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
A healthy adult who skips this standing must offer a sheep. A weak or sick person who skips it does not need to offer anything and the Hajj is still valid.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
