نماز فجر کے بعد امام اور لوگ وقوف اور دعا کریں
کتاب الحج
ثُمَّ وَقَفَ وَوَقَفَ مَعَهُ النَّاسُ فَدَعَا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَقَفَ فِى هَذَا الْمَوْضِعِ يَدْعُو حَتَّى رُوِيَ فِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عَبَّاس فَاسْتَجِيْب لَهُ دُعَاؤُهُ لامَّتِهِ حَتَّى الدِّمَاءَ وَالْمَظَالِم
ترجمہ پھر امام وقوف کرے اور اس کے ساتھ لوگ وقوف کریں اور دعا کرے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس موقع پر وقوف کیا اس حال میں کہ دعا کرے تھے حتی کہ ابن عباس کی روایت میں مروی ہے کہ آپ کی دعا آپ کی امت کے حق میں قبول کی گئی حتی کہ خون اور مظالم
کے حق میں بھی۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ مزدلفہ پہنچ کر امام جبل قزح کے پاس وقوف کرے۔ اور اس کے ساتھ لوگ بھی وقوف کریں اور امام اور لوگ اس جگہ دعا کریں کیونکہ یہ جگہ دعاؤں کے قبول ہونے کا مقام ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس جنگہ دعا کی اور ابن عباس کی روایت کے مطابق تمام دعائیں قبول کی گئیں حتی کہ ناحق قتل کرنے والے اور ظلم کرنے والے کو معاف کر دینے کے حق میں بھی یعنی قیامت میں اللہ تعالی ناحق مقتول اور مظلوم کو اس قدر نواز دیں گے کہ مقتول اور مظلوم خدا کی ان عنایات کو دیکھ کر اپنے مخصوص کو معاف کردیں گے پس اس وجہ سے قاتل اور ظالم مستحق مغفرت ہو جائیں گے۔
نوٹ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنی امت کے قاتلوں اور ظالموں کے لئے وقوف عرفہ کے موقع پر بھی دعا کی تھی لیکن ان کے حق میں اس وقت قبول نہ ہوئی تھی بلکہ وقوف مزدلفہ کے موقع پر قبول ہوئی۔ لہذا اب یہ اعتراض نہ ہوگا کہ وقوف عرفہ کے وقت ان دونوں کے حق میں قبول نہ ہونا بیان کیا گیا ہے اور یہاں قبول ہونا بیان کیا ہے۔
وقوف مزدلفہ کی شرعی حیثیت
ثُمَّ هَذَا الْوُقُوفُ وَاجِبٌ عِندَنَا وَلَيْسَ بِرُكن حَتَّى لَوْتَرَكَهُ بِغَيْرِ عُدْرِ يَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ إِنَّهُ رُكُن لِقَوْلِ، تَعَالَى فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ وَبِمَثَلِهِ يَنْبُتُ الرَّكْنَيَّةُ وَلَنَا مَارُويَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَدَّمَ ضَعَفَةَ أَهْلِهِ، بِاللَّيْلِ وَلَوْ كَانَ رُكُنَّا لَمَا فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ وَالْمَذْكُورُ فِيمَا تَلَا الذَّكَرَ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِرَّكُن بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَإِنَّمَا عَرَّفْنَا الوُجُوبَ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ وَقَفَ مَعَنَا هَذَا الْمُوقَفَ وَقَدْ كَانَ أفَاضَ قَبْلَ ذلِكَ مِنْ عَرَفَاتِ فَقَدَ تَمَّ حَجه عَلَقَ بِه تَمَامَ الْحَجِّ وَهذَا يَصْلِحُ أَمَارَةَ لِلْوُجُوبِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا تَرَكَهُ بِعُذرِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ بِهِ ضُعَفْ أَوَعِلَّةً أَو كَانَتْ امْرَأَةٌ تَخَافَ الرِّحَامَ لَا شَى عَلَيْهِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا
ترجمہ پھر یہ وقوف ہمارے نزدیک واجب ہے اور رکن نہیں ہے حتی کہ اگر حاجی نے اس کو بغیر عذر ترک کیا تو اس پر دم لازم ہو گا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ رکن ہے کیونکہ باری تعالی نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب تم عرفات سے پھرو تو مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ تعالی کا ذکر کرو اور ایسے حکم سے رکن ہونا ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے اہل میں سے ضعیفوں کو رات میں پہلے بھیج دیا۔ اور اگر وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہوتا تو ایسا نہ کرتے اور جو آیت تلاوت کی اس میں تو ذکر مذکور ہے اور وہ بالا جماع رکن نہیں ہے اور ہم نے وقوف

کتاب الحج
۳۵۰
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
مزدلفہ کا واجب ہونا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے (اس) قول سے پہچانا کہ جس نے ہمارے ساتھ اس موقف میں وقوف کیا حالانکہ اس سے پہلے عرفات سے ہو آیا ہے تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تمام حج کو وقوف مزدلفہ پر متعلق کیا ہے۔ اور یہ واجب ہونے کی علامت ہونے کے لائق ہے سوائے اس کے کہ جب حاجی نے اس کو عذر کے ساتھ چھوڑا بایں طور کہ اس میں ضعف ہو یا بیماری ہو یا وہ عورت ہو جو از دحام سے ڈرتی ہے تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک وقوف مزدلفہ واجب ہے نہ کہ رکن ۔ چنانچہ اگر بلا عذر وقوف مزدلفہ ترک کر دیا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نہایہ کے حوالہ سے تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ اس قول کی نسبت امام شافعی کی جانب کا تب کا سہو ہے کیونکہ کتب شوافع میں مذکور ہے کہ وقوف مزدلفہ سنت ہے۔ مبسوط میں امام شافعی کے بجائے لیث بن سعد کا نام مذکور ہے اور کتاب اسرار میں امام شافعی کی جگہ علقمہ کا نام مذکور ہے۔ اور فتاوی قاضی خاں میں امام شافعی کی جگہ امام مالک کا ذکر ہے۔ بہر حال صاحب ہدایہ نے اس قول کو امام شافعی کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے اگر چہ غلط ہے۔ اس کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُمْ مِنْ عَرَفَتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ (البقرة: ۱۹۸) ہے یعنی جب تم عرفات سے لوٹو تو مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ کا ذخر کرو۔ اور مشعر حرام مزدلفہ میں ہے پس مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ کا ذکر اسی وقت ممکن ہو گا جبکہ حاجی مزدلفہ میں حاضر ہو کر مشعر حرام کے پاس وقوف کرے۔ اور آیت کی وجہ سے ذکر اللہ کا رکن ہونا ثابت ہے اور یہ موقوف ہے و قوف مزدلفہ پر اور قاعدہ ہے کہ رکن کا موقوف علیہ بھی رکن ہوتا ہے اس لئے وقوف مزدلفہ بھی رکن ہو گا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے اہل خانہ میں سے کمزوروں کو رات میں پہلے ہی بھیج دیا یعنی بغیر وقوف مزدلفہ کئے منی میں بھیج دیا اور یہ حکم کیا کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی نہ کریں۔ یہاں تک کہ آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے ۔ اگر وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہوتا تو آپ ایسا نہ کرتے یعنی ضعفاء کو آگے بھیجنے کا عمل نہ فرماتے ۔ کیونکہ رکن کو عذر کے ساتھ چھوڑنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت میں ذکر مذکور ہے اور ذکر بالا جماع رکن نہیں ہے ۔ ہیں جس پر ذکر موقوف ہے یعنی وقوف مزدلفہ بھی رکن نہ ہوگا۔ اور وقوف مزدلفہ کا واجب ہو نا حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ حضور نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے ہمارے ساتھ مزدلفہ میں وقوف کیا حالانکہ وہ اس سے پہلے عرفات میں ہو آیا ہے تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا۔ اس حدیث میں کمال حج اور تمام حج کو وقوف مزدلفہ پر معلق کیا ہے اور معلق کرنا وجب کی علامت ہے۔ اس لئے مزدلفہ میں وقوف واجب ہے ہاں اگر عذر کی وجہ سے وقوف مزدلفہ چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر دم وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ حدیث قَدَّمَ ضَعَفَةَ اهْلِهِ الخ میں مذکور ہے ۔ عذر کی مثال حاجی کا کمزور ہونا، بیمار ہونا یا عورت کا بھیٹر بھاڑ سے ڈرنا وغیرہ ہے۔ وادی محسر وقوف مزدلفہ میں داخل نہیں
قَالَ وَالْمُرْدَلَفَةُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقَفٌ الْاوَادِي مُحَسَّرِ لِمَارَوَيْنَا مِنْ قَبْلُ
ترجمہ کہا اور مزدلفہ پورے کا پورا وقوف کرنے کی جگہ ہے علاو ہوادی محسر کے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم پہلے روایت کر چکے۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
Then he stood and the people stood with him and he supplicated because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood in this place supplicating until it was narrated in the hadith of Ibn Abbas that his supplication was answered for his community even for bloods and injustices. Translation: Then the Imam should stand and the people should stand with him and supplicate because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stood at this place while supplicating, until it is narrated in the hadith of Ibn Abbas that his supplication was accepted for his community even for bloods and injustices. Commentary: Sahib Quduri said: When reaching Muzdalifah, the Imam should stand near Jabal Qazh and the people should stand with him, and the Imam and the people should supplicate at this place because it is a place of acceptance of supplications. This is why the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) supplicated there, and according to the hadith of Ibn Abbas, all supplications were accepted even for the forgiveness of the unjust killer and the oppressor, meaning that on the Day of Judgment, Allah will reward the wrongly killed and oppressed so greatly that they will forgive their opponents, thus the killer and oppressor become deserving of forgiveness. Note: The Prophet (peace be upon him) also supplicated for the killers and oppressors of his community at the standing of Arafah, but it was not accepted then; it was accepted at the standing of Muzdalifah. So there is no contradiction. The legal status of standing at Muzdalifah: Then this standing is wajib according to us and not a rukn, so that if one leaves it without excuse, dam becomes obligatory. And al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn because of the saying of Allah: 'So when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' and by such a command the rukniyyah is established. And our evidence is the narration that he (peace be upon him) sent the weak of his family at night, and if it were a rukn he would not have done that. And what is mentioned in the recited verse is remembrance (dhikr), and that is not a rukn by consensus. And we know the obligation by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever stands with us at this standing and has already departed from Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' He attached the completion of Hajj to it, and this is suitable as an indication of obligation. Except that if one leaves it with an excuse, such as being weak or ill, or a woman who fears crowding, then nothing is upon him, because of what we have narrated. Translation: Then this standing is wajib according to us and not a rukn, so that if a pilgrim leaves it without excuse, dam becomes obligatory upon him. And Imam al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn because Allah says: 'So when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' and such a command establishes rukniyyah. And our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent the weak ones among his family at night, and if it were a rukn he would not have done that. And the verse recited mentions remembrance, and that is not a rukn by consensus. And we know the obligation of standing at Muzdalifah from the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever stands with us at this standing while having already left Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' The Prophet attached the entire Hajj to standing at Muzdalifah. And this is fit to be a sign of obligation. Except that if the pilgrim leaves it with an excuse, such as being weak or ill, or a woman who fears crowding, then nothing is obligatory upon him, due to the hadith we narrated. Commentary: Sahib Quduri said that according to us, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn. Therefore, if one leaves it without excuse, dam becomes obligatory. And Imam al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn. Sahib Inayah writes with reference to Nihayah that attributing this statement to Imam al-Shafi'i is likely a mistake, because in Shafi'i books it is mentioned that standing at Muzdalifah is sunnah. In Mabsut, instead of Imam al-Shafi'i, the name of Laith ibn Sa'd is mentioned; in Kitab al-Asrar, instead of Imam al-Shafi'i, the name of 'Alqamah is mentioned; and in Fatawa Qadi Khan, instead of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik is mentioned. Nevertheless, Sahib Hidayah attributed this saying to Imam al-Shafi'i, although it is incorrect. His evidence is the verse: 'So when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (Al-Baqarah: 198). That is, when you return from Arafat, remember Allah near the Sacred Monument. And the Sacred Monument is in Muzdalifah, so remembrance of Allah near the Sacred Monument is only possible when the pilgrim is present in Muzdalifah and stands near the Sacred Monument. And by the verse, the remembrance of Allah is established as a rukn, and it depends on standing at Muzdalifah, and the rule is that that on which a rukn depends is also a rukn, therefore standing at Muzdalifah is also a rukn. Our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent the weak ones of his family ahead at night, i.e., he sent them to Mina without standing at Muzdalifah and instructed them not to stone the Jamrat al-Aqabah until sunrise. If standing at Muzdalifah were a rukn, he would not have done that, i.e., he would not have sent the weak ahead, because leaving a rukn even with excuse is not permissible. And the response to Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that the verse mentions remembrance, and remembrance is not a rukn by consensus. So that on which remembrance depends (i.e., standing at Muzdalifah) is also not a rukn. And the obligation of standing at Muzdalifah is established by the hadith. The Prophet said: 'Whoever stands with us in Muzdalifah while having already been in Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' In this hadith, the completeness and perfection of Hajj are linked to standing at Muzdalifah, and linking is a sign of obligation. Therefore, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib. Yes, if one leaves standing at Muzdalifah due to an excuse, then no dam or anything is obligatory upon him, as mentioned in the hadith 'he sent the weak of his family.' Examples of excuse are the pilgrim being weak, ill, or a woman fearing crowding, etc. And the valley of Muhassir is not included in the standing of Muzdalifah. He said: And all of Muzdalifah is a place of standing except the valley of Muhassir, due to what we have narrated previously. Translation: He said: And all of Muzdalifah is a place of standing except the valley of Muhassir, due to the hadith we narrated earlier. Commentary: It is clear.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the legal status of wuquf (standing) at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The text begins by describing the practice: after Fajr prayer, the Imam and the people stand at Muzdalifah and make supplications, following the example of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary emphasizes the virtue of this place for acceptance of du'a, even for the forgiveness of killers and oppressors, as per the hadith of Ibn Abbas. The core legal discussion then follows: The author states that according to the Hanafi school, wuquf Muzdalifah is wajib (obligatory), not a rukn (pillar). If a pilgrim deliberately omits it without a valid excuse, he must offer a dam (sacrificial animal) as penalty. The Hanafi view is contrasted with an attributed opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i that it is a rukn. The commentary (from Ashraf al-Hidaya) notes that this attribution to Imam al-Shafi'i is likely mistaken; some sources attribute it to Laith ibn Sa'd, 'Alqamah, or Imam Malik. The Shafi'i proof cited is the Quranic verse (2:198) commanding remembrance of Allah at the Sacred Monument (Mash'ar al-Haram, i.e., Muzdalifah). The argument is that if remembrance is a rukn, then the standing upon which it depends must also be a rukn. The Hanafi response has two parts: First, the verse only commands dhikr (remembrance), and dhikr is not a rukn by consensus; the standing is merely a means, not an integral. Second, the Prophet's action of sending the weak members of his family ahead at night (without requiring them to stand at Muzdalifah) proves that it cannot be a rukn, because a rukn cannot be omitted even with excuse. The Hanafi proof for wujub is the hadith: 'Whoever stands with us at this standing after having come from Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' Attaching the completion of Hajj to this act indicates obligation (wajib) rather than pillar (rukn). However, if there is a valid excuse (weakness, illness, or a woman's fear of crowding), no penalty is incurred, as shown by the same hadith. The passage ends with a note that the entire plain of Muzdalifah is a place for standing except the valley of Muhassir, based on an earlier narration.

Key Terms
وقوف (wuquf): The act of standing at a specific place during Hajj, particularly at Arafat and Muzdalifah.
مشعر حرام (Mash'ar al-Haram): The Sacred Monument, located in Muzdalifah, where pilgrims are commanded to remember Allah after departing from Arafat.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) required as a penalty for omitting a wajib act during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required of a pilgrim who deliberately skips wuquf Muzdalifah without a valid excuse?
A) His Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) He must offer a dam (sacrificial animal).
C) He must perform an additional circumambulation (tawaf).
D) Nothing is required; the Hajj is still complete.

Key Takeaway
Wuquf Muzdalifah is wajib in the Hanafi school; omission without excuse requires dam, but with excuse no penalty.

Analysis of the inter-madhhab dispute on wuquf Muzdalifah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and opposing views on wuquf Muzdalifah, evaluate the proofs on both sides, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds wuquf Muzdalifah as wajib; the opposing view (attributed to Shafi'i) considers it a rukn – the practical difference is whether missing it invalidates Hajj or only requires a sacrifice.

The legal status of wuquf Muzdalifah is a point of contention between the Hanafi and some other scholars. This lesson dissects the arguments, noting that the attribution to Imam al-Shafi'i may be mistaken, and demonstrates how the Hanafi school refutes the opposing proof.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that wuquf Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn. If omitted without excuse, dam is required; with excuse, nothing.
This is based on the text: 'ثُمَّ هَذَا الْوُقُوفُ وَاجِبٌ عِندَنَا وَلَيْسَ بِرُكن'.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The text attributes to Imam al-Shafi'i the view that it is a rukn, citing Quran 2:198: 'So when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument.' The argument: if remembrance is a rukn, then the standing it depends on must also be a rukn.
The commentary notes this attribution is likely incorrect; other sources attribute it to Laith ibn Sa'd, 'Alqamah, or Malik.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The verse commands only dhikr, which is not a rukn by consensus; standing is a means, not an integral. (2) The Prophet sent weak family members ahead without standing, which would not be permissible if it were a rukn.
The second argument is stronger: a rukn cannot be omitted even with excuse.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If wuquf Muzdalifah is a rukn, missing it invalidates the Hajj. If it is wajib, the Hajj is valid but a dam is required (without excuse).
This difference affects fatwa and practice.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is upheld in the Hidayah and its commentaries. The text considers the opposing view weak due to the Prophet's action.
The tarjih authority is Al-Marghinani (author of Hidayah) and the subsequent commentators.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
۳۴۹
نماز فجر کے بعد امام اور لوگ وقوف اور دعا کریں
کتاب الحج
ثُمَّ وَقَفَ وَوَقَفَ مَعَهُ النَّاسُ فَدَعَا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَقَفَ فِى هَذَا الْمَوْضِعِ يَدْعُو حَتَّى رُوِيَ فِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عَبَّاس فَاسْتَجِيْب لَهُ دُعَاؤُهُ لامَّتِهِ حَتَّى الدِّمَاءَ وَالْمَظَالِم
ترجمہ پھر امام وقوف کرے اور اس کے ساتھ لوگ وقوف کریں اور دعا کرے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس موقع پر وقوف کیا اس حال میں کہ دعا کرے تھے حتی کہ ابن عباس کی روایت میں مروی ہے کہ آپ کی دعا آپ کی امت کے حق میں قبول کی گئی حتی کہ خون اور مظالم
کے حق میں بھی۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ مزدلفہ پہنچ کر امام جبل قزح کے پاس وقوف کرے۔ اور اس کے ساتھ لوگ بھی وقوف کریں اور امام اور لوگ اس جگہ دعا کریں کیونکہ یہ جگہ دعاؤں کے قبول ہونے کا مقام ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس جنگہ دعا کی اور ابن عباس کی روایت کے مطابق تمام دعائیں قبول کی گئیں حتی کہ ناحق قتل کرنے والے اور ظلم کرنے والے کو معاف کر دینے کے حق میں بھی یعنی قیامت میں اللہ تعالی ناحق مقتول اور مظلوم کو اس قدر نواز دیں گے کہ مقتول اور مظلوم خدا کی ان عنایات کو دیکھ کر اپنے مخصوص کو معاف کردیں گے پس اس وجہ سے قاتل اور ظالم مستحق مغفرت ہو جائیں گے۔
نوٹ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنی امت کے قاتلوں اور ظالموں کے لئے وقوف عرفہ کے موقع پر بھی دعا کی تھی لیکن ان کے حق میں اس وقت قبول نہ ہوئی تھی بلکہ وقوف مزدلفہ کے موقع پر قبول ہوئی۔ لہذا اب یہ اعتراض نہ ہوگا کہ وقوف عرفہ کے وقت ان دونوں کے حق میں قبول نہ ہونا بیان کیا گیا ہے اور یہاں قبول ہونا بیان کیا ہے۔
وقوف مزدلفہ کی شرعی حیثیت
ثُمَّ هَذَا الْوُقُوفُ وَاجِبٌ عِندَنَا وَلَيْسَ بِرُكن حَتَّى لَوْتَرَكَهُ بِغَيْرِ عُدْرِ يَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ إِنَّهُ رُكُن لِقَوْلِ، تَعَالَى فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ وَبِمَثَلِهِ يَنْبُتُ الرَّكْنَيَّةُ وَلَنَا مَارُويَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَدَّمَ ضَعَفَةَ أَهْلِهِ، بِاللَّيْلِ وَلَوْ كَانَ رُكُنَّا لَمَا فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ وَالْمَذْكُورُ فِيمَا تَلَا الذَّكَرَ وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِرَّكُن بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَإِنَّمَا عَرَّفْنَا الوُجُوبَ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ وَقَفَ مَعَنَا هَذَا الْمُوقَفَ وَقَدْ كَانَ أفَاضَ قَبْلَ ذلِكَ مِنْ عَرَفَاتِ فَقَدَ تَمَّ حَجه عَلَقَ بِه تَمَامَ الْحَجِّ وَهذَا يَصْلِحُ أَمَارَةَ لِلْوُجُوبِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا تَرَكَهُ بِعُذرِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ بِهِ ضُعَفْ أَوَعِلَّةً أَو كَانَتْ امْرَأَةٌ تَخَافَ الرِّحَامَ لَا شَى عَلَيْهِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا
ترجمہ پھر یہ وقوف ہمارے نزدیک واجب ہے اور رکن نہیں ہے حتی کہ اگر حاجی نے اس کو بغیر عذر ترک کیا تو اس پر دم لازم ہو گا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ رکن ہے کیونکہ باری تعالی نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب تم عرفات سے پھرو تو مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ تعالی کا ذکر کرو اور ایسے حکم سے رکن ہونا ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے اہل میں سے ضعیفوں کو رات میں پہلے بھیج دیا۔ اور اگر وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہوتا تو ایسا نہ کرتے اور جو آیت تلاوت کی اس میں تو ذکر مذکور ہے اور وہ بالا جماع رکن نہیں ہے اور ہم نے وقوف

کتاب الحج
۳۵۰
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
مزدلفہ کا واجب ہونا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے (اس) قول سے پہچانا کہ جس نے ہمارے ساتھ اس موقف میں وقوف کیا حالانکہ اس سے پہلے عرفات سے ہو آیا ہے تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تمام حج کو وقوف مزدلفہ پر متعلق کیا ہے۔ اور یہ واجب ہونے کی علامت ہونے کے لائق ہے سوائے اس کے کہ جب حاجی نے اس کو عذر کے ساتھ چھوڑا بایں طور کہ اس میں ضعف ہو یا بیماری ہو یا وہ عورت ہو جو از دحام سے ڈرتی ہے تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک وقوف مزدلفہ واجب ہے نہ کہ رکن ۔ چنانچہ اگر بلا عذر وقوف مزدلفہ ترک کر دیا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نہایہ کے حوالہ سے تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ اس قول کی نسبت امام شافعی کی جانب کا تب کا سہو ہے کیونکہ کتب شوافع میں مذکور ہے کہ وقوف مزدلفہ سنت ہے۔ مبسوط میں امام شافعی کے بجائے لیث بن سعد کا نام مذکور ہے اور کتاب اسرار میں امام شافعی کی جگہ علقمہ کا نام مذکور ہے۔ اور فتاوی قاضی خاں میں امام شافعی کی جگہ امام مالک کا ذکر ہے۔ بہر حال صاحب ہدایہ نے اس قول کو امام شافعی کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے اگر چہ غلط ہے۔ اس کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُمْ مِنْ عَرَفَتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ (البقرة: ۱۹۸) ہے یعنی جب تم عرفات سے لوٹو تو مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ کا ذخر کرو۔ اور مشعر حرام مزدلفہ میں ہے پس مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ کا ذکر اسی وقت ممکن ہو گا جبکہ حاجی مزدلفہ میں حاضر ہو کر مشعر حرام کے پاس وقوف کرے۔ اور آیت کی وجہ سے ذکر اللہ کا رکن ہونا ثابت ہے اور یہ موقوف ہے و قوف مزدلفہ پر اور قاعدہ ہے کہ رکن کا موقوف علیہ بھی رکن ہوتا ہے اس لئے وقوف مزدلفہ بھی رکن ہو گا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے اہل خانہ میں سے کمزوروں کو رات میں پہلے ہی بھیج دیا یعنی بغیر وقوف مزدلفہ کئے منی میں بھیج دیا اور یہ حکم کیا کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی نہ کریں۔ یہاں تک کہ آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے ۔ اگر وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہوتا تو آپ ایسا نہ کرتے یعنی ضعفاء کو آگے بھیجنے کا عمل نہ فرماتے ۔ کیونکہ رکن کو عذر کے ساتھ چھوڑنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت میں ذکر مذکور ہے اور ذکر بالا جماع رکن نہیں ہے ۔ ہیں جس پر ذکر موقوف ہے یعنی وقوف مزدلفہ بھی رکن نہ ہوگا۔ اور وقوف مزدلفہ کا واجب ہو نا حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ حضور نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے ہمارے ساتھ مزدلفہ میں وقوف کیا حالانکہ وہ اس سے پہلے عرفات میں ہو آیا ہے تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا۔ اس حدیث میں کمال حج اور تمام حج کو وقوف مزدلفہ پر معلق کیا ہے اور معلق کرنا وجب کی علامت ہے۔ اس لئے مزدلفہ میں وقوف واجب ہے ہاں اگر عذر کی وجہ سے وقوف مزدلفہ چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر دم وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ حدیث قَدَّمَ ضَعَفَةَ اهْلِهِ الخ میں مذکور ہے ۔ عذر کی مثال حاجی کا کمزور ہونا، بیمار ہونا یا عورت کا بھیٹر بھاڑ سے ڈرنا وغیرہ ہے۔ وادی محسر وقوف مزدلفہ میں داخل نہیں
قَالَ وَالْمُرْدَلَفَةُ كُلُّهَا مَوْقَفٌ الْاوَادِي مُحَسَّرِ لِمَارَوَيْنَا مِنْ قَبْلُ
ترجمہ کہا اور مزدلفہ پورے کا پورا وقوف کرنے کی جگہ ہے علاو ہوادی محسر کے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم پہلے روایت کر چکے۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
Then he stood and the people stood with him and he supplicated because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood in this place supplicating until it was narrated in the hadith of Ibn Abbas that his supplication was answered for his community even for bloods and injustices. Translation: Then the Imam should stand and the people should stand with him and supplicate because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stood at this place while supplicating, until it is narrated in the hadith of Ibn Abbas that his supplication was accepted for his community even for bloods and injustices. Commentary: Sahib Quduri said: When reaching Muzdalifah, the Imam should stand near Jabal Qazh and the people should stand with him, and the Imam and the people should supplicate at this place because it is a place of acceptance of supplications. This is why the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) supplicated there, and according to the hadith of Ibn Abbas, all supplications were accepted even for the forgiveness of the unjust killer and the oppressor, meaning that on the Day of Judgment, Allah will reward the wrongly killed and oppressed so greatly that they will forgive their opponents, thus the killer and oppressor become deserving of forgiveness. Note: The Prophet (peace be upon him) also supplicated for the killers and oppressors of his community at the standing of Arafah, but it was not accepted then; it was accepted at the standing of Muzdalifah. So there is no contradiction. The legal status of standing at Muzdalifah: Then this standing is wajib according to us and not a rukn, so that if one leaves it without excuse, dam becomes obligatory. And al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn because of the saying of Allah: 'So when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' and by such a command the rukniyyah is established. And our evidence is the narration that he (peace be upon him) sent the weak of his family at night, and if it were a rukn he would not have done that. And what is mentioned in the recited verse is remembrance (dhikr), and that is not a rukn by consensus. And we know the obligation by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever stands with us at this standing and has already departed from Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' He attached the completion of Hajj to it, and this is suitable as an indication of obligation. Except that if one leaves it with an excuse, such as being weak or ill, or a woman who fears crowding, then nothing is upon him, because of what we have narrated. Translation: Then this standing is wajib according to us and not a rukn, so that if a pilgrim leaves it without excuse, dam becomes obligatory upon him. And Imam al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn because Allah says: 'So when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' and such a command establishes rukniyyah. And our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent the weak ones among his family at night, and if it were a rukn he would not have done that. And the verse recited mentions remembrance, and that is not a rukn by consensus. And we know the obligation of standing at Muzdalifah from the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever stands with us at this standing while having already left Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' The Prophet attached the entire Hajj to standing at Muzdalifah. And this is fit to be a sign of obligation. Except that if the pilgrim leaves it with an excuse, such as being weak or ill, or a woman who fears crowding, then nothing is obligatory upon him, due to the hadith we narrated. Commentary: Sahib Quduri said that according to us, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn. Therefore, if one leaves it without excuse, dam becomes obligatory. And Imam al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn. Sahib Inayah writes with reference to Nihayah that attributing this statement to Imam al-Shafi'i is likely a mistake, because in Shafi'i books it is mentioned that standing at Muzdalifah is sunnah. In Mabsut, instead of Imam al-Shafi'i, the name of Laith ibn Sa'd is mentioned; in Kitab al-Asrar, instead of Imam al-Shafi'i, the name of 'Alqamah is mentioned; and in Fatawa Qadi Khan, instead of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik is mentioned. Nevertheless, Sahib Hidayah attributed this saying to Imam al-Shafi'i, although it is incorrect. His evidence is the verse: 'So when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (Al-Baqarah: 198). That is, when you return from Arafat, remember Allah near the Sacred Monument. And the Sacred Monument is in Muzdalifah, so remembrance of Allah near the Sacred Monument is only possible when the pilgrim is present in Muzdalifah and stands near the Sacred Monument. And by the verse, the remembrance of Allah is established as a rukn, and it depends on standing at Muzdalifah, and the rule is that that on which a rukn depends is also a rukn, therefore standing at Muzdalifah is also a rukn. Our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent the weak ones of his family ahead at night, i.e., he sent them to Mina without standing at Muzdalifah and instructed them not to stone the Jamrat al-Aqabah until sunrise. If standing at Muzdalifah were a rukn, he would not have done that, i.e., he would not have sent the weak ahead, because leaving a rukn even with excuse is not permissible. And the response to Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that the verse mentions remembrance, and remembrance is not a rukn by consensus. So that on which remembrance depends (i.e., standing at Muzdalifah) is also not a rukn. And the obligation of standing at Muzdalifah is established by the hadith. The Prophet said: 'Whoever stands with us in Muzdalifah while having already been in Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' In this hadith, the completeness and perfection of Hajj are linked to standing at Muzdalifah, and linking is a sign of obligation. Therefore, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib. Yes, if one leaves standing at Muzdalifah due to an excuse, then no dam or anything is obligatory upon him, as mentioned in the hadith 'he sent the weak of his family.' Examples of excuse are the pilgrim being weak, ill, or a woman fearing crowding, etc. And the valley of Muhassir is not included in the standing of Muzdalifah. He said: And all of Muzdalifah is a place of standing except the valley of Muhassir, due to what we have narrated previously. Translation: He said: And all of Muzdalifah is a place of standing except the valley of Muhassir, due to the hadith we narrated earlier. Commentary: It is clear.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the legal status of wuquf (standing) at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The text begins by describing the practice: after Fajr prayer, the Imam and the people stand at Muzdalifah and make supplications, following the example of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary emphasizes the virtue of this place for acceptance of du'a, even for the forgiveness of killers and oppressors, as per the hadith of Ibn Abbas. The core legal discussion then follows: The author states that according to the Hanafi school, wuquf Muzdalifah is wajib (obligatory), not a rukn (pillar). If a pilgrim deliberately omits it without a valid excuse, he must offer a dam (sacrificial animal) as penalty. The Hanafi view is contrasted with an attributed opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i that it is a rukn. The commentary (from Ashraf al-Hidaya) notes that this attribution to Imam al-Shafi'i is likely mistaken; some sources attribute it to Laith ibn Sa'd, 'Alqamah, or Imam Malik. The Shafi'i proof cited is the Quranic verse (2:198) commanding remembrance of Allah at the Sacred Monument (Mash'ar al-Haram, i.e., Muzdalifah). The argument is that if remembrance is a rukn, then the standing upon which it depends must also be a rukn. The Hanafi response has two parts: First, the verse only commands dhikr (remembrance), and dhikr is not a rukn by consensus; the standing is merely a means, not an integral. Second, the Prophet's action of sending the weak members of his family ahead at night (without requiring them to stand at Muzdalifah) proves that it cannot be a rukn, because a rukn cannot be omitted even with excuse. The Hanafi proof for wujub is the hadith: 'Whoever stands with us at this standing after having come from Arafat, his Hajj is complete.' Attaching the completion of Hajj to this act indicates obligation (wajib) rather than pillar (rukn). However, if there is a valid excuse (weakness, illness, or a woman's fear of crowding), no penalty is incurred, as shown by the same hadith. The passage ends with a note that the entire plain of Muzdalifah is a place for standing except the valley of Muhassir, based on an earlier narration.

Key Terms
وقوف (wuquf): The act of standing at a specific place during Hajj, particularly at Arafat and Muzdalifah.
مشعر حرام (Mash'ar al-Haram): The Sacred Monument, located in Muzdalifah, where pilgrims are commanded to remember Allah after departing from Arafat.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) required as a penalty for omitting a wajib act during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) between the Hanafi and the opposing view on wuquf Muzdalifah?
A) The Hanafi view requires a larger sacrifice than the opposing view.
B) The opposing view invalidates the Hajj if the standing is missed, while the Hanafi view requires a dam but the Hajj remains valid.
C) Both views agree that missing it invalidates the Hajj.
D) The Hanafi view requires a dam only if the pilgrim is rich; the opposing view requires it only if poor.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies wuquf Muzdalifah as wajib; the opposing view (attributed to Shafi'i) as rukn, with the practical difference being Hajj validity vs penalty.

Waqoof Muzdalifah: Wajib, Not Rukn – An Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Explains ruling of standing at Muzdalifah as wajib with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that standing at Muzdalifah is wajib and not rukn, and evaluate the opposing evidence.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn – the Prophet exempted the weak, proving it is not integral.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling of Waqoof Muzdalifah, a critical point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The source text from al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi position that it is wajib, and systematically refutes the claim that it is a rukn. You will learn the evidence and reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Al-Quduri states that according to the Hanafi school, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn. If left without excuse, a dam is required.
2
Identify the opponent's view
The text attributes to Imam al-Shafi'i the view that it is a rukn, though it notes this attribution may be erroneous (some sources say sunnah or attribute to others).
The author of al-Hidayah questions the Shafi'i attribution.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent cites Quran 2:198 ('remember Allah at the Sacred Monument') and applies the principle that what a rukn depends on is itself a rukn.
The Sacred Monument is in Muzdalifah; remembrance is proven a rukn, so standing is a rukn.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: remembrance (dhikr) is not a rukn by consensus, so dependence doesn't make standing a rukn. Additionally, the Prophet sent the weak ahead without standing, proving it is not integral.
The hadith of sending the weak is the key evidence for wujub.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if omitted with a valid excuse, Hanafi says no penalty; Shafi'i (if rukn) would require compensation or invalidate Hajj.
Hanafi holds that even without excuse, only a dam is required, not invalidation.

مزدلفہ کا واجب ہونا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے (اس) قول سے پہچانا کہ جس نے ہمارے ساتھ اس موقف میں وقوف کیا حالانکہ اس سے پہلے عرفات سے ہو آیا ہے تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تمام حج کو وقوف مزدلفہ پر متعلق کیا ہے۔ اور یہ واجب ہونے کی علامت ہونے کے لائق ہے سوائے اس کے کہ جب حاجی نے اس کو عذر کے ساتھ چھوڑا بایں طور کہ اس میں ضعف ہو یا بیماری ہو یا وہ عورت ہو جو از دحام سے ڈرتی ہے تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک وقوف مزدلفہ واجب ہے نہ کہ رکن ۔ چنانچہ اگر بلا عذر وقوف مزدلفہ ترک کر دیا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نہایہ کے حوالہ سے تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ اس قول کی نسبت امام شافعی کی جانب کا تب کا سہو ہے کیونکہ کتب شوافع میں مذکور ہے کہ وقوف مزدلفہ سنت ہے۔ مبسوط میں امام شافعی کے بجائے لیث بن سعد کا نام مذکور ہے اور کتاب اسرار میں امام شافعی کی جگہ علقمہ کا نام مذکور ہے۔ اور فتاوی قاضی خاں میں امام شافعی کی جگہ امام مالک کا ذکر ہے۔ بہر حال صاحب ہدایہ نے اس قول کو امام شافعی کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے اگر چہ غلط ہے۔ اس کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُمْ مِنْ عَرَفَتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ (البقرة: ۱۹۸) ہے یعنی جب تم عرفات سے لوٹو تو مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ کا ذخر کرو۔ اور مشعر حرام مزدلفہ میں ہے پس مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ کا ذکر اسی وقت ممکن ہو گا جبکہ حاجی مزدلفہ میں حاضر ہو کر مشعر حرام کے پاس وقوف کرے۔ اور آیت کی وجہ سے ذکر اللہ کا رکن ہونا ثابت ہے اور یہ موقوف ہے و قوف مزدلفہ پر اور قاعدہ ہے کہ رکن کا موقوف علیہ بھی رکن ہوتا ہے اس لئے وقوف مزدلفہ بھی رکن ہو گا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے اہل خانہ میں سے کمزوروں کو رات میں پہلے ہی بھیج دیا یعنی بغیر وقوف مزدلفہ کئے منی میں بھیج دیا اور یہ حکم کیا کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی نہ کریں۔ یہاں تک کہ آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے ۔ اگر وقوف مزدلفہ رکن ہوتا تو آپ ایسا نہ کرتے یعنی ضعفاء کو آگے بھیجنے کا عمل نہ فرماتے ۔ کیونکہ رکن کو عذر کے ساتھ چھوڑنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت میں ذکر مذکور ہے اور ذکر بالا جماع رکن نہیں ہے ۔ ہیں جس پر ذکر موقوف ہے یعنی وقوف مزدلفہ بھی رکن نہ ہوگا۔ اور وقوف مزدلفہ کا واجب ہو نا حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ حضور نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے ہمارے ساتھ مزدلفہ میں وقوف کیا حالانکہ وہ اس سے پہلے عرفات میں ہو آیا ہے تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا۔ اس حدیث میں کمال حج اور تمام حج کو وقوف مزدلفہ پر معلق کیا ہے اور معلق کرنا وجب کی علامت ہے۔ اس لئے مزدلفہ میں وقوف واجب ہے ہاں اگر عذر کی وجہ سے وقوف مزدلفہ چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر دم وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ حدیث قَدَّمَ ضَعَفَةَ اهْلِهِ الخ میں مذکور ہے ۔ عذر کی مثال حاجی کا کمزور ہونا، بیمار ہونا یا عورت کا بھیٹر بھاڑ سے ڈرنا وغیرہ ہے۔
The obligation of standing at Muzdalifah is recognized from the statement of the Prophet (PBUH): 'Whoever stands with us at this standing, even though he has come from Arafat before, his Hajj is complete.' The Prophet (PBUH) attached the entire Hajj to the standing at Muzdalifah. And this is worthy of being a sign of obligation, except when the pilgrim leaves it with an excuse, such as weakness, illness, or a woman fearing crowding, then nothing is obligatory upon him, due to the Hadith we have narrated. Commentary: Al-Quduri stated that according to us, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn. Thus, if one leaves it without excuse, a dam (blood offering) becomes obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is a rukn. The author of al-'Inaya, citing al-Nihaya, writes that attributing this saying to Imam al-Shafi'i is an error, because in Shafi'i books it is mentioned that standing at Muzdalifah is sunnah. In al-Mabsut, the name of Layth ibn Sa'd appears instead of Imam al-Shafi'i; in Kitab al-Asrar, the name of 'Alqamah appears instead; and in Fatawa Qadi Khan, Imam Malik's name appears instead. Nevertheless, the author of al-Hidayah attributed this saying to Imam al-Shafi'i, although it is incorrect. His (Shafi'i's) evidence is the saying of Allah Most High: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (Al-Baqarah 198). That is, when you return from Arafat, remember Allah near the Sacred Monument. And the Sacred Monument is in Muzdalifah. So remembrance of Allah near the Sacred Monument is only possible when the pilgrim is present in Muzdalifah and stands near the Sacred Monument. Due to the verse, remembering Allah is proven to be a rukn, and it depends on standing at Muzdalifah. The rule is that that upon which a rukn depends is also a rukn. Therefore, standing at Muzdalifah would also be a rukn. Our proof is that the Prophet (PBUH) sent the weak from his household ahead at night, i.e., sent them to Mina without standing at Muzdalifah, and commanded them not to stone the Jamrat al-Aqaba until sunrise. If standing at Muzdalifah were a rukn, he would not have done that, i.e., he would not have sent the weak ahead, because leaving a rukn with an excuse is not permissible. The answer to Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that the verse mentions remembrance, and remembrance is not a rukn by consensus. So what remembrance is dependent upon, i.e., standing at Muzdalifah, is also not a rukn. And the obligation of standing at Muzdalifah is proven by the Hadith. The Prophet said: 'Whoever stands with us at Muzdalifah while he has come from Arafat before, his Hajj is complete.' In this Hadith, the perfection and completion of Hajj are suspended upon standing at Muzdalifah, and suspension is a sign of obligation. Therefore, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib. However, if one leaves it due to an excuse, then no dam or anything is obligatory upon him, as mentioned in the Hadith 'He sent the weak of his family...' Examples of excuses: the pilgrim being weak, ill, or a woman fearing crowding, etc.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a classic inter-madhhab dispute about the legal status of standing at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Quduri, is that it is wajib — a lesser obligation than a rukn but still binding. The evidence comes from the Prophet's action of exempting the weak from the standing, which would not be permissible if it were a rukn. The opposing view (attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, though the text notes that attribution may be erroneous) holds it to be a rukn, using the Quranic verse about the Sacred Monument. The Hanafi response dismantles the analogy: the verse commands remembrance, which itself is not a rukn, so what it depends on is not a rukn either. The author follows the order: first states the Hanafi ruling, presents the opponent's view, corrects the attribution, gives the opponent's evidence, then gives the Hanafi evidence and rebuttal. The practical consequence: if lost with excuse, no penalty; if without excuse, a dam is owed.

Key Terms
وقوف مزدلفہ (Waqoof Muzdalifah): Standing (brief halt) at Muzdalifah during Hajj after returning from Arafat.
رکن (Rukn): An integral part of Hajj; omission invalidates Hajj.
واجب (Wajib): A lesser obligatory act; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate Hajj.
دم (Dam): A blood offering (sacrifice) required as compensation for certain omissions in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on leaving Waqoof Muzdalifah due to a valid excuse like illness?
A) Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) No penalty is obligated.
C) A dam (blood offering) is required.
D) It is not permissible to leave even with an excuse.

Key Takeaway
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn; it can be omitted with a valid excuse without compensation.

Ruling on the Valid Standing Place in Muzdalifah
States ruling and exception for Muzdalifah standing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the boundaries of the valid standing place (mawqif) in Muzdalifah and identify the exception of Wadi Muhassir.

Core Idea
The entire plain of Muzdalifah is valid for standing except Wadi Muhassir.

This lesson focuses on a specific ruling regarding the Hajj ritual of standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah. The author, al-Quduri, states a clear rule: all of Muzdalifah is a valid place for this wajib act except for one valley, Wadi Muhassir. Understanding this geographical exception is crucial for the correct performance of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the ruling concerns the wuquf (standing) at Muzdalifah on the night of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
This standing is a wajib act of Hajj.
2
State the general ruling
The text says: 'Muzdalifah, all of it, is a standing place.'
This means the entire area is valid for wuquf.
3
Identify the exception
The exception is Wadi Muhassir, a specific valley within Muzdalifah.
This exception is based on a hadith narrated earlier.
4
Apply the ruling
When performing wuquf, ensure that you are within Muzdalifah but outside Wadi Muhassir.
To be safe, avoid the valley floor.

This exception is based on a prophetic tradition (hadith) that was mentioned earlier in the text. The author notes that the commentary is straightforward and requires no further elaboration.

Timing of Departure from Muzdalifah
Textual critique and reconciliation of departure time from Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct time for departure from Muzdalifah to Mina according to the Hanafi school and explain the textual reconciliation of the Quduri matn.

Core Idea
Depart from Muzdalifah when the dawn light spreads, not at sunrise – the Prophet's practice is the standard.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a subtle textual dispute in the Mukhtasar of Al-Quduri regarding the timing of departure from Muzdalifah on the Day of Sacrifice. Some manuscripts state 'when the sun rises,' but the author of Al-Hidayah corrects this based on the Prophet's (PBUH) practice of departing before sunrise. He reconciles the two by interpreting 'sunrise' as 'near sunrise,' ensuring the ruling aligns with the Sunnah. By studying this passage, you will learn how Hanafi scholars critically refine matn texts to preserve authentic legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine what the passage is about: the time of departure from Muzdalifah to Mina on the Day of Sacrifice.
The ruling is about the recommended (sunnah) time, not a condition for the validity of Hajj.
2
Understand the textual dispute
Note the conflicting wording in copies of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar: 'when the sun rises' versus the correct reading 'when the dawn spreads (asfara)'.
The author of Al-Hidayah declares the former a mistake and provides the correct version.
3
Analyze the evidence and reconciliation
The Prophet's action of departing before sunrise is the binding evidence. The author reconciles by reinterpreting 'sunrise' as 'close to sunrise.'
This shows the Hanafi method of harmonizing textual variants with stronger proofs (Sunnah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

کتاب النج
قَالَ فَإِذَا طَلَعَتِ الشَّمْسُ فَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا مِنى قَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ عَصَمَهُ اللَّهُ هكَذَا وَقَعَ فِي نُسخ الْمَخْتَصَرِ وَهَذَا غَلَط وَالصَّحِيحُ إِذَا أَسْفَرَ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ لِأَنَّ النَّبِي عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ دَفَعَ قَبْلَ طُلوع الشمس
ترجمہ کہا پھر جب آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے تو امام لوگ روانہ ہوں یہاں تک کہ منی میں آئیں ۔ عبد ضعیف نے کہا کہ قدوری کے نسخوں میں یو نبی واقع ہے اور یہ غلط ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ جب خوب روشنی ہو جائے تو امام اور لوگ روانہ ہوں کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم آفتاب طلوع ہونے سے پہلے روانہ ہوئے ہیں۔

After sunrise, the Imam and the people come to Mina. The book of (al-Hajj). He said: Then when the sun has risen, the Imam and the people depart until they come to Mina. 'Abd al-Da'if said: This is how it occurs in copies of al-Mukhtasar, and this is a mistake. The correct version is: When the dawn has spread (asfara), the Imam and the people depart, because the Prophet (PBUH) departed before sunrise. Translation: He said: Then when the sun rises, the Imam and the people depart to come to Mina. 'Abd al-Da'if said: In al-Quduri's copies, it is written like this, and it is wrong. The correct view is that when there is good light, the Imam and the people should depart, because the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) departed before sunrise. Commentary: Al-Quduri says: When the sun of the Day of Sacrifice rises, the Imam of the Muslims and the people depart from Muzdalifah and go to Mina. The author of al-Hidayah says: In some copies of al-Quduri, it says that they departed before sunrise. But we say that al-Quduri's wording is also correct, because 'when the sun has risen' can mean 'when it is close to rising'. So there is no contradiction between the two copies.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage addresses a textual dispute regarding the exact wording of al-Quduri's matn about the departure time from Muzdalifah. Some copies state that departure occurs after sunrise, but the correct understanding, supported by the prophetic practice, is that departure should be at the time of isfar (clear dawn light) before sunrise. The author reconciles these by interpreting 'when the sun rises' in al-Quduri's version as 'when the sun is about to rise', thus eliminating the contradiction. The commentary serves as a critical refinement of the matn, ensuring the legal ruling aligns with the Sunnah.

Key Terms
إِذَا أَسْفَرَ (idha asfara): When the dawn light spreads and the sky becomes bright, but before actual sunrise.
دَفَعَ (dafa'a): To depart or move from one place to another, specifically from Muzdalifah to Mina.
غَلَط (ghalat): An error or mistake; here, referring to the incorrect wording in certain manuscripts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When did the Prophet (PBUH) depart from Muzdalifah to Mina on the Day of Sacrifice?
A) After sunrise
B) At the time of clear dawn light (isfar) before sunrise
C) At noon
D) At midnight

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling for departure from Muzdalifah is to go when the dawn light spreads (isfar), before sunrise, based on the Prophet's practice, and any textual variant suggesting sunrise is reinterpreted to mean near sunrise.

Stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba: Procedure and Proof
Describes the method of stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the prescribed procedure for stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, state the required number and size of pebbles, and identify the two prophetic proofs (fi'l and qawl) that establish the ruling.

Core Idea
Seven small pebbles thrown at Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor — a Sunnah established by the Prophet's action and command.

This lesson examines the stoning ritual at Jamrat al-Aqaba, the first rite performed upon arriving in Mina on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The passage from al-Quduri details the method, and the commentary expands on the various dimensions of the act. By understanding the exact specifications, you will be able to perform this essential Hajj rite correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ritual and its status
The text describes the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba, a required rite of Hajj. Recognize that in the Hanafi school, stoning all three jamaraat on the specified days is wajib (obligatory), not merely sunnah. The passage focuses on the procedure, but understanding the obligation context is essential.
Rami is wajib according to Hanafi; missing it requires a dam (sacrificial penalty).
2
Note the prescribed details
The text specifies: seven pebbles (حصیات) of a specific size – like حصى الخذف (small pebbles used for khazaf, approximately fingertip size). The place is بطن الوادي (the bottom of the valley) at Jamrat al-Aqaba. Commit these elements to memory as they are derived from the Prophet's practice.
The number 7 and the small size are crucial; deviation may affect validity.
3
Understand the prophetic proof (dalil)
Two proofs are cited: (1) The Prophet's action: when he came to Mina, he went straight to Jamrat al-Aqaba and stoned it without stopping. (2) The Prophet's command: 'عَلَيْكُمْ بِحِصَى الْخَذْفِ' (Hold fast to pebbles of khazaf) to avoid harming others. This shows the Sunnah is established by both fi'l (action) and qawl (saying).
The action is mutawatir; the hadith concerning size is found in various collections.
4
Expand via the commentary's twelve points
The commentary lists twelve aspects of rami, though only the first six are partially mentioned in this passage: time, place, location, number, size, method. This expansion shows the depth of Hanafi fiqh. Consider these as a framework for the complete rami ritual.
The commentary is not fully reproduced; it serves as an indication of further detail.

Source Text

جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کریں
قال فَيَبْتَدِى بِجَمْرَةِ الْعَقَبَةِ فَيَرُ مِنْهَا مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِى بِسَبْع حَصَيَاتٍ مِثلَ حِصَى الْخَذَفِ لِأَنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمَّا أَتَى مِنى لَمْ يَعْرُجُ عَلَى شَيْ حَتَّى رَمَى جَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةَ وَ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ بِحِصَى الْعَذَفِ لَا يُؤْذِى بَعْضُكُم بَعْضًا
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا پھر جمرہ عقبہ سے شروع کرے پس اس پر بطن وادی سے سات کنکریاں ٹھیکری کی کنکریوں کی طرح پھینکے۔ اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم جب منی میں آئے تو کسی چیز پر توقف نہیں کیا حتی کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی فرمائی ۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ لازم پکڑو پوروں سے پھینکنے کی کنکریاں تم میں سے بعض بعض کو ایذا نہ دیں۔
تشریح رمی کے سلسلہ میں بارہ جگہ کلام ہے۔
(1 وقت وہ یوم نحر اور تین دن اس کے بعد ہیں۔ (۲ موضع رمی : سو وہ بطن وادی ہے۔ ۳) محل رمی : وہ تین جمرے ہیں جمرہ عقبہ مسجد خیف اور جمرہ وسطی ۔ (۴ کنکریوں کی تعداد: سو وہ ہر جہرہ کے پاس سات ہیں۔ (۵ مقدار تو انگلی کے پوروے کے مانند ہے۔ ( رمی کی کیفیت : سو وہ کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔
Perform the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba. He (al-Quduri) said: He begins with Jamrat al-Aqaba, and he throws at it from the bottom of the valley seven pebbles like the pebbles of khazaf (small stone pieces), because when the Prophet (PBUH) came to Mina, he did not stop for anything until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba. And the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Use pebbles of khazaf, so that some of you do not harm others.' Translation: Al-Quduri said: Then he should start with Jamrat al-Aqaba, and throw at it from the bottom of the valley seven pebbles similar to small stones (size of fingertip), because when the Prophet (PBUH) arrived at Mina, he did not pause for anything until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba. And the Prophet said: 'Hold fast to the pebbles of khazaf, so that you do not harm one another.' Commentary: Regarding stoning, there are twelve points of discussion: (1) Time: the Day of Sacrifice and the three days after it. (2) Place of throwing: the bottom of the valley. (3) Location of throwing: the three jamaraat: Jamrat al-Aqaba, Masjid al-Khayf, and al-Jamrah al-Wusta. (4) Number of pebbles: seven at each jamrah. (5) Size: like the tip of the finger. (6) Method: as mentioned in the book.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage presents the procedure for the stoning (rami) of Jamrat al-Aqaba, the largest of the three stone pillars in Mina. The ruling is based on the Prophet's action: he went straight to it upon arriving in Mina. The pebbles should be small, like those used for khazaf (a type of pottery), to avoid harm. The subsequent commentary outlines twelve aspects of rami, though only the first few are enumerated: the time (the 10th and the following three days), the place (the bottom of the valley), the specific locations (the three pillars), the number (seven per pillar), the size (as large as a fingertip), and the manner (detailed in the book). The overall practice is established by prophetic Sunnah and is an essential part of Hajj.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The largest of the three stone pillars in Mina, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
رمى (Rami): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamaraat during Hajj.
حصى الخذف (Hasa al-khazaf): Small pebbles the size of a fingertip, used for stoning.

The stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba must be performed with seven small pebbles from the valley floor, following the Prophet's example and command.

Time for Departure from Muzdalifah on the Day of Nahr
Correcting the time of departure from Muzdalifah based on Prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi position on the time of departure from Muzdalifah and explain the reconciliation of the two wordings in the Quduri text.

Core Idea
Depart from Muzdalifah after bright dawn (isfar), not after sunrise — following the Prophet's practice.

This passage addresses an important detail of the Hajj: when should the imam and pilgrims leave Muzdalifah for Mina on the Day of Nahr? The base text of Quduri appears to say 'after sunrise,' but the commentator corrects this based on the Prophet's own action. Understanding this distinction ensures we follow the sunnah accurately and appreciate how Hanafi scholars resolve textual discrepancies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue in the text
Read the matn (Quduri) and note what time it specifies for departure. Then read the commentator's objection and correction.
The matn says 'when the sun has risen' but the commentator says this is a mistake.
2
Understand the Prophetic evidence
The commentator bases the correction on the fact that the Prophet departed from Muzdalifah before sunrise. Recognise that the Prophet's action is the sunnah.
The hadith is widely reported in Sahih Muslim and other collections.
3
Analyse the Hanafi reconciliation
Learn how al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah reconciles the two wordings: he interprets 'tulu' al-shams' as meaning 'near sunrise' rather than actual sunrise, thus removing the contradiction.
This is a classic example of hermeneutical reconciliation within the madhhab.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is to depart after isfar (bright dawn). This is what the commentator confirms and what the Hidayah upholds.
Departing after full sunrise is permissible but not optimal.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
Consider how a modern pilgrim would implement this: wait until the sky is bright (about 15-20 minutes before sunrise) and then proceed to Mina.
This sunnah is easy to follow and brings reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِذَا طَلَعَتِ الشَّمْسُ فَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ حَتَّى يَأْتُوا مِنى قَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ عَصَمَهُ اللَّهُ هكَذَا وَقَعَ فِي نُسخ الْمَخْتَصَرِ وَهَذَا غَلَط وَالصَّحِيحُ إِذَا أَسْفَرَ أَفَاضَ الْإِمَامُ وَالنَّاسُ لِأَنَّ النَّبِي عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ دَفَعَ قَبْلَ طُلوع الشمس
ترجمہ کہا پھر جب آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے تو امام لوگ روانہ ہوں یہاں تک کہ منی میں آئیں ۔ عبد ضعیف نے کہا کہ قدوری کے نسخوں میں یو نبی واقع ہے اور یہ غلط ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ جب خوب روشنی ہو جائے تو امام اور لوگ روانہ ہوں کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم آفتاب طلوع ہونے سے پہلے روانہ ہوئے ہیں۔
تشریح . صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ جب یوم نحر کا آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے تو امام المسلمین اور لوگ مزدلفہ سے روانہ ہو کر مٹی چلے جائیں ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں یہی ہے کہ آفتاب طلوع ہونے سے پہلے ہی مزدلفہ سے روانہ ہوئے تھے لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ قدوری کی یہ عبارت بھی درست ہے۔ اس لئے کہ إِذَا طَلَعَتِ الشَّمْسُ کے معنی إِذَا قَرُبَتْ إِلَى الطَّلوعِ کے ہیں ۔ پس اب دونوں نسخوں میں کوئی تعارض نہیں رہا۔
He said: Then when the sun has risen, the imam and the people will proceed until they come to Mina. The weak servant (may Allah protect him) said: This occurs in some copies of al-Mukhtasar, and this is a mistake. The correct view is that when it has become bright (asfar), the imam and the people proceed, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) departed before sunrise.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage addresses the time for the departure from Muzdalifah to Mina on the Day of Nahr. The base text (Quduri) states that departure is after sunrise. However, the commentator (al-'Abd al-Da'if) points out that this is an error in some manuscripts; the correct ruling is that departure should be after isfar (bright dawn), not after sunrise. This is based on the Prophet's practice, as he departed before sunrise. The author of Hidayah reconciles the two wordings by interpreting 'idha tala'at al-shams' (when the sun rises) as meaning 'when it is near rising' (idha qarabat ila al-tulu'), thus removing the contradiction. The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah to depart after dawn, imitating the Prophet.

Key Terms
إِسْفَار (isfar): The time when the dawn light becomes bright (white) on the horizon, before sunrise.
طلوع الشمس (tulu‘ al-shams): The actual rising of the sun above the horizon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) At midday

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that departing from Muzdalifah after bright dawn (isfar) is the sunnah, based on the Prophet's practice, and any textual indication to the contrary is reconciled through interpretation.

The Obligation and Proof for Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah
Ruling and proof for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is wajib and identify the Prophetic proof that establishes its obligation.

Core Idea
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is wajib — the Prophet's command 'alaykum' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.

In this lesson, we examine the core ruling of stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr. The Quduri text states that one must begin with this jamrah, throwing seven small pebbles from the bottom of the valley. The proof is the Prophet's immediate action and his explicit command, which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. Omitting it requires a sacrifice (dam) but does not invalidate Hajj.
Wajib is distinct from fard; fard requires a definitive proof (qati), while wajib is based on zanni proof.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: the Prophet's action (he did not stop until he stoned) and his command 'عَلَيْكُمْ بِحِصَى الْخَذَفِ' (use small pebbles).
The hadith is ahad, making it zanni al-thubut, hence the ruling is wajib.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'عَلَيْكُمْ' is a command (amr), and in Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the imperative indicates obligation). The Prophet's immediate action reinforces this.
The same command also indicates the preferred size of pebbles (small) to avoid harm.
4
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
This ruling is agreed upon (muttifaq alayh) among the four schools. There is no significant dispute regarding the obligation of stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah.
5
Understand the hukm level: wajib
Because the dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut), the ruling is wajib, not fard. The practical consequence: omission requires a dam (sacrifice), not invalidation of Hajj.
If someone deliberately omits stoning, they must sacrifice a sheep to compensate.

کتاب الحج .
(۷) مقدار رمی یہ بھی کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ (۸) رامی کی صفت : وہ یہ ہے کہ رامی سوار ہو یا پیادہ پا۔ (۹) کنگریان گرنے کی جگہ۔ (۱۰ جہاں سے کنکریاں لی جائیں گی۔ یہ دونوں بھی کتاب میں مذکور ہیں (11) کنکریاں کس قسم کی ہوں : وہ یہ ہے کہ زمین کی جنس سے ہوں ۔ (۱۲ یوم اول میں فقط جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کی جائے گی اور بقیہ ایام میں تینوں جمروں کی۔

صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ رمی کا آغاز جمرہ عقبہ سے ہوگا چنانچہ وادی کے نیچے سے سات کنکریاں پھینک مارے اور یہ کنکریاں انگلی کے پوروں کے بقدر ہوں جن کو انگوٹھے اور شہادت کی انگلی کے کنارے سے پھینکا جا سکتا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم جب منی میں تشریف لائے تو آپ نے بلا توقف کئے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی فرمائی۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم پر کنکریاں پھینکنا لا زم ہے۔ بعضے تم میں سے بعض کو ایذا نہ دیں۔
رمی کی کنگری کا حجم کتنا ہونا چاہئے
وَلَوْ رَمَى بِأَكْبَرَ مِنْهُ جَازَ لِحُصُولِ الرَّمُ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَرْمِي بِالْكَبِيرِ مِنَ الْأَحْجَارٍ كَيْلَا يَتَأَذًى بِهِ غَيْرَهُ وَلَوْ رَمَاهَا مِنْ فَوْقِ الْعَقَبَةِ أَجْرَاهُ لِأَنَّ مَا حَوْلَهَا مَوْضِعُ النُّسُكِ وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِي لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَيُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ كَذَا رَوَى ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ وَابْنُ عُمَرَ وَلَوْ سَبَّحَ مَكَانَ التَّكْبِيرِ أَجْزَاهُ لِحُصُولِ الذِّكْرِ وَهُوَ مِنْ آدَابِ الرَّمَى وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمْ يَقِفْ عِنْدَهَا وَيَقْطَعُ التَّلْبِيَةَ مَعَ أَوَّلِ حَصَاةٍ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَرَوَى جَابِرٌ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَطَعَ التَّلْبِيَةَ عِنْدَ أَوَّلِ حَصَاةٍ رَمَى بِهَا جَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ
He said: He begins with Jamrat al-Aqabah and throws from it from the bottom of the valley seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhaf (small stones). Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he came to Mina did not stop for anything until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah. And he said (peace be upon him): 'Use small pebbles (khadhaf); let not some of you harm others.'
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage details the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr. It begins by stating that one should start with this jamrah, throwing seven small pebbles (like khadhaf — small stones used in slings) from the bottom of the valley (Batin al-Wadi). The proof is the Prophet's immediate action upon reaching Mina and his command to use small stones to avoid harming others. The commentary expands on twelve aspects of ramy, including time (Day of Nahr and three subsequent days), place (Batin al-Wadi for Jamrat al-Aqabah), number (seven per jamrah), and size (fingertip-sized). It then addresses valid variations: throwing larger stones is permissible but discouraged due to potential harm; throwing from above the jamrah is valid but the best is from Batin al-Wadi; saying takbir (Allahu Akbar) with each stone is recommended, but tasbih is sufficient; one should not stand at the jamrah (for Jamrat al-Aqabah on the first day) because the Prophet did not; and the talbiyah is cut with the first stone thrown, based on reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Jabir.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqabah): The largest of the three stone pillars in Mina, located near the end of the valley, stoned on the Day of Nahr and on subsequent days.
حصى الخذف (hasa al-khadhaf): Small pebbles, approximately the size of a fingertip, used for stoning.
بطن الوادي (Batin al-Wadi): The bottom or low area of the valley, the preferred location for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah.
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' with each pebble thrown; if one says another dhikr like tasbih, it suffices.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred location for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr?
A) From above the jamrah
B) From the bottom of the valley (Batin al-Wadi)
C) From inside the mosque of Mina
D) From the top of the mountain

Key Takeaway
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is wajib, proved by the Prophet's command and action; omitting it requires a dam but does not invalidate Hajj.

Manner and Etiquettes of Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah
Expansion on etiquettes and permissible variations in stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunnan (recommended practices) of stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah and distinguish between permissible variations and optimal practices.

Core Idea
The sunnah in stoning is to use small pebbles, throw from Batin al-Wadi, say takbir, and not stand; but variations are generally valid.

While the core ruling of stoning is wajib, the Prophet's practice established several etiquettes (adab) that perfect the act. This lesson explores these details from the commentary of Al-Hidayah, covering permissible alternatives and recommended practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the adab (etiquettes)
List the recommended actions: using small pebbles (like khadhaf), throwing from the bottom of the valley (Batin al-Wadi), saying Takbir with each pebble, not standing after stoning (on the first day), and cutting the talbiyah with the first stone.
These are based on the Prophet's practice and are sunnah, not wajib.
2
Note the permissible alternatives
Larger pebbles are valid but discouraged to avoid harm. Throwing from above the jamrah is valid, though the bottom is best. Saying tasbih instead of takbir suffices.
The principle: the essence of the act (throwing) is achieved, so variations are accepted unless explicitly prohibited.
3
Understand the basis
Each adab is rooted in the Prophet's action or command. For example, the prohibition against standing is because the Prophet did not stand at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr.
4
Distinguish between adab and wajib
The adab are not required; omitting them does not require any compensation (dam). They perfect the act but do not affect its validity.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: wajib requires compensation, sunnah does not.

Rulings on the Size of Pebbles and Ritual of Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah
Rulings on pebble size, location, takbir, and cutting talbiyah for Jamrat al-Aqabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi rulings on the size of pebbles for stoning, the preferred location, the accompanying dhikr, and the timing for cutting talbiyah, and EXPLAIN the proofs from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah must be with small pebbles from the valley, accompanied by takbir, and talbiyah ends with the first pebble.

The stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah is a wajib ritual of Hajj with specific etiquettes derived from the Prophet's practice. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rulings on the size of pebbles, the preferred location, the recommended dhikr, and the termination of talbiyah, as well as the permissible variations and their proofs. Understanding these details ensures the ritual is performed correctly and with optimal reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
Stoning the jamarat is wajib in the Hanafi school. The passage focuses on sunnah acts within the stoning ritual.
The overall obligation is already established; here we learn the details.
2
Locate the dalil for each sub-ruling
Find the specific hadith proofs: for pebble size (Prophet's action and command), location (hadith of stoning from valley), takbir (hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar), cutting talbiyah (hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and Jabir).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Each proof indicates recommended (sunnah) practice, not obligation. The imperative or narrated action shows desirability.
Hanafi usul: commands can indicate wujub or nadb; here context shows nadb.
4
Note the permissible deviations
Identify what is valid but less preferred: using larger pebbles, stoning from above the Aqabah, saying tasbih instead of takbir.
These are allowed but reduce reward.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is to follow the sunnah: finger-knuckle pebbles, valley floor, takbir, and cutting talbiyah with first pebble.
The text also cautions against excessively large stones to avoid harm.

رمی کی کنگری کا حجم کتنا ہونا چاہئے
وَلَوْرَمَى بِأَكْبَرَ مِنْهُ جَازَ لِحُصُولِ الرَّمُ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَرْمِي بِالْكَبِيرِ مِنَ الْأَحْجَارٍ كَيْلَا يَتَأَذًى بِهِ غَيْرَهُ وَلَوْرَمَاهَا مِنْ فَوْقِ الْعَقَبَةِ أَجْرَاهُ لِأَنَّ مَاحَولَهَا مَوْضِعُ النُّسُكِ وَالْأَفْضَلُ أنْ يَكُونَ مِنْ بَطْنِ الْوَادِي لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَيُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ كَذَا رَوَى إِبْنُ مَسْعُودٍ وَابْنُ عُمَرَ وَلَوْ سَبَّحَ مَكَانَ التَّكْبِيرِ أجْزَاهُ لِحُصُولِ الذِكرِ وَهُوَ من آدابِ الرَّمى وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمْ يَقِفْ عِنْدَهَا وَيَقْطَعُ التَّلْبِيَة مَعَ أَوَّلِ حَصَاةٍ لِمَارَوَيْنَا عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَرَوى جَابِرٌ أَنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَطَعَ التَّلْبِينَ عِنْدَ أَوَّلِ حَصَاةٍ رَمَى بِهَا جَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ
ترجمہ اور اگر حاجی نے انگلی کے پورے سے بڑی کنگری پھینکی تو جائز ہے کیونکہ رمی حاصل ہو گئی مگر یہ کہ بڑا پتھر نہ پھینکے تا کہ اس سے دوسرے کو اذیت پہنچے۔ اور اگر عقبہ کے اوپر سے رمی کی تو کافی ہے۔ کیونکہ جمرہ کے گردنسک کا مقام ہے اور افضل یہ ہے کہ بطن وادی سے ہو اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی۔ اور ہر کنکری مارنے کے ساتھ تکبیر کہے ایسا ہی ابن مسعود اور ابن عمر سے مروی ہے۔ اور اگر تکبیر کی جگہ تسبیح کی تو کافی ہے کیونکہ ذکر اللہ حاصل ہو گیا اور ذکر کر نارمی کے آداب میں سے ہے۔ اور جمرہ عقبہ کے پاس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نہیں ٹھہرے ہیں اور پہلی ہی کنگری کے ساتھ تلبیہ قطع کر دے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم کو ابن مسعودؓ سے پہنچی ہے۔ اور جابر نے روایت کی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پہلی ہی کنکری کے وقت جس سے آپ نے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی فرمائی تلبیہ قطع کر دیا۔ تشریح طول و عرض کے اعتبار سے کنکریوں کی مقدار بیان کر دی گئی کہ وہ انگلی کے پورے کے مانند موٹی اور لمبی ہوں۔ لیکن اگر اس سے بڑی کنکریوں کے ساتھ رمی کی تو بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ مقصود می حاصل ہو گیا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ بڑے بڑے پتھر نہ پھینکے ورنہ خواہ مخواہ لوگوں کو اذیت پہنچے گی ۔ افضل تو یہ ہے کہ ری بطن وادی سے کی جائے لیکن اگر عقبہ کے اوپر سے رمی کی تو بھی جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ جمرہ کے چاروں طرف موضع نسک ہے۔ ہر کنکری کے ساتھ اللہ اکبر کہے جیسا کہ ابن مسعود اور ابن عمر کی حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے لیکن اگر تکبیر کی جگہ تسبیح کہی ساتھ اللہ اورابن کی ہوتا تب بھی درست ہے کیونکہ ذکر اللہ حاصل ہو گیا اور ذکر اللہ ہی رمی کے آداب میں سے ہے۔ حاجی جمرہ عقبہ کے پاس نہ ٹھہرے اس لئے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم بھی نہیں ٹھہرے تھے۔ اور پہلی کنکری پھینکتے ہی تلبیہ ختم کر دے کیونکہ ابن مسعود اور حضرت جابر کی روایت میں یہی مذکور ہے۔
Book of Hajj. (7) The amount of stoning is also mentioned in the book. Description of the stoner: He should be mounted or on foot. (9) The place where the pebbles fall. (10) From where the pebbles will be taken. Both of these are also mentioned in the book. (11) What kind of pebbles: They should be from the genus of the earth. (12) On the first day, only Jamrat al-Aqabah will be stoned, and on the remaining days, all three jamarat. The author of Quduri says: Stoning will begin with Jamrat al-Aqabah, so he should throw seven pebbles from the bottom of the valley, and these pebbles should be the size of the phalanx of a finger, which can be thrown with the edge of the thumb and index finger. The proof is that when the Prophet, peace be upon him, came to Mina, he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah without stopping. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: Stoning pebbles is obligatory upon you; do not harm some of you to others. The size of the pebbles for stoning: And if he stoned with larger than that, it is permissible because stoning is achieved, but he should not throw large stones so that others are not harmed by it. And if he stoned from above the Aqabah, it is sufficient because the area around it is the place of the ritual, and the best is that it be from the bottom of the valley due to what we have narrated. And he should say takbir with each pebble; thus it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. And if he says tasbih instead of takbir, it is sufficient because dhikr is achieved, and dhikr is among the etiquettes of stoning. And he should not stand near it because the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not stand near it. And he should cut the talbiyah with the first pebble due to what we have narrated from Ibn Mas'ud, and Jabir narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, cut the talbiyah at the first pebble with which he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah. Translation: And if the pilgrim threw a pebble larger than the fingertip, it is permissible because stoning is achieved, but he should not throw a large stone so as not to harm others. And if he stoned from above the Aqabah, it is sufficient because the area around the jamrah is the place of the ritual, and the best is that it be from the bottom of the valley due to the hadith we have narrated. And he should say takbir with each pebble; thus it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. And if he says tasbih instead of takbir, it is sufficient because the remembrance of Allah is achieved, and remembrance is among the etiquettes of stoning. And he should not stand near Jamrat al-Aqabah because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did not stand there. And he should cut the talbiyah with the first pebble due to the hadith that has reached us from Ibn Mas'ud, and Jabir narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, cut the talbiyah at the time of the first pebble with which he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah. Explanation: The size of the pebbles in terms of length and breadth has been stated: they should be thick and long like the phalanx of a finger. But if he stoned with larger pebbles than that, it is also permissible because the purpose is achieved. However, it is necessary that he not throw large stones, otherwise he will unnecessarily harm people. The best is that stoning be done from the bottom of the valley, but if he stoned from above the Aqabah, it is also permissible because the area around the jamrah is the place of the ritual. He should say Allahu Akbar with each pebble, as is known from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar, but if he says tasbih instead of takbir, it is also correct because the remembrance of Allah is achieved, and remembrance of Allah is among the etiquettes of stoning. The pilgrim should not stand near Jamrat al-Aqabah because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did not stand there. And he should end the talbiyah with the first pebble because this is mentioned in the narration of Ibn Mas'ud and Hadrat Jabir.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the stoning ritual (rami) on the first day of Eid. It opens by stating foundational rules: stoning begins exclusively with Jamrat al-Aqabah, the pebbles must be small (size of a finger phalanx) and from earth. The proof is the Prophet's action at Mina and his command to stone without causing harm. The text then addresses permissible variations: using larger pebbles is valid but makruh if excessively large due to harm; stoning from above the Aqabah is valid but preferable from the valley bottom. Each pebble should be accompanied by takbir, but tasbih suffices since dhikr is the objective. The pilgrim should not pause after stoning this jamrah, following the Prophet's practice. Talbiyah ends with the first pebble thrown. The commentary explains these as recommended (sunnah) practices; deviations from the sunnah may reduce reward but do not invalidate the stoning.

Key Terms
رمی (ramy): The ritual of throwing pebbles at the jamarat during Hajj.
جمرہ عقبہ (jamrat al-'aqabah): The largest jamrah near Mina, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The invocations 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the pilgrim stop reciting the talbiyah?
A) At the beginning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
B) With the first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah
C) After completing all stoning on the 10th
D) At sunset of the 10th

Key Takeaway
The stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah should be performed with small pebbles from the valley, saying takbir with each throw, and talbiyah ends with the first pebble; deviations are permissible but reduce reward.
