Method of Stoning: Placement and Distance
Describes how to hold and throw pebbles, required distance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the sunnah method of stoning from dropping and placing, and state the ruling for each action.

Core Idea
Sunnah throw uses thumb+index with five cubits; dropping is valid but sinful; placing is invalid.

Stoning the jamarat is a wajib act of Hajj, but its performance has a specific sunnah method that maximizes reward. This passage, narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa through Hasan ibn Ziyad, clarifies the correct technique and the consequences of deviation. Understanding these gradations helps the pilgrim fulfill the obligation with full compliance to the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
Recognize that the passage deals specifically with the physical method of throwing pebbles (rami) at the jamarat, not with the number of pebbles or timing.
The context is the ritual stoning during Hajj.
2
Extract the sunnah method
Note that the sunnah method requires placing the pebble on the back of the right thumb, using the index finger to propel it, and achieving a distance of at least five cubits (approx. 2.5 meters) between thrower and target.
This narration is from the nawadir but widely accepted.
3
Analyze the three scenarios
The passage describes three possible actions: sunnah throw (ramy), dropping (tarh) with less than five cubits, and placing (wad') without throwing. For each, identify the ruling: ramy is sunnah muakkadah, tarh fulfills the obligation but is sinful, wad' is invalid.
The key distinction is whether the act is considered ‘throwing’ (رمي) or not.
4
Evaluate the evidence
The proof for the five-cubit distance and thumb placement is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa. The rational basis (illa) is that less than five cubits constitutes dropping (tarh), which is not the sunnah.
The proof is a qawl sahabi with zanni thubut and dalala.

کنکری پھینکنے کا طریقہ
ثُمَّ كَيْفِيةُ الرَّمَى أَنْ يَضَعَ الْحِصَاةَ عَلَى ظَهَرا بَهَامِهِ الْيُمْنَى وَيَسْتَعِينُ بِالْمُسَحَةِ وَمِقْدَارُ الرَّمَى أَنْ يَكُونَ بَينَ الرَّمَى وَبَيْنَ مَوْضِع السُّقوطِ خَمْسَةَ أذرع كَذَا رَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ طَرُحًا وَلَوْ طَرَحَهَا طَرْحًا أَجْزَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ رَمَى إِلى قَدَمَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ، مُسِيُّ لِمُخَالِفَةِ السُّنَّةِ وَلَوْ وَضَعَهَا وَضُعَالَمْ يَجُرُهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ
ترجمہ پھر کنکری پھینک مارنے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ کنکری کو اپنے دائیں انگوٹھے کی پشت پر رکھے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے مدد لے۔ اور رمی کی مقدار یہ ہے کہ پھینکنے والے اور گرنے کی جگہ کے درمیان پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ہو ۔ ایسا ہی حسن نے ابوحنیفہ سے روایت کیا ہے کیونکہ اس سے کم تو ڈال دینا ہو گا۔ اور اگر اس نے کنکری کو ڈال دیا تو بھی کافی ہے کیونکہ اس نے کنکری اپنے قدموں کی طرف پھینکی مگر یہ شخص مخالفت سنت کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے کنکری کو رکھ دیا تو کافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ میری نہیں ہے۔
تشریح رمی کی کیفیت بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ کنکری کو اپنے دائیں انگوٹھے کی پشت پر رکھ کر شہادت کی انگلی کے تعاون سے۔ پھینک دے اور رمی کرنے والے اور کنکری گرنے کی جگہ کے درمیان کم از کم پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ہونا چاہئے حسن بن زیاد نے ابو حنیفہ سے یہی روایت کی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس سے کم فاصلہ کی صورت میں پھینکنے کا اطلاق نہیں ہوگا بلکہ ڈالنے کا اطلاق ہوگا حالانکہ کنگری کا پھینکنا سنت ہے نہ کہ ڈالنا۔ اور اگر اس نے کنکری کو بجائے پھینکنے کے عمد اڈال دیا تو بھی کافی ہے کیونکہ اس نے کنکری کو اپنے قدموں کی طرف پھینکا ہے لیکن سنت کے خلاف کام کرنے کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا اور اگر اس نے کنکری کو رکھ دیا تو کافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ کسی طرح رمی نہیں ہے۔
Method of throwing pebbles: Then the method of stoning is that he places the pebble on the back of his right thumb and seeks help from the index finger. And the measure of stoning is that there be a distance of five cubits between the thrower and the place of falling. Thus Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa because less than that would be dropping. And if he drops it by dropping, it suffices him because he threw it towards his feet, but he is sinful for contradicting the sunnah. And if he placed it (without throwing), it does not suffice because it is not stoning. Translation: Then the method of throwing a pebble is that he places the pebble on the back of his right thumb and uses the index finger for assistance. And the measure of stoning is that there be a distance of five cubits between the thrower and the place of falling. Thus Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa because less than that would be dropping. And if he dropped the pebble, it still suffices because he threw it towards his feet, but this person will be sinful due to contradicting the sunnah. And if he placed the pebble (without throwing), it does not suffice because it is not stoning. Explanation: Describing the method of stoning, it is stated that he places the pebble on the back of his right thumb and with the help of the index finger throws it, and there should be a minimum distance of five cubits between the thrower and the place where the pebble falls. Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated this from Abu Hanifa. The proof is that with a lesser distance, the term 'throwing' does not apply; rather it is 'dropping,' whereas throwing pebbles is sunnah, not dropping. And if he deliberately dropped the pebble instead of throwing, it still suffices because he threw the pebble towards his feet, but he is sinful for acting against the sunnah. And if he placed the pebble (without throwing), it does not suffice because this is not stoning in any way.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage details the method of throwing pebbles during rami. The sunnah method, narrated by Hasan ibn Ziyad from Imam Abu Hanifa, is to place the pebble on the back of the right thumb and use the index finger to propel it. A minimum distance of five cubits (approx. 2.5 meters) between the thrower and the target is required, otherwise the action is considered 'dropping' (tarh) rather than 'throwing' (ramy). Dropping intentionally fulfills the obligation but incurs sin for abandoning the sunnah. Simply placing the pebble on the ground or near the jamrah does not count as stoning at all. The distinction between ramy (sunnah) and tarh (valid but sinful) is a precise Hanafi legal point.

Key Terms
طرح (tarh): Dropping the pebble without throwing force; distance less than five cubits.
رمی (ramy): Throwing with force, typically with a distance of at least five cubits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim places the pebble on the jamrah without throwing, what is the ruling?
A) It suffices as stoning
B) It does not suffice
C) It suffices but he is sinful
D) It is better than throwing

Key Takeaway
The sunnah method of stoning is a precise technique; dropping fulfills the obligation but is sinful; placing does not count as stoning.

Pebble Proximity and Stoning in Hajj: Two Rulings
Rulings on pebble landing proximity and multiple pebbles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on (1) when a pebble's landing near the jamrah suffices, and (2) the effect of throwing all seven pebbles together, and apply these rulings to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
A pebble must fall near the jamrah; throwing all seven at once counts as only one.

This passage covers two important practical points during the stoning ritual in Hajj. First, what if the pebble does not hit the jamrah directly but falls close? Second, what if a pilgrim throws all seven pebbles in one handful? The Hanafi school provides clear rulings based on the nature of the act and the difficulty of precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct rulings
Read the passage and separate the two issues: proximity of the pebble's landing, and throwing multiple pebbles together.
The passage uses 'ولَوْرَمَاهَا' and 'وَلَوْرَمَىٰ' to introduce each case.
2
Understand the rationale for proximity
The text says 'because it is unavoidable to this extent' (laa yumkin al-ihthiraz). This is a principle of ease (taysir) in worship.
The distance 'near' is not precisely defined; it is left to 'urf (custom).
3
Understand the rationale for multiple pebbles
The text says 'because what is prescribed is separate actions' (al-mansoos alayhi tafarruq al-af'al). The sunnah is to throw one by one; throwing together violates the prescribed manner.
This ruling applies even if the intention was to throw all seven.
4
Apply to scenarios
Consider variations: pebble lands exactly on jamrah (valid), lands far (invalid), lands near (valid). Throwing six together and one separately (only one count? Actually, the text says throwing seven together counts as one; applying analogy, throwing fewer than seven together would count as one throw for that group).
Stick to the text: only the scenario of all seven together is addressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جمرہ کے قریب گرنے والی کنکری کافی ہے
وَلَوْرَمَاهَا فَوَقَعَتْ قَرِيبًا مِّنَ الْجَمَرَةِ يَكفِيهِ لأَنَّ هَذَا الْقَدْرَ مِمَّا لَا يَمُكِنُ الْاتر از عَنهُ وَلَوْ وَقَعَتْ بَعِيد امِنْهَا لَا يُجْزِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُعْتَرَفُ قُرَبَةً إِلَّا فِي مَكَانٍ مَخصُوصِ وَلَوْرَمَى بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ جُمْلَةٌ فَهَذِهِ وَاحِدَةً لِأَنَّ الْمَنْصُوصَ عَلَيْهِ تَفَرَّقُ الْأَفْعَالِ
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے کنکری پھینکی پس وہ جمرہ سے نزدیک گری تو اس کو کافی ہے کیونکہ اس قدر سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے اور اگر وہ جمرہ سے دور گری تو کافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اسکا عبادت ہونا نہیں پہچانا گیا مگر ایک خاص جگہ میں اور اگر سات کنکریاں ایک ساتھ پھینکی تو وہ ایک کنکری شمار ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ منصوص علیہ تو جدا جدا فعل کرنا ہے۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
A pebble that falls near the jamrah is sufficient. And if he threw it and it fell close to the jamrah, it suffices him because it is unavoidable to this extent. And if it fell far from it, it does not suffice because it is not recognized as an act of worship except in a specific place. And if he threw seven pebbles all together, then that is counted as one (pebble) because what is prescribed is separate actions. Translation: And if he threw a pebble and it fell near the jamrah, it is sufficient for him because it is not possible to avoid (falling at exactly the jamrah) to this extent. And if it fell far from it, it does not suffice because its being an act of worship is not recognized except in a specific place. And if he threw seven pebbles all together, they will be counted as one pebble because what is prescribed is separate actions. Explanation: It is clear.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings regarding the stoning ritual. First, if the pebble lands close to the jamrah (i.e., within the immediate vicinity), the stoning is valid because it is difficult to aim precisely. However, if it lands far away, it does not count; the act of worship is only valid at the designated area around the jamrah. Second, throwing all seven pebbles at once counts only as one pebble. The prescribed sunnah is to throw them one by one, as separate actions. This emphasizes the importance of individual throws, and failing to do so reduces the count.

Key Terms
قريب (qarib): Near the jamrah; a distance that is considered unavoidable in practice.
بعيد (ba'id): Far from the jamrah; a distance that does not count as valid stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim throws a pebble that lands far from the jamrah, what is the ruling?
A) It suffices because he intended worship
B) It does not suffice because worship is only valid in a specific place
C) It suffices if he says 'Allahu Akbar'
D) It suffices only if the pebble was thrown with the right hand

Key Takeaway
For stoning in Hajj, a pebble must land near the jamrah; throwing all seven together counts as only one pebble.

Method of Stoning (Kamiyyah al-Rami)
Describes the proper technique for throwing pebbles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended method for stoning in Hajj and distinguish between valid (ramy, tarh) and invalid (wad') delivery.

Core Idea
A pebble must be thrown with force to travel five cubits; mere dropping sins but suffices; mere placement invalidates.

Stoning (ramy) is a pillar of Hajj, but its proper execution has detailed rulings. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the sunnah technique and what constitutes a valid delivery, distinguishing between throwing (ramy), dropping (tarh), and placing (wad'). Understanding these distinctions ensures one’s stoning is both valid and meritorious.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ramy (stoning). The described method is sunnah muakkadah; following it earns reward, while abandoning it without excuse incurs sin.
The method is not wajib; the stoning itself is wajib (or pillar) but the technique is sunnah.
2
Extract the sunnah method
Place the pebble on the back of the right thumb, use the index finger (musabbihah) to propel, and ensure a distance of five cubits between hand and landing spot.
This is the riwayah from Abu Hanifa through Hasan ibn Ziyad.
3
Understand the proof
The method is transmitted as a sunnah ahad from Abu Hanifa, establishing it as a preferred practice (zahir riwayah).
Zanni thubut and dalala, so the ruling is sunnah not wajib.
4
Analyze consequences of deviation
If one drops (tarh) the pebble without force, the stoning is still valid because the pebble reaches the jamrah, but the person sins for abandoning the sunnah. If one merely places (wad') the pebble, it does not constitute stoning and is invalid.
The key is whether the act is a 'throw' (ramy) or mere placement.
5
Apply to scenarios
Given a real scenario, classify the delivery as ramy, tarh, or wad' and state the ruling and sin status accordingly.
Use the five-cubit criterion as a guideline for ramy; tarh fails the distance but still suffices; wad' fails entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ كَيْفِيةُ الرَّمَى أَنْ يَضَعَ الْحِصَاةَ عَلَى ظَهَرا بَهَامِهِ الْيُمْنَى وَيَسْتَعِينُ بِالْمُسَحَةِ وَمِقْدَارُ الرَّمَى أَنْ يَكُونَ بَينَ الرَّمَى وَبَيْنَ مَوْضِع السُّقوطِ خَمْسَةَ أذرع كَذَا رَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِأَنَّ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ طَرُحًا وَلَوْ طَرَحَهَا طَرْحًا أَجْزَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ رَمَى إِلى قَدَمَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ، مُسِيُّ لِمُخَالِفَةِ السُّنَّةِ وَلَوْ وَضَعَهَا وَضُعَالَمْ يَجُرُهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ

ترجمہ پھر کنکری پھینک مارنے کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ کنکری کو اپنے دائیں انگوٹھے کی پشت پر رکھے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے مدد لے۔ اور رمی کی مقدار یہ ہے کہ پھینکنے والے اور گرنے کی جگہ کے درمیان پانچ ہاتھ کا فاصلہ ہو ۔ ایسا ہی حسن نے ابوحنیفہ سے روایت کیا ہے کیونکہ اس سے کم تو ڈال دینا ہو گا۔ اور اگر اس نے کنکری کو ڈال دیا تو بھی کافی ہے کیونکہ اس نے کنکری اپنے قدموں کی طرف پھینکی مگر یہ شخص مخالفت سنت کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے کنکری کو رکھ دیا تو کافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ میری نہیں ہے۔
Then the manner of stoning is that he places the pebble on the back of his right thumb and seeks help with the index finger. The distance of stoning is that between the thrower and the place of falling there be five cubits. Thus narrated al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, because less than that would be a drop. If he dropped it, it suffices him because he threw it towards his feet, except that he is a wrongdoer for opposing the sunnah. If he placed it as a placement, it does not set it as stoning because it is not.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage describes the recommended method (sunnah) for stoning in Hajj. The pebble should be placed on the back of the right thumb and propelled with the index finger. It must be thrown with force so that it travels at least five cubits (approximately 2.5 meters) from the hand to the landing spot. This distance ensures the act is considered 'ramy' (throwing) and not merely 'tarh' (dropping). Ibn Abi Hanifa's report from Abu Hanifa establishes this as the sunnah. If one drops the pebble intentionally, the stoning is still valid because the pebble reaches the jamrah area, but the person sins for abandoning the sunnah. If one simply places or rolls the pebble without throwing, it is invalid because it does not constitute stoning at all. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the physical act of throwing is essential; mere placement is insufficient.

Key Terms
رمى (ramy): The specific act of stoning with force and distance, not mere dropping.
طرح (tarh): Dropping the pebble without force, which suffices but is blameworthy.
مسحة (musahah): The index finger used as a slingshot to propel the pebble.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three cubits
B) Five cubits
C) Seven cubits
D) The distance from hand to ground

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for stoning requires thumb-index propulsion and five cubits; dropping suffices but sins, placing invalidates.

Ruling on Pebble Landing and Throwing All Pebbles Together
Rulings on where the pebble must land relative to the jamrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the required proximity of the pebble to the jamrah and on throwing all seven pebbles at once, and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each.

Core Idea
The pebble need only land near the jamrah; all seven thrown at once count as one.

Stoning the jamarat is a key rite of Hajj. But what if the pebble falls a bit short? What if you throw all pebbles together? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on these practical questions, based on the principle of unavoidability and the prescribed method of separate actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage addresses two separate rulings: (1) the effect of the pebble landing near or far from the jamrah, and (2) the ruling when all seven pebbles are thrown at once.
These are distinct but both relate to the validity of the stoning.
2
Analyze the ruling on proximity
The text states that if the pebble falls near the jamrah, it suffices, because avoiding such a small deviation is impossible. If it falls far, it does not suffice, because the act of devotion is only recognized at a specific place.
The term 'near' is not defined by a specific distance; it is left to what is unavoidable.
3
Analyze the ruling on grouping
If a person throws all seven pebbles in one go, it counts as only one pebble. The prescribed method is separate, distinct throws for each pebble.
This emphasizes that each pebble must be thrown individually.
4
Understand the ta'lil
The ruling on proximity is based on practical necessity ('this measure is unavoidable'). The ruling on grouping is based on the explicit prescription of separate actions.
The reasoning shows that the law takes into account both the impossibility of perfection and the requirement of intentional individual acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْرَمَاهَا فَوَقَعَتْ قَرِيبًا مِّنَ الْجَمَرَةِ يَكفِيهِ لأَنَّ هَذَا الْقَدْرَ مِمَّا لَا يَمُكِنُ الْاتر از عَنهُ وَلَوْ وَقَعَتْ بَعِيد امِنْهَا لَا يُجْزِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُعْتَرَفُ قُرَبَةً إِلَّا فِي مَكَانٍ مَخصُوصِ وَلَوْرَمَى بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ جُمْلَةٌ فَهَذِهِ وَاحِدَةً لِأَنَّ الْمَنْصُوصَ عَلَيْهِ تَفَرَّقُ الْأَفْعَالِ

ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے کنکری پھینکی پس وہ جمرہ سے نزدیک گری تو اس کو کافی ہے کیونکہ اس قدر سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے اور اگر وہ جمرہ سے دور گری تو کافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اسکا عبادت ہونا نہیں پہچانا گیا مگر ایک خاص جگہ میں اور اگر سات کنکریاں ایک ساتھ پھینکی تو وہ ایک کنکری شمار ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ منصوص علیہ تو جدا جدا فعل کرنا ہے۔
If he throws it and it falls near the jamrah, it suffices him because this measure is something unavoidable. If it falls far from it, it does not suffice him because it is not recognized as an act of devotion except in a specific place. If he throws seven pebbles as one, then it is one because what is prescribed is separate actions.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues. First, the required precision of stoning: if the pebble lands near the jamrah (within reasonable proximity), the stoning is valid because it is impossible to always hit exactly. However, if it falls far away, it is invalid because the stoning must occur in the designated area around the jamrah. Second, if a person throws all seven pebbles at once (e.g., in one handful), it counts as only one pebble, as the prescribed sunnah is to throw them one by one separately. Hanafi rulings emphasize that the act must be intentional and distinct; grouping invalidates the sequence.

Key Terms
جمرة (jamrah): The stone pillar(s) representing the devil; the stoning site.
قرب (qurb): Nearness; the text does not define a specific distance, but leaves it to what is unavoidable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It counts as seven valid throws.
B) It counts as one throw only.
C) It invalidates the stoning.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, stoning the jamrah is valid if the pebble lands in the general area (proximity suffices), and all seven pebbles must be thrown individually; grouping reduces the count to one.

Throwing Seven Pebbles at Once
Ruling on collective pebble throwing during stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on throwing multiple pebbles simultaneously during Hajj stoning and explain why only one throw is counted.

Core Idea
Throwing seven pebbles together counts as one — ritual actions require individual separation.

The stoning of the jamarat is a pillar of Hajj that demands precise performance. This ruling clarifies a common error: throwing multiple pebbles in one go does not satisfy the requirement. Understanding this protects the pilgrim from incomplete rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage addresses throwing seven pebbles simultaneously. The ruling: it counts as only one throw.
The act is part of ramy al-jamarat.
2
Locate the proof
The text states 'because what is prescribed is separate actions' — the sunnah (prophetic practice) mandates individual throws.
Dalil is the Sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ).
3
Determine the consequence
Since only one throw is counted, the pilgrim must repeat the remaining six throws separately.
The rite is not void but incomplete.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may deem grouping sufficient if the count is fulfilled. Hanafi position is stricter to preserve the sunnah form.
Cross-madhhab variance exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْرَمَى بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ جُمْلَةٌ فَهَذِهِ وَاحِدَةً لِأَنَّ الْمَنْصُوصَ عَلَيْهِ تَفَرَّقُ الْأَفْعَالِ

ترجمہ اور اگر سات کنکریاں ایک ساتھ پھینکی تو وہ ایک کنکری شمار ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ منصوص علیہ تو جدا جدا فعل کرنا ہے۔
If he throws seven pebbles as one, then it counts as one because what is prescribed is separate actions.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This brief ruling clarifies that the prescribed sunnah for stoning is to throw each pebble individually, with one throw per pebble. If a pilgrim throws all seven at once (e.g., in a handful), only one throw is counted. The remaining six are considered missed, so the pilgrim must repeat them. This emphasises the importance of intentional separate actions in the stoning ritual.

Key Terms
حصى (hasa): The pebbles used for stoning; plural of hasah.
جملة (jumlatan): Collectively, in one action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) One

Key Takeaway
Throwing pebbles in a single handful counts as one throw; each pebble must be thrown separately to fulfill the sunnah.

Taking Pebbles for Stoning: Makruh but Valid
Ruling on taking pebbles for stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking pebbles from near the jamrah and explain why the stoning remains valid.

Core Idea
Pebbles near the jamrah are makruh to use but still valid if cast.

This passage addresses a specific detail of Hajj: where to obtain the pebbles for stoning the jamarat. While the general rule allows any source, the text cautions against taking pebbles directly from near the jamrah itself. We will examine the ruling, its basis in tradition, and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Note that the text begins with a general permission: 'He takes pebbles from any place he wishes'.
This establishes the default permissibility.
2
Locate the Exception
The exception is 'except from near the jamrah', which is ruled as makruh (disliked).
The dislike is based on an athar (tradition).
3
Understand the Reasoning
The reason given is that those pebbles are 'rejected' (mardud) and considered inauspicious.
This is from the athar; it does not affect validity.
4
Assess the Consequence of Violation
The text explicitly states that even if one uses such pebbles, the stoning suffices (ajza'ahu).
This shows that valid (sahih) is distinct from disliked (makruh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَأْخُذُ الحِصى من أي موضع شَاءَ إِلَّا مِنْ عِنْدِ الْجَمُرَةِ فَإِن ذَلِكَ يَكْرَهُ لِأَنَّ مَا عِندَهَا مِنَ الْحِطَى مَرْدُودُ هكَذَا جَاءَ فِي الْأَثَر فَيُتشَامُ بِهِ وَمَعَ هَذَا لَوْ فَعَلَ أَجْزَاهُ لِوُجُودِ فَعَلِ الرَّمَى

ترجمہ اور کنکریاں جس جگہ سے چاہے لیوے سوائے جمرہ کے پاس کے کہ یہ مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ جمرہ کے پاس جو کنکریاں ہیں مردود ہیں یونہی اثر میں آیا ہے میں اس کے لینے میں نحوست شمار ہوگی ۔ اور اس کے باوجود اگر اس نے کیا تو کافی ہو گیا کیونکہ پھینکنے کا فعل پایا گیا۔
He takes pebbles from any place he wishes except from near the jamrah, for that is disliked because the pebbles near it are rejected; thus it came in the athar, so he considers them inauspicious. Despite this, if he does it, it suffices him because the act of stoning exists.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage permits collecting pebbles from any location for stoning, but it is makruh (disliked) to take them from directly near the jamrah itself. The reason is that those pebbles are considered 'rejected' (mardud)—possibly because they were thrown by pilgrims whose Hajj may not have been accepted. The tradition (athar) indicates that taking such pebbles is inauspicious. However, if one does use them, the stoning is still valid because the essential act of throwing is fulfilled. Hanafi fiqh balances ritual caution with practical validity.

Key Terms
أثر (athar): A tradition from the Companions or early scholars, not necessarily a marfu' hadith.
مردود (mardud): Rejected; stones of rejected Hajj, considered inauspicious.
تشأم (tasha'um): To consider something as a bad omen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Haram and invalid
B) Makruh but valid if done
C) Sunnah to do so
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
Taking pebbles from near the jamrah is disliked but does not invalidate the stoning.

Permissible Material for Stoning: Earth Components vs. Stone
Dispute with Shafi'i regarding stoning with earth vs. stone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on permissible stoning materials and explain the talil that distinguishes throwing from scattering.

Core Idea
Any earth component suffices for stoning; gold and silver scatter, not throw.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani explains the Hanafi view that any natural earth material can be used for stoning during Hajj, opposing Imam al-Shafi'i who restricts it to stones. The key distinction lies in the purpose: the act of throwing (ramy) versus mere scattering (nathr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Stoning (rami) is a wajib act of Hajj. The issue here is what material is permissible for this act.
The hukm is about the permissibility of the substance, not the act itself.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafi school, any component of the earth (ajza' al-ard) is permissible, including stone, clay, dirt, and sand.
The text says 'indana' (according to us), emphasizing it's the school's view.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts stoning to stones only, citing practice (athar).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both views are based on evidence.
4
Understand the talil (ratiocination)
The intended aim is the act of throwing (ramy) with force. Any earth material can be thrown; gold and silver cannot be thrown with force and instead scatter (nathr), thus not fulfilling the purpose.
This qiyas-based reasoning shows the Hanafi emphasis on the underlying purpose (maqsud).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ بِكُلِّ مَا كَانَ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ الْأَرْضِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ فِعْلُ الرَّمْيِ وَذَلِكَ يَحْصِلُ بِالطَّيِّنِ كَمَا يَحصلُ بِالْحَجَرِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا رَمَى بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ لأنَّه يُسمَّى نَشْرًا لَاَرْمِيَّا

ترجمہ اور ہمارے نزدیک ہر اس چیز کے ساتھ رمی کرنا جائز ہے جو زمین کی جنس سے ہو۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے کیونکہ اصل مقصود تو پھینکے کا فعل ہے اور یہ جیسے پتھر سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اسی طرح مٹی سے حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے جبکہ سونے یا چاندی کے ساتھ ری کی۔ کیونکہ یہ بکھیر نا کہلائے گا نہ کہ پھینک کر مارنا۔
It is permissible with everything that is from the components of the earth according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the intended aim is the act of throwing, and that is achieved with clay just as it is achieved with stone, unlike if he threw with gold and silver because that is called scattering, not throwing.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school (our school) holds that any substance that is part of the earth—such as clay, dirt, or stone—may be used for stoning (rami). The essential element is the act of throwing (ramy), which all such materials fulfill. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to stones only, citing practice (athar). The Hanafi response reasons that clay or dried mud clods can be thrown with force just like stones. However, using gold or silver is impermissible because it is considered scattering (nathr), not the intended forcible throwing. This ruling highlights the Hanafi emphasis on the underlying purpose (maqsud) over the specific substance, applying istihsan.

Key Terms
أجزاء الأرض (ajza' al-ard): Components of the earth: stone, clay, dirt, sand, etc.
نشر/نثر (nathr): Scattering, not throwing with force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only stones
B) Any earth component including clay
C) Any metal
D) Only pebbles from Mina

Key Takeaway
In stoning, the substance matters: earth components fulfill the act of throwing; gold and silver do not.

Order of Rituals on Yawm al-Nahr for the Mufrid
Prescribed sequence: stoning, then sacrifice, then shaving/trimming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed order of rituals on Yawm al-Nahr for the Mufrid, explain the evidence from hadith, and identify which ritual is optional and why.

Core Idea
Stoning first, then sacrifice (optional for Mufrid), then shaving – a sequence based on hadith and reasoned precedence.

On Yawm al-Nahr, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the pilgrim performs a specific sequence of rites: stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba, then sacrificing an animal (if applicable), then shaving or trimming the hair. This order is derived from the Prophet's own practice and command, as recorded in a hadith. However, this passage focuses on the Mufrid – the pilgrim performing Hajj only – and clarifies that for him, the sacrifice is supererogatory, not obligatory. Understanding this sequence and its evidence helps the pilgrim follow the sunnah correctly and avoid unnecessary compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses the order of three acts on Yawm al-Nahr: stoning, sacrificing, and shaving/trimming. Determine the ruling level for the Mufrid: stoning is wajib, sacrificing is optional (tatavvu'), shaving is wajib as part of tahlil.
The sacrifice for the Mufrid is not wajib; it becomes wajib only for Qarin and Mutamatti.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from the Prophet: 'Indeed the first of our rites on this day is that you stone, then we slaughter, then you shave.' This is a clear textual evidence for the order.
The hadith is considered mutawatir in meaning, so its transmission is certain (qat'i al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'tarumi' (you stone) indicates an obligatory sequence according to Hanafi usul; the command implies order. However, the Hanafi school categorizes the order as sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, because breaking it does not invalidate the rites but requires compensation.
The word 'thumma' (then) in the hadith denotes sequence, but the level of obligation is derived from other evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All major schools agree on this order generally. The passage focuses on the Hanafi perspective, especially the nuance that the Mufrid's sacrifice is optional.
The Hanafi position is consistent with the literal text, but the permissibility of optional sacrifice is a distinctive point.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the order is sunnah muakkadah; if reversed, the later act is valid but makruh and may necessitate a dam (compensation). The sacrifice for the Mufrid is not wajib because the primary obligation (on the Qarin and Mutamatti) is based on other proofs.
The rationale: stoning begins tahlil (partial release), shaving completes it. Since shaving is a prohibited act during ihram, sacrifice is offered before it to avoid performing a prohibited act while still in ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَذْبَحُ إِنْ أَحَبَّ لَمَارُوتَ ثُمَّ يَحْلِقُ أَوْ يَقْصِرُ لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ إِنَّ أَوَّلَ نُسُكِنَا يَوْمَنَا هَذَا أَن تَرْمِي ثُمَّ نَذْبَحْ ثُمَّ تَحْلِقُ وَلانَّ الحَلَقَ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ التَّحَلَّلِ وَكَذَا الذَّبْحُ حَتَّى يَتَعَلَّلُ بِهِ الْمُحْصِرُ فَيُقَدَّمُ الرَّمَى عَلَيْهِمَا ثُمَّ الْعَلَّقِ مِنْ مَحْظُورَاتِ الْإِحْرَامِ فَيُقَدَّمُ عَلَيْهِ الذَّبْحُ وَإِنَّمَا عَلَّقَ الدَّبَّحَ بِالْمَحَبَةِ لِأَنَّ الدَّمَ الَّذِى يَأْتِي بِهِ الْمُفَرِدُ تُطَوَّعَ وَالْكَلَامُ فِى الْمُفْرِدِ

ترجمہ وہ ذبح کرے اگر چاہے پھر حلق کرے یا قصر کرے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جس میں ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ پہلی قربانی ہماری اس دن کے یہ ہے کہ تم رمی کرو پھر ذبح کرو پھر حلق کرو۔ اور اس لئے کہ حلق تحلیل کے اسباب میں سے ہے اور اسی طرح ذبح ہے یہاں تک کہ محصر اسی کے ساتھ متحلل ہوتا ہے تو رمی کو ان دونوں پر مقدم کیا جائے گا اور اس لئے کہ حلق محظورات احرام میں سے ہے تو اس پر ذبح مقدم کیا جائے گا اور ذبح کو مشیت کے ساتھ معلق کیا اس لئے کہ مفرد جو خون لاتا ہے وہ تطوع ہے اور کلام مفرد میں ہے۔
He slaughters if he wishes, then shaves or trims, due to what is narrated from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'Indeed the first of our rites on this day is that you stone, then we slaughter, then you shave.' And because shaving is among the causes of tahlil, and similarly slaughtering, such that the muhsar (blocked person) becomes halal with it. Thus stoning is advanced over both. Then shaving is among the prohibitions of ihram, so slaughtering is advanced over it. He linked slaughtering to 'if he wishes' because the blood that the mufrid brings is supererogatory, and the discussion is about the mufrid.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage establishes the order of rituals on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) for the Mufrid (one performing Hajj only, not Qiran or Tamattu). The sequence is: (1) Stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba, (2) Sacrifice (although it is supererogatory for the Mufrid, hence 'if he wishes'), (3) Shaving or trimming the hair. The proof is a hadith from the Prophet commanding this order. The rationale: stoning is the first act of tahlil (partial release from ihram). Then shaving/trimming completes tahlil, but since shaving is a prohibited act (mahzur) during ihram, the sacrifice is performed before it. However, for the Mufrid, the sacrifice is optional (tatavvu'). The Hanafi school holds that the sacrifice is not wajib for the Mufrid; it becomes wajib only for the Qarin and Mutamatti. Thus the passage uses 'if he wishes' to indicate its voluntary nature.

Key Terms
مفرد (mufrid): Person performing Hajj only (not Qiran/Tamattu).
تحلل (tahlil): Release from ihram; partial by stoning, complete by shaving.
محظورات الإحرام (mahzurat al-ihram): Prohibited acts during ihram; shaving is one.

Key Takeaway
On Yawm al-Nahr, the Mufrid should stone first, then may optionally sacrifice, then shave; the order is based on prophetic command and the logic of tahlil.

Where to Collect Pebbles for Ramy
Ruling on permissible location for taking ramy pebbles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on taking pebbles for ramy from near the jamrah and explain why the act remains valid despite being makruh.

Core Idea
Pebbles from near the jamrah are makruh but the ramy is valid – the essential act suffices.

When performing the stoning ritual (ramy) during Hajj, the pilgrim needs seven pebbles. The Hanafi school specifies that while pebbles may be taken from any location, it is disliked to collect them from directly around the stoning pillar. This ruling balances a reported tradition with the principle that the core action determines validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is taking pebbles for ramy. The ruling: permissible from anywhere except near the jamrah, where it is makruh. Identify the explicit permission and the exception.
2
Understand the reason for karahah
The reason given is that pebbles near the jamrah are 'rejected' (mardud), based on a tradition (athar). This implies they are from a hajj that was not accepted, so using them is ill-omened.
Understand that this karahah is tanzihi (disliked, not sinful).
3
Analyze the consequence if done
Despite the karahah, if the pilgrim takes pebbles from that spot and performs ramy, the act is valid. The text says 'yujzi'uhu' (it suffices him). Why? Because the essential action of throwing is achieved.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that the validity of an act depends on fulfilling its essentials (arkan), not on recommended or disliked elements.
4
Locate the dalil and its authority
The proof is a tradition (athar) – a hadith that is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut. The karahah is based on this, while the validity is based on general principles.
The dalil is not strong enough to render the act invalid, only disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَأْخُذُ الحِصى من أي موضع شَاءَ إِلَّا مِنْ عِنْدِ الْجَمُرَةِ فَإِن ذَلِكَ يَكْرَهُ لِأَنَّ مَا عِندَهَا مِنَ الْحِطَى مَرْدُودُ هكَذَا جَاءَ فِي الْأَثَر فَيُتشَامُ بِهِ وَمَعَ هَذَا لَوْ فَعَلَ أَجْزَاهُ لِوُجُودِ فَعَلِ الرَّمَى
He takes the pebbles from any place he wishes except from near the jamrah, for that is disliked because the pebbles near it are rejected; thus it has come in the athar (tradition), so it is considered inauspicious. Yet despite this, if he did it, it suffices him due to the existence of the act of ramy.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on where to collect pebbles for ramy (the stoning ritual). According to the Hanafi school, it is permissible to take pebbles from any location, except it is makruh (disliked) to take them from directly near the jamrah. The reason is that the pebbles that land near the jamrah are considered 'rejected' (mardud), based on a tradition (athar) that indicates such pebbles are from those whose hajj was not accepted, so using them carries a negative connotation. However, if someone does take pebbles from that spot and performs the ramy, the act is still valid (yujzi'uhu) because the essential action of throwing (ramy) has been fulfilled. The commentator (Imam al-Quduri) explains that the goal is the act of throwing itself, and since that is achieved, the ritual is complete. This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle that the validity of an act depends on the fulfillment of its essential elements (arkan), even if a recommended or disliked element is present.

Key Terms
حصى (hasā): Pebbles used for ramy (stoning) during Hajj.
جمرة (jamrah): The stoning pillar; specifically Jamrat al-Aqabah in this context.
مردود (mardūd): Rejected; pebbles that have been thrown and are considered from those whose hajj was not accepted.

Permissible Materials for Ramy: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the material used for ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits ramy with any part of the earth and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ramy is valid with any earth material because the objective is the act of throwing.

In this lesson, we examine a legal disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the material used for the ramy (stoning) ritual during Hajj. While both agree that stones are valid, the Hanafi school extends permissibility to any natural earth substance, such as clay or dirt. The proof revolves around the objective (maqsūd) of the ritual versus transmitted practice (athar).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school permits ramy with anything that is part of the earth, except gold and silver.
This is based on the principle that the objective is the act of throwing.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts ramy to stones only.
Shafi'is rely on the transmitted practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument is based on ittibā' al-athar: following the reported practice which was limited to stones.
No explicit prohibition of other materials in the Sunnah.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the objective is the act of ramy, which is achieved equally with any earth material.
They use qiyas based on the maqsūd to extend the ruling beyond the literal practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis consider ramy with clay/dirt valid; Shafi'is require repetition with stones.
This affects the validity of the ritual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ بِكُلِّ مَا كَانَ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ الْأَرْضِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ فِعْلُ الرَّمْيِ وَذَلِكَ يَحْصِلُ بِالطَّيِّنِ كَمَا يَحصلُ بِالْحَجَرِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا رَمَى بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ لأنَّه يُسمَّى نَشْرًا لَاَرْمِيَّا
And it is permissible with everything that is from parts of the earth according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the objective is the act of ramy, and that is achieved with clay just as it is achieved with stone, unlike if he throws with gold and silver, because that is called scattering (nashr), not ramy.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the material used for ramy during Hajj. According to the Hanafi school, it is permissible to throw any substance that is a part of the earth (ajzā' al-arḍ), such as stones, clods of dirt, or dried clay. This is opposite to Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts ramy to stones only. The Hanafi evidence is based on the objective (maqsūd) of the act: the purpose is the act of throwing (ramy) itself, and this is achieved with any earth material in the same manner as with stone. Therefore, there is equal validity. However, the Hanafis exclude gold and silver because throwing such valuables is considered scattering (nashr) rather than the specific act of ramy intended in the ritual. The commentator explains that Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is following the reported practice (ittibā' al-athar), while the Hanafis rely on the rational extension of the objective (qiyas based on the maqsūd). This illustrates the methodological difference between the schools in deriving rulings from the Sunnah.

Key Terms
أجزاء الأرض (ajzā' al-arḍ): Literally 'parts of the earth', meaning natural earth materials like stone, clay, dirt.
رمي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat during Hajj.
نشر (nashr): Scattering; used for throwing gold/silver which is not considered ramy.

Order of Rites: Ramy, then Sacrifice, then Shaving
Ruling with proof on the recommended sequence of Hajj rites after ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of rites on Yawm al-Nahr and explain why the sequence is sunnah, not wajib, citing the prophetic hadith and rational reasoning.

Core Idea
The order of ramy, sacrifice, then shaving is sunnah; reversing does not invalidate the rites.

On the Day of Sacrifice, a pilgrim performing Hajj al-Ifrad completes the ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah and then performs sacrifice and shaving. This lesson examines the recommended sequence based on the Prophet's instruction and the underlying legal reasoning. Understanding the distinction between sunnah and wajib in this context is crucial for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sequence of rites (ramy, sacrifice, shaving) on Yawm al-Nahr. The Hanafi ruling is that the order is sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
Sunnah means the act is meritorious but omission does not require compensation or repetition.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith: 'The first of our rites this day is that you throw (ramy), then we sacrifice, then you shave.' This is a sunnah ahad (single-chain narration).
The hadith provides textual evidence for the order.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement is informative and directive. In Hanafi usul, the imperative form (ulf) indicates recommendation (nadb) when there is no qarinah (context) requiring obligation. Here, the context of ease and the absence of explicit penalty for reversal make the order sunnah.
Other schools may interpret the imperative as wajib, but Hanafis rely on additional proofs.
4
Understand the rational reasoning (ta'lil)
The commentator provides rational reasoning: ramy is given precedence because it is the first act of tahlul; sacrifice is placed before shaving because shaving involves violating a prohibition of ihram, so the worship (sacrifice) precedes it.
This ta'lil strengthens the recommendation but does not elevate it to wajib.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a pilgrim reverses the order (e.g., sacrifices before ramy), the rites are still valid but the sunnah is missed. In schools that consider the order wajib, the sacrifice might need to be repeated (if done before ramy) or the pilgrim incurs a penalty.
The Hanafi position provides ease for the pilgrim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَذْبَحُ إِنْ أَحَبَّ لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ إِنَّ أَوَّلَ نُسُكِنَا يَوْمَنَا هَذَا أَن تَرْمِي ثُمَّ نَذْبَحْ ثُمَّ تَحْلِقُ وَلأَنَّ الْحَلَقَ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ التَّحَلُّلِ وَكَذَا الذَّبْحُ حَتَّى يَتَحَلَّلَ بِهِ الْمُحْصِرُ فَيُقَدَّمُ الرَّمْيُ عَلَيْهِمَا ثُمَّ الْحَلَقُ مِنْ مَحْظُورَاتِ الْإِحْرَامِ فَيُقَدَّمُ عَلَيْهِ الذَّبْحُ وَإِنَّمَا عُلِّقَ الذَّبْحُ بِالْمَحَبَّةِ لِأَنَّ الدَّمَ الَّذِي يَأْتِي بِهِ الْمُفْرِدُ تَطَوُّعٌ وَالْكَلَامُ فِي الْمُفْرِدِ
He sacrifices if he wishes, based on what was narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Indeed, the first of our rites this day is that you throw (ramy), then we sacrifice, then you shave.' And because shaving is among the causes of tahlul (becoming halal), and likewise sacrifice, such that the one prevented (muhsar) becomes halal through it. So ramy is given precedence over both. Then shaving is among the prohibitions of ihram, so sacrifice is given precedence over it. And the sacrifice is made conditional on desire because the blood that the mufrid (performer of Hajj ifrad) brings is voluntary, and the discussion is about the mufrid.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage outlines the recommended sequence of rites on the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) for a pilgrim performing Hajj al-Ifrad. According to the Hanafi school, after completing the ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah, the pilgrim may perform the sacrifice (dhabh) if he wishes, then shave or trim his hair. The proof is from the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) who said: 'The first of our rites this day is that you throw, then we sacrifice, then you shave.' The commentator provides additional rational reasoning: both shaving and sacrifice are means of achieving tahlul (exiting the state of ihram). The muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj) becomes halal through sacrifice. Since ramy is the first act of tahlul, it is given precedence. Between sacrifice and shaving, sacrifice is given precedence because shaving involves violating a prohibition of ihram (cutting hair), so the sacrifice, which is a form of worship, is performed first. The phrase 'if he wishes' indicates that the sacrifice is voluntary for the mufrid (one performing Hajj al-Ifrad) because the animal he brings is a voluntary offering (tatattu'), not obligatory. The text specifies that the discussion is about the mufrid.

Key Terms
تحلل (taḥallul): Exiting the state of ihram; becoming permitted what was prohibited.
محصر (muḥṣar): A pilgrim prevented from completing Hajj due to illness, enemy, etc.
مفرد (mufrid): One performing Hajj al-Ifrad (Hajj only, without 'Umrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred order of rites on Yawm al-Nahr for a mufrid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Shave, then sacrifice, then throw pebbles.
B) Throw pebbles, then sacrifice, then shave or trim.
C) Sacrifice, then throw pebbles, then shave.
D) Only throw pebbles and shave, no sacrifice needed.

Key Takeaway
The preferred order is ramy, then sacrifice, then shaving, but each rite remains valid even if the sequence is altered, as the order is only sunnah.

Shaving (Halq) is Preferred Over Trimming (Taqsir)
Ruling with proof for superiority of shaving over trimming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school considers shaving (halq) superior to trimming (taqsir) in Hajj tahlul, and identify the minimum amount of head that must be shaved for halq to be valid.

Core Idea
Shaving the head is more complete in removing ihram's restrictions, and the Prophet's prayer for those who shave proves its virtue.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the preferred method of tahlul after completing Hajj. While both shaving and trimming are permissible, the Hanafi school teaches that shaving carries greater reward. The proof draws from a well-known hadith and a rational analogy to washing. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate how the school weighs textual evidence (dalil naqli) and reasoned expedience (ma'qul) in deriving fiqh preferences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tahlul after Hajj: shaving (halq) vs trimming (taqsir). The ruling is that shaving is afdal (more virtuous).
2
Locate the dalil naqli
The hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prays for those who shave, repeating it three times.
The exact wording: 'Rahim Allah al-muhalliqin' (May Allah have mercy on those who shave).
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's repeated prayer for mercy indicates special virtue for those who shave, implying it is better than trimming.
This is a zanni dalala (probative indication) because it urges but does not command.
4
Examine the rational proof (talil)
Shaving more completely removes tafath (the state of prohibition). The text draws an analogy: like ghusl (full bath) is more thorough than wudu, so shaving is more complete than trimming.
5
Note the minimum requirement
For shaving to be valid, at least a quarter of the head must be shaved. This is derived by analogy from the quarter required in wiping the head (mash) during wudu.
Shaving the whole head is better (awla) in emulation of the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْحَلقُ أَفْضَلُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: رَحِمَ اللَّهُ الْمُحَلِقِينَ، قَالَهُ ثَلَاثًا، الْحَدِيثُ ظَاهِرٌ بِالرَّحْمَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَلِأَنَّ الْحَلَقَ أَكْمَلُ فِي قَضَاءِ التَّفَثِ وَهُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ، وَفِي التَّقْصِيرِ بَعْضُ التَّقْصِيرِ، فَأَشْبَهَ الِاغْتِسَالَ مَعَ الْوُضُوءِ. وَيَكْتَفِي فِي الْحَلْقِ بِرُبْعِ الرَّأْسِ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْمَسْحِ، وَحَلْقُ الْكُلِّ أَوْلَى اقْتِدَاءً بِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ. وَالتَّقْصِيرُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنْ رُءُوسِ شَعْرِهِ مِقْدَارَ الْأَنْمُلَةِ.
And shaving is better, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'May Allah have mercy on those who shave.' He said it three times. The hadith is clear in mercy upon them. And because shaving is more complete in removing the filth (tafath), and that is the objective. And in trimming there is some shortcoming, so it resembles bathing (ghusl) with wudu. And one suffices in shaving with a quarter of the head, by analogy with wiping (mash). And shaving all (the head) is better, following the example of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And trimming is that he takes from the tips of his hair the amount of a fingertip.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage establishes that shaving the entire head (halq) is superior (afḍal) to trimming the hair (taqsir) for the tahlul of Hajj. Two proofs are given: First, the hadith in which the Prophet (PBUH) prayed for mercy three times for those who shave, indicating their virtue. Second, rational reasoning: the purpose of removing tafath (remaining dirt/uncleanliness from ihram) is more completely achieved by shaving, which removes all hair, whereas trimming leaves some hair. This is similar to how ghusl (full bath) is more comprehensive than wudu (ablution). The commentator also notes that in shaving, it is sufficient to shave a quarter of the head, analogizing to the rule of wiping the head in wudu (which is wajib over a quarter). However, shaving the entire head is better (awla) in emulation of the Prophet. Finally, trimming (taqsir) is defined as cutting the length of a fingertip from the ends of the hair. This ruling applies to men; for women, the sunnah is to trim the length of a fingertip.

Key Terms
حلق (ḥalq): Shaving the head completely (for men) as part of tahlul.
قصر (taqsīr): Trimming the hair; cutting the length of a fingertip from the ends.
تفث (tafath): The filth and remaining prohibitions of ihram that are removed by shaving/trimming.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of the head that must be shaved for halq to be valid?
A) The entire head.
B) One quarter of the head.
C) Half of the head.
D) Three strands of hair.

Key Takeaway
Shaving the head (halq) is more virtuous than trimming (taqsir) because the Prophet prayed for those who shave and because it removes tafath more completely; a quarter of the head is the minimum for halq.

The Recommended Order of Rites on Yawm al-Nahr
States the recommended sequence of Hajj rites after ramy al-jamrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sequence of ramy, dhabh, and halq on the Day of Nahr, and explain why the order is sunnah rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Ramy then dhabh then halq is the sunnah order; reversing does not invalidate the Hajj.

On the Day of Nahr, a pilgrim performs multiple rites: throwing at Jamrat al-Aqabah, sacrificing an animal (if applicable), and shaving or trimming the head. The Hanafi school prescribes a recommended sequence based on the Prophet's ﷺ own practice and a rational analysis of the causes of tahlil (exiting ihram). This lesson unpacks that sequence and its legal weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rites
List the three main actions: ramy (throwing at Jamrat al-Aqabah), dhabh (sacrifice), and halq/taqsir (shaving/trimming).
For a mufrid bil-hajj, sacrifice is nafl (optional); for mutamatti' and qarin, it is wajib.
2
State the recommended order
According to the Hanafi school, the preferred order is: 1) ramy, 2) dhabh, 3) halq. This is established by the Prophet's ﷺ statement and his practice.
The order is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
3
Analyze the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Today our first rite is ramy, then sacrifice, then shaving.' The Hanafi school understands this as indicating sunnah, not wujub, because the imperative is overridden by other evidence that the acts are valid in any order.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut, so it does not impose wujub.
4
Understand the rational reasoning
Ramy is not a direct cause of tahlil (it does not remove ihram), whereas dhabh and halq both contribute to tahlil. Among the latter two, halq directly removes a prohibition of ihram, so dhabh is performed before halq to avoid delaying the removal of that prohibition. Ramy precedes both because it is not a cause of tahlil.
This reasoning is based on qiyas and istihsan.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some other schools consider the order wajib, meaning if reversed, the acts are invalid or require blood. The Hanafi school maintains that the order is sunnah, and the Hajj is valid even if the sequence is changed.
The practical difference: Hanafis do not require dam for reversing the order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ کہا کہ پھر اگر اس کا جی چاہے تو ذبح کرے پھر حلق کرے یا قصر کرے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ آج کے دن پہلا نسک ہمارا یہ ہے کہ ہم رمی کریں پھر قربانی کریں پھر حلق کریں اور اس لئے کہ سرمنڈانا احترام سے نکلنے کے اسباب سے ہے اور یونہی قربانی کرنا بھی حتی کہ جو شخص احرام باندھ کر ادائے احرام سے روکا گیا وہ قربانی سے حلال ہو جاتا ہے تو رمی کو ان دونوں پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ پھر حلق کرنا احترام کے ممنوعات سے ہے اس لئے حلق پر قربانی کرنا مقدم کیا جائے گا ۔ اور قربانی کو چاہنے پر اس لئے معلق کیا گیا ہے کہ قربانی جو تنہا مج والا کرتا ہے وہ فضل ہے اور کلام مفرد بالمج کے بارے میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کے بعد اگر جی چاہے تو قربانی کرلے پھر سر منڈا دے یا بال کٹا دے۔ دلیل یہ ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ آج کے دن یعنی یوم نحر میں پہلا نسک یہ ہے کہ ہم رمی کریں پھر قربانی کریں۔ پھر حلق کریں ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق احترام سے نکلنے کے اسباب میں سے ہے اور قربانی کرنا بھی اسباب تحلل سے ہے۔ چنانچہ محصر قربانی کرنے سے حلال ہو جاتا ہے پس جب حلق اور قربانی کرنا دونوں اسباب محلل سے ہیں تو رمی کرنے کو دونوں پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ پھر حلق چونکہ ممنوعات احرام میں سے ہے اس لئے ذبح کو اس پر مقدم کیا جائے گا اور قربانی کرنے کو چاہنے پر معلق اس لئے کیا گیا ہے کہ مفرد بالمج جو قربانی کرتا ہے وہ نفل ہوتی ہے نہ کہ واجب۔ اور اس وقت کلام مفرد بالمج ہی کے سلسلہ میں ہے۔
Translation: He said: Then if he wishes, he may slaughter, then shave or trim, because it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ that he said: 'Today, our first rite is that we do ramy, then sacrifice, then shave.' And because shaving the head is from the causes of leaving ihram, and similarly sacrificing, so much so that one who is hindered from performing ihram becomes halal by sacrificing. So ramy is given precedence over both. Then shaving is among the prohibitions of ihram, so sacrifice is given precedence over shaving. And sacrifice is made contingent on desire because the sacrifice performed by a mufrid bil-hajj is nafl (supererogatory), not wajib, and the discussion here concerns the mufrid bil-hajj. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said: After ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah, if he wishes, he may sacrifice, then shave his head or trim his hair. The proof is that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Today, on the day of Nahr, our first rite is that we do ramy, then sacrifice, then shave.' The second proof is that shaving is among the causes of exiting ihram, and sacrifice is also among the causes of tahlil. Thus, the muhsar becomes halal by sacrificing. So when both shaving and sacrificing are causes of tahlil, ramy is given precedence over both. Then, since shaving is among the prohibitions of ihram, slaughtering is given precedence over it. And sacrificing is made contingent on desire because the sacrifice performed by a mufrid bil-hajj is nafl, not wajib, and the discourse here is specifically concerning the mufrid bil-hajj.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended order of acts on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah) for a pilgrim performing Hajj. The base text from al-Quduri states that after throwing the pebbles at Jamrat al-Aqabah, the pilgrim may, if he wishes, sacrifice an animal, then shave or trim his hair. The commentator explains that this order is established by the Prophet's ﷺ own practice as narrated in hadith: first ramy, then sacrifice, then shaving. The rationale is both textual and rational: ramy is not itself a cause of tahlil but precedes the other acts; shaving and sacrifice both cause partial tahlil, but shaving directly removes a prohibition of ihram, so sacrifice is done before shaving to avoid delaying the shaving after the sacrifice. The passage also clarifies that for a mufrid (one performing only Hajj, not Umrah), the sacrifice is nafl (supererogatory), not wajib, so it is optional and the ruling is conditional on his wish. This order is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory; if one reverses the order, it is still valid but contrary to the sunnah.

Key Terms
رمی (ramy): Throwing pebbles at the Jamarat, specifically Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr.
قربانی (qurbani): Sacrificing an animal; for a mufrid bil-hajj, it is nafl (supererogatory).
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely.
محصر (muhsar): One who is prevented from completing Hajj due to enemy or illness, etc.
مفرد بالمج (mufrid bil-hajj): One who performs only Hajj, not combined with Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mubah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends the sequence ramy → dhabh → halq on Yawm al-Nahr, but considers it sunnah; reversal does not invalidate the Hajj or require compensation.

Superiority of Shaving (Halq) over Trimming (Taqsir)
Proves that shaving (halq) is superior to trimming (taqsir) using hadith and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds shaving (halq) to be superior to trimming (taqsir) for exiting ihram, and apply the minimum requirement of one-quarter shaving.

Core Idea
Shaving (halq) is superior to trimming (taqsir) because it fully removes tafath and the Prophet ﷺ prayed three times for those who shave.

The question of whether to shave or trim the head when exiting ihram is a practical issue for every pilgrim. This passage from the Hanafi tradition provides the proof for why shaving is considered better. We will examine the primary evidence from the hadith and the logical analogy (qiyas) that supports this preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the shaving or trimming of the head to exit ihram. The Hanafi ruling is that shaving (halq) is superior (afdal) but both are valid.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith in Sahihayn where the Prophet ﷺ said three times 'O Allah, have mercy on those who shave' and once for those who trim.
The repetition indicates greater merit for shaving.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The triple du'a for those who shave compared to the single du'a for those who trim shows that shaving is more meritorious in the sight of Allah.
This is a clear indication of preference (afdaliyyah).
4
Consider the secondary analogy
The passage also uses an analogy: just as ghusl (full bath) is superior to wudu (partial wash) because it achieves greater cleanliness, halq is superior to taqsir because it completely removes tafath.
The analogy reinforces the primary evidence.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'is consider taqsir equal or even better, but the Hanafi school maintains that halq is superior based on the stronger evidence.
The practical difference is in merit, not validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْحَلْقُ أَفْضَلُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَحِمَ اللَّهُ الْمُحَلِقِينَ قَالَهُ ثَلَاثًا لِمَا الْحَدِيثُ ظَاهِرٌ بِالرَّحْمَةِ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلِأَنَّ الْحَلْقَ أَكْمَلُ فِى قَضَاءِ التَّفَثِ وَهُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ وَ فِى التَّقْصِيرِ بَعْضُ التَّقْصِيرِ فَأَشْبَهَ الْغُسْلَ مَعَ الْوُضُوءِ وَيَكْتَفِي فِي الْحَلْقِ بِرُبْعِ الرَّأْسِ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْمَسْحِ وَحَلْقُ الْكُلِّ أَوْلَى إِقْتَدَاءً بِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَالتَّقْصِيرُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنْ رُوسِ شَعْرِهِ مِقْدَارَ الْأَنْمِلَةِ. ترجمہ اور سر منڈانا افضل ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ اللہ تعالی حلق کرنے والوں پر رحم فرمائے اس کو تین مرتبہ کہا۔ ان پر تین بار رحمت بھیجی اور اس لئے کہ سر منڈانا میل کچیل سے بدن کو صاف ستھرا کرنے میں مکمل ہے اور یہی مقصود ہے اور بال کترانے میں کچھ نقص ہے۔ پس یہ غسل مع الوضو کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور سر منڈانے میں چوتھائی سر پر اکتفاء کر سکتا ہے سح راس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ۔ اور پورا سر منڈانا رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی اقتداء کرتے ہوئے اولیٰ ہے اور کترنے کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اپنے بالوں کے سروں سے ایک انگلی کے بقدر تراش لے ۔ تشریح - صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ سر منڈانا افضل ہے اور اگر کسی کے سر پر بالکل بال نہ ہوں تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ اپنے سر پر استرہ پھیرے۔ حلق کے افضل ہونے کی دلیل حدیث رسول ہے۔ چنانچہ صحیحین میں مروی ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے اللهُمَّ ارْحَمِ الْمُحَلِّقِينَ قَالُوا وَالْمُقَصِّرِينَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ قَالَ اللَّهُمَّ ارْحَمِ الْمُحَلِّقِينَ قَالُوا وَالْمُقَصِّرِينَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ قَالَ اللَّهُمَّ ارْحَمِ الْمُحَلِّقِينَ قَالُوا وَالْمُقَصِّرِينَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ قَالَ وَالْمُقَصِّرِينَ - حدیث میں حلق کرنے والوں پر اللہ کے رسول نے تین بار دعائے رحمت کی ہے۔ پس تکرار رحمت حلق کے افضل ہونے کی بین دلیل ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود بدن کو صاف ستھرا کرنا ہے اور اس مقصد میں حلق اکمل ہے اس لئے بھی حلق ہی افضل ہوگا اور بال کترانے میں اس مقصود میں کچھ نقص ہے یعنی بال کترنے میں مکمل صفائی و ستھرائی نہیں پائی جاتی ۔ پس یہ غسل اور وضو کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ یعنی جس طرح غسل کرنا وضو سے افضل ہے اسی طرح حلق، قصر سے افضل ہے۔ اور حلال ہونے کے لئے چوتھائی سر کا منڈانا کافی ہے جیسے وضو میں چوتھائی سر کا مسح کرنا کافی ہے لیکن پورے سر کا منڈانا اولی ہے کیونکہ اس میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فعل کی اقتداء ہو جاتی ہے اور تقصیر یعنی کترانا یہ ہے کہ اپنے سر کے بال بقدر انگشت تراش لے۔
Shaving is superior due to his ﷺ saying: 'May Allah have mercy on those who shave.' He said it three times, because the hadith is apparent in mercy for them. And because shaving is more complete in removing the dirt (tafath), which is the objective, and in trimming there is some deficiency, so it resembles ghusl compared to wudu. And in shaving, one quarter of the head suffices, by analogy with wiping (mash). But shaving the entire head is better, following the example of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And taqsir is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Translation: Shaving the head is superior because the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'May Allah have mercy on those who shave.' He said it three times, sending mercy upon them three times. And because shaving the head is complete in cleaning the body from dirt and filth, and this is the objective, and in trimming there is some deficiency. So it resembles ghusl compared to wudu. And in shaving, one can suffice with one quarter of the head by analogy with wiping the head. But shaving the entire head is better, following the example of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And taqsir means to cut from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri states that shaving is superior, and if one has no hair on his head, it is wajib to pass the razor over his head. The proof for the superiority of shaving is the hadith of the Messenger. Thus, in the two Sahihs, it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'O Allah, have mercy on those who shave.' They said: 'And those who trim, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'O Allah, have mercy on those who shave.' They said: 'And those who trim, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'O Allah, have mercy on those who shave.' They said: 'And those who trim, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'And those who trim.' In the hadith, the Messenger of Allah made du'a for mercy for those who shave three times. So the repetition of mercy is a clear proof for the superiority of shaving. The second proof is that the objective is to clean the body, and shaving is more complete in achieving this objective; therefore shaving is superior. Trimming has some deficiency in achieving this objective. So it resembles ghusl and wudu: just as ghusl is superior to wudu, similarly shaving is superior to trimming. And for becoming halal, shaving one quarter of the head is sufficient, just as in wudu, wiping one quarter of the head is sufficient. But shaving the entire head is better because it follows the action of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And taqsir means to cut the hair of the head to the length of a fingertip.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that shaving the head (halq) is superior to trimming (taqsir) when exiting ihram during Hajj. The primary evidence is the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim where the Prophet ﷺ prayed for mercy for those who shave three times, and only once for those who trim. This repetition indicates preference. Additionally, the purpose of halq or taqsir is to remove the state of tafath (dirt and untidiness) that comes with ihram; shaving accomplishes this completely, while trimming leaves some hair. The commentator uses an analogy: just as ghusl (full bath) is superior to wudu (partial wash) because it achieves greater cleanliness, halq is superior to taqsir. The passage also addresses the minimum requirement: shaving one quarter of the head is sufficient for tahlil (exiting ihram), by analogy with the quarter-head wiping in wudu. However, shaving the entire head is better (awla) out of following the Prophet's ﷺ practice. For someone with no hair, it is wajib to pass the razor over the head. Taqsir is defined as cutting approximately the length of a fingertip from the ends of the hair.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely; recommended act during Hajj for exiting ihram.
تقصیر (taqsir): Trimming the hair to the length of a fingertip; sufficient for tahlil but less meritorious.
تفث (tafath): The state of being unkempt and dirty during ihram; removing it is the purpose of halq/taqsir.
مسح (mash): Wiping the head in wudu; used analogically to justify quarter-head shaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire head
B) One quarter of the head
C) A fingertip length
D) The front half of the head

Key Takeaway
Shaving the head is superior to trimming in the Hanafi school, but both are valid methods to exit ihram.

What Becomes Halal After Halq/Taqsir: Women Excluded
Determines what prohibitions of ihram are lifted after shaving/trimming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on what is permitted after halq/taqsir, explain the dispute with Malik and al-Shafi'i, and apply the principle that a clear text (nass) takes precedence over analogy (qiyas).

Core Idea
After halq/taqsir, everything is halal except women—meaning sexual acts, not perfume.

After a pilgrim shaves or trims his hair on the Day of Nahr, he exits the first stage of ihram. Most prohibitions are lifted, but not all. This lesson explores what exactly remains forbidden, focusing on the Hanafi ruling that 'everything except women' is halal, and how this is defended against objections from Imam Malik (about perfume) and Imam al-Shafi'i (about lesser sexual acts). Understanding this ruling requires grasping the authority of explicit prophetic text over analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds becomes halal after halq/taqsir, and what remains forbidden. Note the explicit exception: 'except women' means sexual relations.
The hadith 'حل له كل شيء إلا النساء' is the basis.
2
Identify Malik's objection and his proof
Imam Malik argues that perfume also remains forbidden by qiyas (analogy) because it incites to intercourse. Understand his reasoning: perfume is a du'a' (incitement) to the act that is still forbidden.
Malik extends the ruling from intercourse to its means.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the explicit hadith (nass) is given precedence over qiyas. The text says only 'women' are excepted, not perfume. Therefore, perfume is halal.
Usul rule: al-nass muqaddam 'ala al-qiyas (the text is prioritized over analogy).
4
Address the Shafi'i disagreement on lesser acts
Al-Shafi'i holds that sexual acts short of full penetration (ma duna al-faraj) become halal after halq/taqsir. The Hanafis disagree, arguing that such acts also fulfill desire with women and are thus included in the exception.
The Hanafi reasoning: qada' al-shahwa bi al-nisa' (fulfilling desire with women) is deferred until complete tahlil.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: for a Hanafi, after halq/taqsir, perfume is permissible but any sexual activity (including kissing with desire) remains forbidden; for a Maliki, perfume is also forbidden; for a Shafi'i, lesser sexual acts become permissible.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position that all sexual acts remain forbidden until after tawaf al-ziyarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءَ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ وَلَا الطِّيبُ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ دَوَاعِى الْجِمَاعِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِيهِ حَلَّ لَهُ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءُ وَهُوَ مُقَدَّمٌ عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الْجِمَاعُ فِيمَا دُونَ الْفَرْجِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ لِأَنَّهُ قَضَاءُ الشَّهْوَةِ بِالنِّسَاءِ فَيُؤَخَّرُ إِلَى تَمَامِ الْإِحْلَالِ. ترجمہ اور اس کو سوائے عورتوں کے ہر چیز حلال ہو گئی ۔ اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ سوائے خوشبو کے بھی ۔ کیونکہ وہ جماع کے دوائی میں سے ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل حضور نوے کا قول اس بارے میں کہ ان کے لئے سوائے عورتوں کے ہر چیز حلال ہو گئی ۔ اور یہ نص قیاس پر مقدم ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک اس کے واسطے مادوان الفرج میں جماع حلال نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی عورتوں کے ساتھ شہوت کو پورا کرنا ہے۔ پس پورے حلال ہونے تک مؤخر کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ حلق یا قصر کے بعد محرم کے لئے ہر وہ چیز حلال ہوگئی جو احرام کی وجہ سے ممنوع ہوگئی تھی ۔ علاوہ عورتوں کے ساتھ جماع اور دوائی جماع کے ۔ حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے جماع کی طرح خوشیوں کا نا بھی حلال نہیں ہوا کیونکہ خوشبو لگا نا دوائر جماع میں سے ہے۔ جیسے عورت کو چھونا اور اس کا بوسہ لین دوائی جماع میں سے ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول ہے حل له كل شيء إلا النساء یعنی عورتوں کے علاوہ محرم کے لئے ( حلق کے بعد ) ہر چیز حلال ہوگئی ۔ اور یہ ض امام مالک کے پیش کرو قیاس پر مقدم ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک شرمگاہ کے علاوہ میں بھی جماع حلال نہیں ہوا اگر چہ امام شافعی اس کی حلت کے قائل ہیں ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مادون الفرج میں عورت کے ساتھ جماع کرنا بھی شہوت کو پورا کرنا ہے اس لئے اس کو بھی احلال کے مکمل ہونے یعنی بعد الطواف تک مؤخر کیا جائے گا۔
And everything becomes halal for him except women. And Malik said: 'Also not perfume, because it is from the incitements to intercourse.' And our proof is the saying of him ﷺ: 'Everything has become halal for him except women.' And this text (nass) is given precedence over qiyas. And our proof is the saying of the Prophet ﷺ in this regard: 'For him, everything became halal except women.' And this text is given precedence over qiyas. And according to us, intercourse short of the private parts (less than full penetration) is not halal for him, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because it is fulfilling desire with women, so it is deferred until complete tahlil (i.e., after tawaf al-ziyarah). Commentary: He says that after halq or taqsir, everything that became prohibited due to ihram becomes halal for the muhrim, except intercourse with women and its preliminaries. Imam Malik said: Just as intercourse, perfume also has not become halal, because applying perfume is from the incitements to intercourse, just like touching a woman and kissing her are from the incitements to intercourse. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Everything has become halal for him except women.' That is, for the muhrim (after halq), everything became halal except women. And this text is given precedence over the qiyas of Imam Malik. According to us, intercourse other than the private part has also not become halal, even though al-Shafi'i believes it is permissible. Our proof is that engaging in intercourse with a woman in less than the private part is also fulfilling desire with women, so it is deferred until the completion of tahlil, i.e., after tawaf.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage explains the stage of tahlil (exiting ihram) that occurs after halq or taqsir. According to the Hanafi school, once a pilgrim shaves or trims his hair, all prohibitions of ihram are lifted except for sexual relations with women. This includes the prohibition on perfume; contrary to Imam Malik, who argues that perfume remains forbidden by analogy because it incites desire. The Hanafi response is that the explicit hadith of the Prophet ﷺ ('Everything is halal except women') is a clear text (nass) that takes precedence over analogical reasoning (qiyas). Furthermore, the Hanafis hold that even sexual acts short of full penetration (e.g., touching, kissing with desire) remain forbidden, disagreeing with Imam al-Shafi'i who considers them permissible at this stage. The reasoning is that such acts also fulfill sexual desire and thus are included in the exception of 'women' by way of being means to intercourse. Complete tahlil (full exit from ihram) occurs only after performing tawaf al-ziyarah, when all prohibitions, including sexual relations, are lifted.

Key Terms
تحلل (tahlil): Exiting the state of ihram; partial after halq/taqsir, complete after tawaf.
مادون الفرج (ma duna al-faraj): Sexual acts short of full penetration; Hanafi: these remain haram until complete tahlil.
نص (nass): A clear, unambiguous text from the Qur'an or Sunnah that does not require interpretation.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
After halq/taqsir, the Hanafi school permits everything except sexual relations with women, based on the explicit hadith that takes precedence over analogical reasoning.
